# Analysis of the sermon

<!-- section 1 (id=3577, raw_sort=1): عقل اور توحید -->

## Intellect and Monotheism

There is a fundamental distinction between intellect and reasoning. Intellect—*al-ʿAql*—constitutes an infinite potential capable of transcending the mortal realm and penetrating the spiritual world, wherein it grasps intelligible realities directly. Reasoning (*istidlāl*), by contrast, represents a finite faculty that proceeds discursively from one subject to another through logical inference, operating within the domain of conceptual thought. By the illumination of intellect, man perceives absolute truths; through reasoning alone, he can only contemplate them partially and provisionally. Reasoning thus serves as the instrument of intellect, a resource the intellect deploys according to its needs.[^cite-1]

### Intentions and Actions

When the Battle of Jamal was imminent, a Bedouin approached Amīr al-Muʾminīn and inquired: "O ʿAlī! Do you affirm that God is one?" Those nearby protested that this was an inauspicious moment for such questions. Yet ʿAlī commanded them to silence and said to the Bedouin: "Surely this man seeks knowledge; we wage war so that people may come to know!" With this utterance, he illuminated the supremacy of intention over outward act. He made manifest that the apprehension of Absolute Reality—its *tawhīd* (monotheistic affirmation)—constitutes the true purpose underlying every action, whether worship, invocation, or warfare. His ⟪ar:توحید رب العزت،⟫intention has forever been centered upon the monotheistic knowledge of Allah's majesty. His declaration—"so that people may know"—reveals that the authentic motivation ⟪ar:علم⟫behind every intention, conception, and movement, whether on the battlefield or in the sanctuary, is knowledge itself. Therefore, the question of Allah's oneness remains permissible at every place and hour. In ʿAlī's time, the three campaigns (⟪ar:جمل⟫, ⟪ar:صفین⟫, ⟪ar:نحروان⟫) were waged precisely in response to this inquiry. As the Messenger of Allah declared: "O ʿAlī! You shall wage war for the interpretation of the Qur'ān as I have waged war for its revelation."[^cite-2]

### Unity of Right

Upon the battlefield itself, ʿAlī delivered a magnificent sermon on Allah's monotheistic oneness. He addressed the Bedouin, saying that it is impermissible to call Allah "one" in the sense of numerical enumeration, for He who has no peer cannot be subsumed under quantification. Not only is partnership with Him inconceivable—since ⟪ar:لا ثانی⟫there exists no second—but no being resembles Him whatsoever.

Such is ⟪ar:'الحق المبین'⟫—the Manifest Truth. Transcending all creation, yet manifest to all things, simultaneously inaccessible and inescapable. Through this utterance, he clarified to those possessed of insight that one must not conceive Allah as "one" in comparison to many deities, but rather as ⟪ar:الحق⟫the sole Reality, all else being mere semblance and illusion.[^cite-3]

*In Arabic, the word āyat signifies "sign" or "verse." Each sign points toward its maker. The hoofprints of a horse upon sand constitute a verse attesting to the horse's presence; smoke is a verse for fire.* Everything exists as ⟪ar:'آیت'⟫—a sign and argument proclaiming Allah's existence. The word ⟪ar:تاویل⟫—esoteric interpretation or "return to origin"—bears precisely this meaning: *He is the First, the Last, the Outward, the Inward*, and all outward multiplicity returns to ⟪ar:'وحدانیت'⟫His singular unity and ⟪ar:'أحدیت'⟫His absolute oneness, as Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 41:53⟫
> ⟪ar:‏سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ حَتَّىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ ۗ أَوَلَمْ يَكْفِ بِرَبِّكَ أَنَّهُۥ عَلَىٰ كُلِّ شَىْءٍۢ شَهِيدٌ ‎⟫
> *We will show them Our Signs in the universe, and in their ownselves, until it becomes manifest to them that this (the Qur'an) is the truth. Is it not sufficient in regard to your Lord that He is a Witness over all things?*

In this verse, Allah employs the plural "verses" and "horizons," yet for the Truth employs the singular with the definite article ⟪ar:ال⟫—signifying that the multiplicity of cosmic and interior signs converges upon one singular, singular Truth.[^cite-4] Within the human being dwells an uneasiness and yearning that impels us toward the bliss of unity; there exists a perpetual need to strive for the repose of oneness.

### Qur'ān and Interpretation

For this reason, the Qur'ān is one, yet each verse admits of multiple interpretations. *Just as ʿAlī is singular, so too are the Imams of his progeny, who have become "verses" pointing to him—yet they are many.*

Imām Jaʿfar al-Ṣādiq said to one of his companions: "Were I to wish, I could expound seventy interpretations of every verse of the Qur'ān."[^cite-5] Allah taught ⟪ar:محمد مصطفی صلی اللہ علیہ و آلہ و سلم⟫the Messenger the interpretation of the Qur'ān, and he in turn conveyed it to ʿAlī. Then the Messenger declared: ⟪ar-quote:علی مع القرآن و القرآن مع العلی⟫"ʿAlī is with the Qur'ān and the Qur'ān is with ʿAlī." When ʿAlī told al-ʿAbbās that were he to unveil the taʾwīl (esoteric meaning) of ⟪ar:سورۃ الفاتحۃ⟫the Chapter of Opening, seventy camels would be laden with books, he testified to his role as the true interpreter of the Qur'ān.

*The Qur'ān is a book inscribed between two volumes: Muḥammad and ʿAlī. All pages between them refer to the Imāms descended from them.*

### Reason, Revelation, Spirit

Allah's revelation—the Qur'ānic text—is ⟪ar:'صامت'⟫mute; it does not speak in its own language. It requires an interpreter to disclose its meanings (⟪ar:لا بُدَّ لَہُ مِن تَرجُماَن⟫). Similarly, to comprehend divine messages, an interpreter is necessary—and this interpreter is *intellect itself*. The connection between ⟪ar:وحی⟫revelation and ⟪ar:عقل⟫intellect is evident from the Messenger's saying: ⟪ar-quote:رسول الرجل ترجمان عقلہ⟫"The messenger of man is the interpreter of his intellect." Thus, intellect functions as the inner messenger. This is why every utterance of Maulana ʿAlī reflects the Qur'ān: each statement traverses from the Qur'ān's words to its revelation, from revelation to its spirit, thence to its Revealer. His discourse returns the Qur'ān's words through all these stages to their source and origin—⟪ar:عقل اول⟫the First Intellect. Therefore, the One who revealed this Word simultaneously remains concealed in its meaning and manifest through its language. ⟪ar:'الہ'⟫He cannot be grasped or described directly; only through the impressions of His creation may His existence and manifestation be acknowledged.[^cite-6]

| | | |
|---|---|---|
| **The Revelation** | **The Intermediary** | **The Interpretation** |
| al-ʿAql al-Awwal (First Intellect) | Muḥammad | ʿAlī |
| Revelation of the Qur'ān | Words of the Qur'ān | The Meaning of the Qur'ān |
| Allah | Revelation | Intellect |

On the surface, revelation and intellect appear as two distinct entities, divided by scholars into separate categories:

| **Revelation** | **Intellect** |
|---|---|
| Convention; Tradition | Nature |
| Imitation; Conformity | Research; Verification |
| Piety | Inquiry; Quest |

Yet in reality, they are intimately proximate, complementary and reciprocal. These ostensibly separate phenomena unite to form a singular reality—the supreme purpose of creation itself: ⟪ar:توحید⟫*tawhīd*, literally "to make one" or "to unify." Truth emerges through the synthesis of negation and affirmation. If the truth be that Aḥmad owns one goat, this is established solely by negating that he owns two. The synthesis of intellect and revelation—which points toward singular Reality—is that which lies between them: ⟪ar:'روح'⟫the Spirit. Intellect alone is limited in its vastness and cannot withstand revelation; but Spirit, the animating principle of intellect, is boundless. Only Spirit receives the messages of revelation, perceives them with clarity, and tests their sublimity. It conveys these messages to intellect, which processes and refines them. Were this otherwise, revelation would devolve into mere rules and regulations for human will, rather than becoming creative inspiration for the intellect.[^cite-7]

Revelation, multidimensional by nature, cannot be confined to the single dimension of words. The Messenger clothed Allah's revelation in language so that spirituality might assume physical form, perceptible to the five senses. Therein lies the crucial connection between revelation and intellect: while revelation constrains meaning within words, intellect liberates meaning from that confinement. Through intellect, the outward surface of words generates innumerable streams of inner significance. This is illustrated in the narrative of Moses: when he struck the stone with his staff—symbolizing intellect—twelve springs of meaning gushed forth:

> ⟪quran 2:60⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ وَإِذِ ٱسْتَسْقَىٰ مُوسَىٰ لِقَوْمِهِۦ فَقُلْنَا ٱضْرِب بِّعَصَاكَ ٱلْحَجَرَ ۖ فَٱنفَجَرَتْ مِنْهُ ٱثْنَتَا عَشْرَةَ عَيْنًۭا ۖ قَدْ عَلِمَ كُلُّ أُنَاسٍۢ مَّشْرَبَهُمْ ۖ كُلُوا۟ وَٱشْرَبُوا۟ مِن رِّزْقِ ٱللَّهِ وَلَا تَعْثَوْا۟ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ مُفْسِدِينَ ‎⟫
> *And (remember) when Musa (Moses) asked for water for his people, We said: "Strike the stone with your stick." Then gushed forth therefrom twelve springs. Each (group of) people knew its own place for water. "Eat and drink of that which Allah has provided and do not act corruptly, making mischief on the earth."*

The more refined and subtle the spirit, the greater its capacity to grasp revelation's content and extract pearls of profound meaning from a single shell. Intellect functions as the inner witness through which man empirically confirms and verifies divine messages. Without it, one would be compelled to accept revelation's message solely through dogmatic adherence. For this reason, Amīr al-Muʾminīn told Kumayl that one of the purposes of sending prophets was to extract the hidden treasures of intellect. Intellect is awakened and quickened by revelation—a voice reaching the spiritual depths, germinating the seeds of consciousness that Allah sowed within it from eternity. Revelation cannot be procured save through intellect, nor can the treasures concealed beneath intellect's soil be unveiled except through revelation. From this perspective, there emerges an eternal bond between intellect and revelation, such that they may be called analogous, or at minimum, intellect may be understood as revelation's manifestation.[^cite-8]

That Maulana ʿAlī stated the extraction of intellect's hidden treasures as a reason for prophetic mission proves that the spiritual intellect of any human being cannot remain ignorant of revelation's message; rather, it recognizes it, for the message of Allah accords with the essence of intellect itself. Since both derive from the same origin, intellect recognizes revelation's source—that it emanates from the Divine. These ⟪ar:'الہ الحقیقی'⟫divine messages awaken intellect; they are not separate from it but constitute its authentic purpose. Thus ⟪ar:'روح'⟫the Spirit receives these messages through intellect and inculcates them such that the two become one. When this occurs, the heart becomes capable of "seeing" Allah. He cannot be perceived with the eyes, only through the heart—what Amīr al-Muʾminīn calls ⟪ar:'حق الیقین'⟫the Truth of Certainty.

<!-- section 2 (id=3599, raw_sort=2): عقل اور استدلال کا فرق -->

## The Distinction Between Intellect and Reasoning

A continuity subsists between the power of intellect and the power of reasoning (*istidlāl*), yet they are in a sense distinct and separable. The continuity lies in this: every thought and concept originates in meaningful understanding. Reasoning yields ideas that are logical and grounded in reality. It operates through ⟪ar:مفارقۃ⟫paradox, ⟪ar:تناقض⟫antinomy, ⟪ar:نفی⟫negation, and ⟪ar:اثبات⟫assertion—instruments through which it cultivates the hidden treasures of intellect. Yet reasoning possesses a limit beyond which it cannot advance: its boundaries are confined to the material realm and it cannot enter the spiritual domain. To traverse into those heights, it requires an external guide—⟪ar:'وحی'⟫revelation itself—which intellect can apprehend as its inner messenger. Through this companion, intellect steps into spirituality's realm.

Therefore, when ⟪ar:'الہ'⟫Maulana ʿAlī negates concepts pertaining to Allah, he does so because of reasoning's inadequacy and weakness. This negation becomes the springboard for evoking and absorbing consciousness concealed within intellect—consciousness transcending reason's boundaries. The negation of finite human imagination thus becomes the foundation for confessing infinite divinity. It is negation that ascends, not negation that descends and destroys. This dialectic of negation and affirmation appears throughout ⟪ar:نہج البلاغۃ⟫the Path of Eloquence, particularly in his praise of Allah:

> Praise be to Allah, whose praise transcends the utterance of speakers, whose beneficence cannot be enumerated, whose vigilant servants cannot discharge His due—He whom understanding cannot perceive after determination, whom intellectual penetration cannot attain. His attributes have no limits, no description, no bounded nor extended time. He created creation through His power; He spread forth the winds through His mercy; He swallowed up the earth's expanse with rocks.

Observe this paradox in Amīr al-Muʾminīn's discourse: Allah is worthy of praise, yet He cannot be praised; His beneficence exists, yet remains uncounted, though all else admits enumeration. To discharge Allah's due is obligatory, yet impossible. Such contradictory obligations permeate his utterances.[^cite-9]

Divine attributes cannot be ⟪ar:لیس لصفاتہ حد محدود⟫defined nor described, yet they subsist. The Qur'ān itself describes Allah as ⟪ar:'کریم'⟫Generous, ⟪ar:'عزیز'⟫Mighty, ⟪ar:'رحیم'⟫Merciful—yet Maulana ʿAlī insists none of these attributes can be delimited. God is generous: but how generous? How much generosity? Is it the generosity of myself, of you, of others? His statement—⟪ar:أخلاص⟫"Sincerity arises from negating all His attributes from Allah"—exemplifies this tension. On one hand, we must acknowledge Allah's attributes; on the other, we must negate them. The problem is that human mind grasps God through attributed language, yet ʿAlī negates these very attributes, leaving no conceptual purchase. If we can identify His attributes through these words, and yet must negate them, what is one to do? Yet from this contradiction of affirmation and negation emerges a deeper knowledge: the hidden treasures of intellect awaken, and man is forced to recognize that knowledge of Allah surpasses our faculties of thought, reasoning, and intellection—knowledge only the Spirit can perceive, which intellect cannot comprehend. As he says: "My Lord cannot be confined within dimensions, motion, time, or space; He is subtle yet not subtlety; magnificent yet not majesty; great yet not magnitude."

Here again, he simultaneously affirms and negates Allah's attributes. Allah possesses these attributes, yet cannot be imprisoned within them; He cannot be reduced to our imaginings. These attributes provide intellect with some concept, yet that concept is weak and incomplete. To acknowledge the perfection of these attributes, they must be negated—precisely because our concepts are deficient. From the interplay of negation and affirmation emerges the depth of Knowledge. This depth cannot be established unless it is acknowledged that negation and affirmation are insufficient to mirror this reality accurately. To negate all attributes is to "confess" His infinite Self—the universe's true purpose: ⟪ar:کلمۃ اخلاص، لا الہ الا اللہ⟫the Word of Sincerity: "There is no divinity save Allah." For any concept to establish itself in the human mind, definition is necessary; where definition exists, limitations and exclusions follow. Yet divine attributes, being infinite attributes of an infinite Essence, transcend such limitation and exclusion. We may thus substitute all attributes in the place of negation within the Word of Sincerity, reciting: ⟪ar:'لا رحمن الا اللہ'⟫"There is no Merciful save Allah"; ⟪ar:'لا عظیم الا اللہ'⟫"There is no Mighty save Allah"; ⟪ar:'لا کریم الا اللہ'⟫"There is no Generous save Allah"—such that apparent negation of attributes becomes affirmation of His Identity. All these attributes are not externally appended to His Essence but constitute its substance, distinguished only through ⟪ar:'علم الوجود'⟫knowledge of Being through mental conception. For this reason, Allah Himself declares:

> ⟪quran 23:91⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مَا ٱتَّخَذَ ٱللَّهُ مِن وَلَدٍۢ وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُۥ مِنْ إِلَهٍ ۚ إِذًۭا لَّذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِلَهٍۭ بِمَا خَلَقَ وَلَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَىٰ بَعْضٍۢ ۚ سُبْحَنَ ٱللَّهِ عَمَّا يَصِفُونَ ‎⟫
> *No son (or offspring or children) did Allah beget, nor is there any ilah (god) along with Him; (if there had been many gods), behold, each god would have taken away what he had created, and some would have tried to overcome others! Glorified be Allah above all that they attribute to Him!*[^cite-10]

Allah's "infinity" deserves liberation from all imaginary constraints; yet the "heart" is not incapable of knowing Him—it sees Him through its own vision. The heart has always been the seat of rational wisdom; intellect depends upon it for purification. Indeed, it is the source of intellect's purity, which is why ʿAlī declares: ⟪ar:'ذکر اللہ'⟫"The remembrance of Allah is the noblest worship." Yet here too a paradox emerges: ⟪ar:ذکر⟫remembrance cannot be attained unless the worshipper "loses" himself in remembrance of Allah—a state called ⟪ar:'فنا بااللہ'⟫annihilation in Allah—not the cessation of intellect, but the absorption of soul in Allah's remembrance.[^cite-11]

Intellect is a spiritual faculty whose origin and vivifying cause is the soul. Without intellect, the soul becomes an unconscious entity; without authentic soul, intellect inclines toward inert thoughts. Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 32:7-9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِىٓ أَحْسَنَ كُلَّ شَىْءٍ خَلَقَهُۥ ۖ وَبَدَأَ خَلْقَ ٱلْإِنسَنِ مِن طِينٍۢ ‎ ‏ثُمَّ جَعَلَ نَسْلَهُۥ مِن سُلَلَةٍۢ مِّن مَّآءٍۢ مَّهِينٍۢ ‎ ‏ثُمَّ سَوَّىٰهُ وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِن رُّوحِهِۦ ۖ وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ ٱلسَّمْعَ وَٱلْأَبْصَرَ وَٱلْأَفْـِٔدَةَ ۚ قَلِيلًۭا مَّا تَشْكُرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Who made everything He has created good, and He began the creation of man from clay. Then He made his offspring from semen of worthless water (male and female sexual discharge). Then He fashioned him in due proportion, and breathed into him the soul (created by Allah for that person), and He gave you hearing (ears), sight (eyes) and hearts. Little is the thanks you give!*

⟪ar:'نفخ الروح'⟫The breathing of the Spirit engenders life and consciousness. If the soul is not given its due, such existence becomes akin to death. Through this Spirit, static things are animated and unconscious objects awakened and made aware. By this Divine Spirit, one acquires knowledge not merely of others but of oneself. From the synthesis of "existence" and "knowledge" arises every spiritual concept. When the soul attaches to the body, it quickens it; thus knowledge revives it, as Allah says:

> ⟪quran 8:24⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱسْتَجِيبُوا۟ لِلَّهِ وَلِلرَّسُولِ إِذَا دَعَاكُمْ لِمَا يُحْيِيكُمْ ۖ وَٱعْلَمُوٓا۟ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يَحُولُ بَيْنَ ٱلْمَرْءِ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَأَنَّهُۥٓ إِلَيْهِ تُحْشَرُونَ ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Answer Allah (by obeying Him) and (His) Messenger when he (PBUH) calls you to that which will give you life, and know that Allah comes in between a person and his heart (i.e. He prevents an evil person to decide anything). And verily to Him you shall (all) be gathered.*

ʿAlī affirmed that the divine invitation in which people find life is ⟪ar:'وحی'⟫revelation itself—that which awakens the hidden treasures of intellect. Intellect, the expression of soul, is not merely mental power but is rooted in "life." Maulana ʿAlī defines ⟪ar:'عاقل'⟫the wise one as one whose knowledge is not only correct but whose action accords with truth, whose striving tends always toward the Absolute. Another meaning of ⟪ar:'عاقل'⟫ is "one who places things in their proper place"; ⟪ar:'عادل'⟫only the wise can be just, for only those who perceive things according to their reality can place them in their rightful station. Right thinking, flawless virtue, and authentic being are faculties of intellect.

<!-- section 3 (id=3578, raw_sort=3): علی کا کمیل ابن زیاد کو خطاب -->

## ʿAlī's Discourse with Kumayl ibn Ziyād al-Nakhaʿī

Kumayl ibn Ziyād al-Nakhaʿī reported: Amīr al-Muʾminīn ʿAlī ibn Abī Ṭālib, upon him be peace, took hold of my hand and led me into the graveyard. When we had passed through and emerged beyond the city, he heaved a deep sigh and said:

⟪ar-quote:قال كُمَيْل بن زياد- أخذ بيدي أميرالمؤمنين علي بن أبي طالب عليه السلام ، فأخرجني إلى الجبّان فلمّا أصحر تنفّس الصّعَدَاء ثمّ قال⟫

O Kumayl, these hearts are vessels. The finest of them is that which preserves its contents; so preserve what I convey to you.

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْل بْن زِيَادٍ، إِنَّ هذهِ الْقُلُوبَ أَوْعِيَةٌ فَخَيْرُهَا أَوْعَاهَا فَاحْفَظْ عَنِّي مَا أَقُولُ لَكَ⟫

People are of three kinds. First are the learned and godly—the *ʿālim rabbānī*. Second are the seeker of knowledge traversing the path of salvation. Last are the masses, the heedless rabble, followers of every caller, yielders to every wind—those who have sought no illumination from knowledge's radiance nor taken shelter in any reliable support.

⟪ar-quote:النَّاسُ ثَلاَثَةٌ- فَعَالِمٌ رَبَّانِيٌّ وَمُتَعَلِّمٌ عَلَى سَبِيلِ نَجَاةٍ، وَهَمَجٌ رَعَاعٌ أَتْبَاعُ كُلِّ نَاعِقٍ يَمِيلُونَ مَعَ كُلِّ رِيحٍ، لَمْ يَسْتَضِيئُوا بِنُورِ الْعِلْمِ، وَلَمْ يَلْجَؤُوا إِلَى رُكْنٍ وَثِيقٍ⟫

O Kumayl, knowledge surpasses wealth. Intellect guards you; you must guard wealth. Wealth diminishes by expenditure; knowledge multiplies through giving. The benefits of wealth perish as wealth itself decays.

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْلُ، الْعِلْمُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ الْمَالِ- الْعِلْمُ يَحْرُسُكَ وَأَنْتَ تَحْرُسُ المَالَ، وَالْمَالُ تَنْقُصُهُ النَّفَقَةُ، وَالْعِلْمُ يَزْكُوعَلَى الاْنْفَاقِ، وَصَنِيعُ الْمَالِ يَزُولُ بِزَوَالِهِ⟫

O Kumayl, knowledge is a *dīn* (faith) by which one is devoted. Through it man acquires obedience during his life and a fair name after death. Knowledge is the ruler; wealth, the ruled.

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْلَ بْن زِيَادٍ مَعْرِفَةُ الْعِلْمِ دِينٌ يُدَانُ بِهِ . بِهِ يَكْسِبُ الْإِنْسَانُ الطَّاعَةَ فِى حَيَاتِهِ وَ جَمِيلَ الْأُحْدُوثَةِ بَعْدَ وَفَاتِهِ وَ الْعِلْمُ حَاكِمٌ وَ الْمَالُ مَحْكُومٌ عَلَيْهِ⟫

O Kumayl, those who hoard wealth are dead, though they live; scholars endure as long as the world endures. Though their bodies vanish, their likenesses dwell in hearts. Behold, herein lies an abundance of knowledge—and he pointed to his breast. I have sought a bearer for it. Yes, I have found one; but either he was unreliable, exploiting religion for worldly gain, domineering over people through Allah's favors, ruling over His devotees through His arguments; or he was obedient to truth's carriers, yet devoid of insight, whose heart would harbor misgivings at the first doubt's appearance.

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْلُ هَلَكَ خُزَّانُ الْأَمْوَالِ وَ هُمْ أَحْيَاءٌ وَ الْعُلَمَاءُ بَاقُونَ مَا بَقِيَ الدَّهْرُ أَعْيَانُهُمْ مَفْقُودَةٌ وَ أَمْثَالُهُمْ فِى الْقُلُوبِ مَوْجُودَةٌ هَا إِنَّ هَاهُنَا لَعِلْماً جَمّاً وَ أَشَارَ بِيَدِهِ إِلَى صَدْرِهِ لَوْ أَصَبْتُ لَهُ حَمَلَةً بَلَى أَصَبْتُ لَقِناً غَيْرَ مَأْمُونٍ عَلَيْهِ مُسْتَعْمِلًا آلَةَ الدِّينِ لِلدُّنْيَا وَ مُسْتَظْهِراً بِنِعَمِ اللَّهِ عَلَى عِبَادِهِ وَ بِحُجَجِهِ عَلَى أَوْلِيَائِهِ أَوْ مُنْقَاداً لِحَمَلَةِ الْحَقِّ لَا بَصِيرَةَ لَهُ فِى أَحْنَائِهِ يَنْقَدِحُ الشَّكُّ فِى قَلْبِهِ لِأَوَّلِ عَارِضٍ مِنْ شُبْهَةٍ⟫

Neither type suffices. One is enslaved to pleasure, malleable before desire; the other consumed by wealth-gathering and hoarding—neither serves religion in any measure. Their nearest resemblance is to grazing cattle. Thus knowledge perishes with the death of its bearers.

⟪ar-quote:أَلَا لَا ذَا وَ لَا ذَاكَ أَوْ مَنْهُوماً بِاللَّذَّةِ سَلِسَ الْقِيَادِ لِلشَّهْوَةِ أَوْ مُغْرَماً بِالْجَمْعِ وَ الِادِّخَارِ لَيْسَا مِنْ رُعَاةِ الدِّينِ فِى شَيْ‏ءٍ أَقْرَبُ شَيْ‏ءٍ شَبَهاً بِهِمَا الْأَنْعَامُ السَّائِمَةُ كَذَلِكَ يَمُوتُ الْعِلْمُ بِمَوْتِ حَامِلِيهِ⟫

O Allah! Yet indeed, the earth is never bereft of one who upholds Allah's proof, either manifest and renowned, or hidden and fearful—lest Allah's proofs and evidence be invalidated. How many are they, and where? By Allah, they are few in number, yet immense in worth before Allah. Through them Allah preserves His proofs and evidence until they entrust them to others like themselves and plant the seeds thereof in hearts similar to theirs.

⟪ar-quote:اللَّهُمَّ بَلَى! لاَ تَخْلُو الاْرْضُ مِنْ قَائِمٍ لله بِحُجَّةٍ، إِمَّا ظَاهِراً مَشْهُوراً، أوْ خَائِفاً مَغْمُوراً لِئَلاَّ تَبْطُلَ حُجَجُ اللهِ وَبَيِّنَاتُهُ. وَكَمْ ذَا وَأَيْنَ أُولئِكَ؟ أُولئِكَ ـ وَاللَّهِ ـ الاْقَلُّونَ عَدَداً، وَالاْعْظَمُونَ قَدْراً، يَحْفَظُ اللهُ بِهِمْ حُجَجَهُ وَبَيِّنَاتِهِ، حَتَّىٰ يُودِعُوهَا نُظَرَاءَهُمْ، وَيَزْرَعُوهَا فِي قُلُوبِ أَشْبَاهِهِمْ⟫

Knowledge has hurled them upon the realities of insight; they have touched the spirit of certainty. They find easy what the pampered find grievous; they befriend what the ignorant shun. They dwell in this world with bodies here, yet their spirits hover in the highest station. These are Allah's vicegerents upon His earth and callers to His *dīn*. O, how I long to see them! Depart now, O Kumayl, whenever you wish!

⟪ar-quote:هَجَمَ بِهِمُ الْعِلْمُ عَلَى حَقِيقَةِ الْبَصِيرَةِ، وَبَاشَرُوا رُوحَ الْيَقِينِ، وَاسْتَلاَنُوامَا اسْتَوْعَرَهُ الْمُتْرَفُونَ وَأَنِسُوا بِمَا اسْتَوْحَشَ مِنْهُ الْجَاهِلُونَ، وَصَحِبُوا الدُّنْيَا بِأَبْدَانٍ أَرْوَاحُهَا مُعَلَّقَةٌ بِالْـمَحَلِّ الاْعْلَىٰ، أُولئِكَ خُلَفَاءُ اللهِ فِي أَرْضِهِ، وَالدُّعَاةُ إِلَىٰ دِينِهِ، آهِ آهِ شَوْقاً إِلَىٰ رُؤْيَتِهِمْ! انْصَرِفْ إذَا شِئْتَ!⟫[^cite-12]

<!-- section 4 (id=3579, raw_sort=4): علم اور بصیرت -->

## Knowledge and Insight

In this sermon, ʿAlī references the blessed servants of Allah—the Imāms—as the life of Allah's *dīn* (religion). By divine religion, he signifies the faith descending from the Almighty, the essence of belief, complete and immutable. He declared: "Religion stands firm through the knowledge of truthful scholars." Were these *ʿulamāʾ* (learned ones) absent, all vestiges of religion would vanish. He said: ⟪ar-quote:هَجَمَ بِهِمُ الْعِلْمُ عَلَى حَقِيقَةِ الْبَصِيرَةِ⟫"Knowledge thrusts them upon the realities of *baṣīra* (insight)." Though knowledge has always lain latent within intellect's essence, it must be awakened. His use of the word "hurled" (*hajama*) suggests that this knowledge lies concealed in the depths beneath superficial meanings—layers of interpretation subordinate to external sense. The quotation points to distinct degrees of knowledge. When he indicated his breast, declaring: ⟪ar-quote:هَاهُنَا لَعِلْماً جَمّاً⟫"Here lies an immense knowledge," he signified that though the chest contains the heart, reaching the heart requires penetrating the chest's depths. Words may gesture toward hidden truths, yet cannot encompass them.

In Arabic, ⟪ar:'ھَجَمَ'⟫—"to assail" or "to attack"—invites us to assault the surface of words and penetrate to realities concealed within. When the depths of insight become embedded in the intellect, the doors of contemplation open, and one knows the truth of this knowledge, as the Lord declares: "He who has cultivated understanding has grasped knowledge's essence." To reach such depths requires struggle, echoed in the saying: ⟪ar-quote:بالتَّعَلُّم یَناَلُ العلم⟫"Knowledge is attained through learning." The aim is that one must internalize external knowledge through the intellect such that the two become one. It is the power of ⟪ar:'روح'⟫the Spirit that effects this ⟪ar:'توحید'⟫unification of knowledge and essence.[^cite-13]

### *Jihād al-Nafs*: The Struggle Against the Self

Yet this unification is possible only when egocentricity—⟪ar:أنانیت⟫*al-ānāniyyat* (selfhood)—is purged. Maulana ʿAlī teaches that the wise one is perpetually at war with the inferior tendencies, lusts, and desires of his soul; all transgress against knowledge's power. The soul's evils are clouds that, when they obscure intellect's sky, dim vision and obscure reality. The Qur'ān terms these evils *rān* (rust):

> ⟪quran 83:14⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كَلَّا ۖ بَلْۜ رَانَ عَلَىٰ قُلُوبِهِم مَّا كَانُوا۟ يَكْسِبُونَ ‎⟫
> *Nay! But on their hearts is the Ran (covering of sins and evil deeds) which they used to earn.*[^cite-14]

Though morally reprehensible, from a spiritual standpoint, these evils oppose God's created realities as their antithesis. Following them obliterates sight and blinds the eye of the heart through which Allah is "seen." The wise engage in constant struggle against desire and cultivate virtuous character. The root of all vice is ignorance, against which one must wage *al-jihād al-akbar* (the Greater Struggle)—the *jihād al-nafs* (struggle of the self) that the Prophet called "the Supreme Jihad." Maulana ʿAlī stated thus:

| The wise man contends with his self through knowledge.
| He is most mighty who overcomes his own self.
| Verily, those who struggle against their souls for Allah's sake attain the rank of the martyred before Allah.
| The ultimate warfare is man's struggle against himself.
| He who knows his self fights against it.
| No Jihad surpasses the Jihad of the Self. |

He declares that though this war appears external, in truth it serves the self's welfare. The intellect—⟪ar:العقل⟫—is the army's commander; ⟪ar:الھوی⟫caprice is Satan's general. The self stands between them, affected by both; whoever it yields to, he joins that army. Thus one must utterly subdue the self to enter the Merciful's ranks. The goal is not the self's annihilation, but the eradication of ⟪ar:'ھوی'⟫caprice within it. The Qur'ān testifies that the Messenger did not speak from ⟪ar:ھوی⟫personal desire:

> ⟪quran 53:3-4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمَا يَنطِقُ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْىٌۭ يُوحَىٰ ‎⟫
> *Nor does he speak of (his own) desire. It is only an Inspiration that is inspired.*[^cite-15]

Intellect functions as the interpreter of the Merciful's army, warring against Satan's legions. The Qur'ān presents ⟪ar:الھوی⟫caprice another way:

> ⟪quran 25:43⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ أَفَأَنتَ تَكُونُ عَلَيْهِ وَكِيلًا ‎⟫
> *Have you (O Muhammad PBUH) seen him who has taken as his ilah (god) his own desire? Would you then be a Wakîl (a disposer of his affairs or a watcher) over him?*

> ⟪quran 45:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ وَأَضَلَّهُ ٱللَّهُ عَلَىٰ عِلْمٍۢ وَخَتَمَ عَلَىٰ سَمْعِهِۦ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَجَعَلَ عَلَىٰ بَصَرِهِۦ غِشَوَةًۭ فَمَن يَهْدِيهِ مِنۢ بَعْدِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أَفَلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Have you seen him who takes his own lust (vain desires) as his ilah (god), and Allah knowing (him as such), left him astray, and sealed his hearing and his heart, and put a cover on his sight. Who then will guide him after Allah? Will you not then remember?*[^cite-16]

⟪ar:'شرک خفی'⟫This is "hidden polytheism." The Messenger declared: ⟪ar-quote:الشرك فيكم أخفی من دبيب النمل⟫"Polytheism walks among you more secretly than the ant's footfall." To shatter the self's idols of ⟪ar:أنانیت⟫egocentrism, an external force unconnected to the self is necessary: the divine sciences emanating from intellect and faith. Allah says:

> ⟪quran 79:40-41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِۦ وَنَهَىٰ ٱلنَّفْسَ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰ ‎ ‏فَإِنَّ ٱلْجَنَّةَ هِىَ ٱلْمَأْوَىٰ ‎⟫
> *But as for him who feared standing before his Lord, and restrained himself from impure evil desires, and lusts. Verily, Paradise will be his abode.*[^cite-17]

The core energy of the soul cannot be eliminated, only redirected from countless satanic desires toward the Beneficent. *Tawhīd* (monotheism) means "to make one" or "to integrate." Allah is not merely ⟪ar:'أحد'⟫singular in Himself but ⟪ar:أحد⟫the only Creator. Thus monotheism entails not only acknowledging Allah's ⟪ar:أحدیت⟫singularity but declaring one's own ⟪ar:أحد⟫singularity—⟪ar:أحد حقیقی⟫authentic oneness—such that it can properly mirror the Divine. To know God is to be joined with Him. One meaning of intellect is "binding," for it gathers and encompasses meaning. Unlike intellect stands the "heart," ⟪ar:الحام⟫the locus and broadcaster of intellect's spiritual realities. Intellect captures; the heart radiates. Intellect is the force uniting the soul's diverse elements. The Creator thus says:

⟪ar-quote:مَنْ عَرَفَ اللہ تَوَحَّدُ⟫"He who knows Allah becomes unified with Him."
⟪ar-quote:مَنْ عَرَفَ اللہ اِسْتَحَيَا⟫"He who knows Allah is abashed."
⟪ar-quote:مَنْ عَرَفَ النَّاسَ تَفَرّقَ⟫"He who knows people becomes detached."
⟪ar-quote:مَنْ عَرَفَ الدُّنْيَا زَهِدَ⟫"He who knows the world renounces it."

### Sincerity (*Ikhlas*)

In another place, Maulana ʿAlī designates this complete integration of the self with divine reality as *ikhlas* (sincerity). The word ⟪ar:خَلُصَ⟫means to be entirely purified, to attain essence, or to be unmixed. In this sense, he declares: ⟪ar-quote:أخلص لی اللہ العلم و العمل والحب و العداوۃ، والقبض و المغادرۃ، والنطق و الصمت⟫"Make your knowledge and action, love and hatred, acquisition and renunciation, speech and silence pure for the sake of Allah." The meaning of sincerity is to purify one's self for Allah's sake such that no stain remains. By stain is meant everything ⟪ar:'غیر اللہ'⟫other-than-Allah. Sincerity is the purification of all devotion, action, intention, and passion from that which is other. The most pernicious stain is ⟪ar:أنانیت⟫egocentrism. Sincerity demands that every action, thought, and existence be selfless and for Allah's sake. ʿAlī used the term "ultimate struggle" to emphasize this point. Whoever achieves such sincerity becomes, in Allah's sight, a *shahīd* (martyr/witness), having killed himself in Allah's path, living by intellect's illumination and sustained through revelation, as He declared:

> ⟪quran 3:169⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَحْسَبَنَّ ٱلَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا۟ فِى سَبِيلِ ٱللَّهِ أَمْوَتًۢا ۚ بَلْ أَحْيَآءٌ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ ‎⟫
> *Think not of those who are killed in the Way of Allah as dead. Nay, they are alive, with their Lord, and they have provision.*[^cite-18]

⟪ar:شہید⟫The witness also testifies: the sincere one testifies through self-sacrifice that he stands with Allah against all other-than-Allah. The focus of such a being is not his own self but Allah as the center of all. Thus sincerity is existence for Allah's sake and fullness in Allah, as He declares:

> ⟪quran 6:162⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلْ إِنَّ صَلَاتِى وَنُسُكِى وَمَحْيَاىَ وَمَمَاتِى لِلَّهِ رَبِّ ٱلْعَلَمِينَ ‎⟫
> *Say (O Muhammad PBUH): "Verily, my Salat (prayer), my sacrifice, my living, and my dying are for Allah, the Lord of the 'Alamîn (mankind, jinns and all that exists).*[^cite-19]

### Sincerity and Prayer

Prayer constitutes an integral dimension of sincerity. The human soul's nourishment is worship; no sustenance surpasses prayer. Thus Allah mentions prayer first in this verse and many others. Whoever neglects prayer has deprived the soul of its sustenance and failed its due. One unable to fulfill his own rights cannot fulfill others'. Whoever sets right his relationship with Allah, Allah sets right his relationship with His servants. The Qur'ān confirms:

> ⟪quran 15:99⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱعْبُدْ رَبَّكَ حَتَّىٰ يَأْتِيَكَ ٱلْيَقِينُ ‎⟫
> *And worship your Lord until there comes unto you the certainty (i.e. death).*[^cite-20]

Should the hidden treasures of intellect be awakened, one must seek knowledge with constancy and total dedication. Such dedication requires focus on divine realities and profound worship—a worship where no barrier separates seeker from sought. In such worship, the servant forgets all, even himself; mere mechanical worship avails nothing. Maulana ʿAlī teaches that one who prays without earnest struggle (*ijtihād*) resembles one who shoots arrows without a bow. Similarly, knowledge depends upon action; without balanced action, it is lost. The heart cannot digest acquired knowledge without seriousness, depriving it of insight and the ability to perceive Allah.[^cite-21]

The Master of the Universe taught: "Acquire knowledge, and life will acquire you." Initially, one is ignorant of life's realities. Through knowledge, consciousness awakens. But when this unfolds with sincerity over time—as one continuously transforms knowledge into action—a moment arrives when one no longer integrates knowledge into oneself; rather, lived reality absorbs it. The process initially performed with great effort and earnestness becomes the rhythm of existence, undertaken unconsciously with the same dedication. Habit thus transforms into instinct.

Returning to the Master's pronouncement that knowledge is embedded in insight's realities: the scholar is not immersed in insight but receives these divine insights, making the world itself his means, because he has integrated himself into knowledge itself.[^cite-22]

<!-- section 5 (id=3580, raw_sort=5): The Spirit of Certainty -->

## The Spirit of Certainty

You declare: "They rejoice because they are attached to the Spirit of Faith" (⟪ar-quote:وبشِّرُ روح الیقین⟫). When ordinary humans speak of attachment or relationship to something, they invoke the word ⟪ar:'مباشرت'⟫ (*mubāsharat*, direct contact or intimacy), yet this term carries another dimension entirely—that of *supreme gladness*. When a person touches the spirit of faith—that inner certainty wrought by proximity to the Divine—the joy that ensues transcends all utterance. This happiness surpasses even the greatest blessings of Paradise itself, of which Allāh says:

> ⟪quran 9:72⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَٱلْمُؤْمِنَتِ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ خَلِدِينَ فِيهَا وَمَسَكِنَ طَيِّبَةًۭ فِى جَنَّتِ عَدْنٍۢ ۚ وَرِضْوَنٌۭ مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۚ ذَلِكَ هُوَ ٱلْفَوْزُ ٱلْعَظِيمُ ‎⟫
> *Allah has promised to the believers—men and women—Gardens under which rivers flow, wherein they shall dwell forever, and beautiful mansions in Gardens of Eden. Yet the greatest of all is the Good Pleasure of Allah. That is the supreme attainment.*

Maulānā ʿAlī teaches that it is a scholar's blessing to acquire knowledge and contemplate it deeply. Allāh Himself is singular—"One"—and He has created every being in singularity; each human possesses a unique identity, a solitary station in which no other participates. Therefore, true knowledge of the self is the most essential knowledge—yet one that the soul cannot fully grasp. This is why the Messenger of Allāh (may the blessings of Allāh and peace be upon him and his family) declared: ⟪ar-quote:من عرف نفسہ فقد عرف ربہ⟫ "Whoever knows his own soul, verily he knows his Lord."[^cite-17] In the early stages of acquiring knowledge, a person experiences joy akin to that of one returning from the exile of ignorance to the peace of home. The wisest among humankind are the most alive, and the most alive are those closest to Allāh—for life itself is joy.

This happiness differs entirely from pleasures obtained through mundane means. Maulānā ʿAlī observes that the true ⟪ar:'فقیہ'⟫ (*faqīh*, jurist or scholar of spiritual law) is one who does not disappoint people regarding the mercy of Allāh. Such a person dwells perpetually in the light of Divine mercy, never tasting despair. He possesses confidence that whatever Allāh ordains contains within it the fullness of His compassion. As Allāh states:

> ⟪quran 15:56⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قَالَ وَمَن يَقْنَطُ مِن رَّحْمَةِ رَبِّهِۦٓ إِلَّا ٱلضَّآلُّونَ ‎⟫
> *[Abraham] said: "And who despairs of the Mercy of his Lord except those who have gone astray?"*

And again:

> ⟪quran 6:54⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذَا جَآءَكَ ٱلَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِـَٔايَتِنَا فَقُلْ سَلَمٌ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَىٰ نَفْسِهِ ٱلرَّحْمَةَ ۖ أَنَّهُۥ مَنْ عَمِلَ مِنكُمْ سُوٓءًۢا بِجَهَلَةٍۢ ثُمَّ تَابَ مِنۢ بَعْدِهِۦ وَأَصْلَحَ فَأَنَّهُۥ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *When those who believe in Our signs come to you, say: "Peace be upon you. Your Lord has prescribed mercy upon Himself. Whosoever among you commits evil in ignorance and thereafter repents and reforms—verily He is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful."*

The joy dwelling in Allāh's mercy is, in its essence, the definition of beauty. Yet this beauty transcends aesthetics; it is the true beauty, the sublime imagination that arises from the intellect. The Arabic word ⟪ar:'أحسان'⟫ (*ihsān*, excellence or virtue) often signifies moral perfection, yet it also carries the meaning ⟪ar:حُسن⟫ (*husn*, beauty)—those qualities that render the soul itself beautiful. Maulānā ʿAlī teaches that the excellence of intellect lies in perceiving ⟪ar:ینظر جمال الظاہر والباطن⟫ the beauty of all things, both external and internal. The beauty of outward forms and deeds is perfected by their inner radiance, just as the beauty of actions springs from the beauty and virtue of the soul. Thus did the Prophet (peace be upon him) say: "Allāh is beautiful and loves beautiful things."[^cite-18]

By cultivating noble character within oneself, a person becomes capable of loving Allāh—for Allāh loves what is beautiful. Because of these virtuous dispositions, ⟪ar:محمد مصطفی صلی اللہ علیہ و آلہ و سلم⟫ became the most beloved servant of Allāh. He summoned his *Umma* (community) to adopt these same exalted manners and declared:

> ⟪quran 3:31⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلْ إِن كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ ٱللَّهَ فَٱتَّبِعُونِى يُحْبِبْكُمُ ٱللَّهُ وَيَغْفِرْ لَكُمْ ذُنُوبَكُمْ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *Say: "If you love Allah, then follow me, and Allah will love you and forgive you your sins. And Allah is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful."*

In exposition of this verse, the Creator of all existence declares: ⟪ar-quote:اول العقل التَوَدُّد⟫ "The foundation of intellect is love."[^cite-19] To cultivate the principles of love within one's being and then to express this love through outward action—so that it becomes the radiance of the exterior and the attraction of the interior—this is the essence of following the Messenger of Allāh. For following him is nothing other than embodying his moral character, given that only he achieved the perfection of these virtues. Thus we understand that the intellect's connection to Truth is established through the finest moral qualities: gentleness, contentment, gratitude, generosity, shame, wisdom, forbearance—each beautiful in itself, each kindling love in both the seen and unseen worlds. A true intellect is the living embodiment of all these virtues; without them, the intellect remains incomplete. Through these qualities, one creates depth in spontaneous action and brings forth the hidden treasures of understanding.

Molding these virtues into the crucible of one's own soul, uniting them within—this is, in essence, an act of *tawḥīd* (توحید, witnessing Divine oneness). Although truth touches the soul, morality must become the leavening agent for the intellect, allowing it to spread through action and reach its perfection by actualizing ⟪ar:بالفعل⟫ what was previously mere ⟪ar:بالقوۃ⟫ potential. Thus all moral depravity is not merely evil; it is a cause of intellectual enfeeblement. The heart grows sick thereby, and the eye grows blind—unable to perceive reality itself. The Qur'ān attests:

> ⟪quran 2:10⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فِى قُلُوبِهِم مَّرَضٌۭ فَزَادَهُمُ ٱللَّهُ مَرَضًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ أَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا كَانُوا۟ يَكْذِبُونَ ‎⟫
> *In their hearts is a sickness, and Allah has increased their sickness. A painful torment awaits them, for they used to lie.*

> ⟪quran 22:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَلَمْ يَسِيرُوا۟ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ فَتَكُونَ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌۭ يَعْقِلُونَ بِهَآ أَوْ آذَانٌۭ يَسْمَعُونَ بِهَا ۖ فَإِنَّهَا لَا تَعْمَى ٱلْأَبْصَرُ وَلَكِن تَعْمَى ٱلْقُلُوبُ ٱلَّتِى فِى ٱلصُّدُورِ ‎⟫
> *Have they not journeyed through the earth, possessing hearts to comprehend with, or ears to hear? Verily, it is not the eyes that grow blind—but it is the hearts within the breasts that grow blind.*

Maulānā ʿAlī teaches that he who subdues his desires has prospered. Through this well-being comes the happiness born of certainty—and the spirit of that certainty arises from the union of *niyyah* (intention) and sincerity, combined with observance of the *Sharīʿah* (Divine Law). Should sincerity be absent from the performance of the Law, then what remains is hypocrisy and pretense—which themselves constitute *shirk* (associating partners with Allāh). Thus he declares: "Know that even the slightest hypocrisy is *shirk*."[^cite-20] Allāh elucidates this in the *Sūra* of the Deceivers:

> ⟪quran 107:1-7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَرَءَيْتَ ٱلَّذِى يُكَذِّبُ بِٱلدِّينِ ‎ ‏فَذَلِكَ ٱلَّذِى يَدُعُّ ٱلْيَتِيمَ ‎ ‏وَلَا يَحُضُّ عَلَىٰ طَعَامِ ٱلْمِسْكِينِ ‎ ‏فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْمُصَلِّينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَآءُونَ ‎ ‏وَيَمْنَعُونَ ٱلْمَاعُونَ ‎⟫
> *Hast thou seen him who denies the Faith? Behold, he it is who repulses the orphan and does not urge the feeding of the poor. Woe to the worshippers who are heedless of their prayers, who perform them only to be seen of men, and refuse small kindnesses.*

This *Sūra* demonstrates that external acts of worship possess no worth unless accompanied by sincerity and a life of virtue. Without this inward depth, religion becomes hollow. An action beautified by pure intention is a true deed; otherwise, all outward performance is mere dust, rising not in Allāh's sight:

> ⟪quran 22:37⟫
> ⟪ar:‏لَن يَنَالَ ٱللَّهَ لُحُومُهَا وَلَا دِمَآؤُهَا وَلَكِن يَنَالُهُ ٱلتَّقْوَىٰ مِنكُمْ ۚ كَذَلِكَ سَخَّرَهَا لَكُمْ لِتُكَبِّرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ عَلَىٰ مَا هَدَىٰكُمْ ۗ وَبَشِّرِ ٱلْمُحْسِنِينَ ‎⟫
> *Neither their flesh nor their blood reaches Allah—but piety from you reaches Him. Thus have We subjected them to you, that you might magnify Allah for His guidance to you. And give glad tidings to the doers of good.*

Maulānā ʿAlī declares: "He who possesses no intellect possesses no religion. And the sleep of certainty is superior to the waking of doubt." Such persons remain spiritually awake even in slumber. Thus did the Messenger of Allāh (peace be upon him) say: "My eyes sleep, but my heart remains vigilant."[^cite-21] The wise understand that although external acts of worship are necessary in themselves, the blessings of Allāh cannot be obtained through them alone. They require awareness—consciousness of *what* one does and *why* one does it. This consciousness, united with noble character and inner beauty, draws down the acceptance of Allāh. Maulānā ʿAlī states: "The best knowledge for you is that which renders your deeds acceptable to Allāh."

*Verses referenced in this topic (curated linkage from KASHKOLE. TopicAyats—5 of 5 not already cited above):*

> ⟪quran 2:25⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَبَشِّرِ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ أَنَّ لَهُمْ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ ۖ كُلَّمَا رُزِقُوا۟ مِنْهَا مِن ثَمَرَةٍۢ رِّزْقًۭا ۙ قَالُوا۟ هَذَا ٱلَّذِى رُزِقْنَا مِن قَبْلُ ۖ وَأُتُوا۟ بِهِۦ مُتَشَبِهًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ فِيهَآ أَزْوَجٌۭ مُّطَهَّرَةٌۭ ۖ وَهُمْ فِيهَا خَلِدُونَ ‎⟫
> *And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous deeds: for them are Gardens beneath which rivers flow. Whenever they are provided with fruit therefrom, they will say, "This is what we were provided before"—yet it shall be given them in likeness. And therein they shall have purified spouses, and therein they shall abide forever.*

> ⟪quran 38:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَخْلَصْنَهُم بِخَالِصَةٍۢ ذِكْرَى ٱلدَّارِ ‎⟫
> *Verily, We chose them for a distinct favor: the remembrance of the Hereafter.*

> ⟪quran 55:60⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هَلْ جَزَآءُ ٱلْإِحْسَنِ إِلَّا ٱلْإِحْسَنُ ‎⟫
> *Is there any recompense for goodness other than goodness?*

> ⟪quran 87:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْآخِرَةُ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَبْقَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Yet the Hereafter is better and more enduring.*

> ⟪quran 89:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎⟫
> *O soul at peace and contentment!*

---

<!-- section 6 (id=3600, raw_sort=6): Life of the Hereafter While Dwelling in This World -->

## Life of the Hereafter While Dwelling in This World

He declares that the believers are bound to this world through their bodies alone; their souls remain tethered to the Hereafter. His statement may be illuminated by another utterance of Amīr al-Muʾminīn, wherein he speaks of a people whose spiritual station is such that their hearts dwell in Paradise even as their bodies labor in this world. Your words that the hearts are "settled" in heaven signify that although they inhabit this world, they have already attained Paradise spiritually, conceptually, and in truth. This affirmation confirms the Messenger of Allāh's teaching: "Allāh preserves His servants in the state they desire." Those who live by the upper world order their entire existence upon the Hereafter as foundation; for those anchored in this world, by contrast, the world itself becomes the source of all thought and conception. Their imaginings, ruminations, and all actions bear the imprint of this lower realm. Yet the wise base every deed upon the reward they shall receive in the Hereafter—understanding the reality that "all action is dust save that which is sincere and which Allāh accepts."

Maulānā ʿAlī speaks frequently of Paradise's blessings and Hell's torments in his sermons. Does this not lend a commercial hue to Divine command? By no means! To know of heaven and hell is one matter; to comprehend their meaning is another. His aim is to instill in the *Umma* a feeling through which morality becomes luminous. From a mercenary perspective, a commodity becomes worthless once its transaction is complete. Shall then the attributes of piety, noble conduct, and the avoidance of forbidden acts become useless upon attaining Paradise? Never! Rather, the very atmosphere of Paradise *is* these attributes. His mention of Paradise serves a single purpose: that a person prepare himself while in this world for the environment of that Paradise, so that he might enter it. In one sermon, speaking of Paradise, he paints this vision:

If you turn your heart to the descriptions of Paradise, your soul will recoil from the marvels, pleasures, and blandishments of this world. And she will be lost in Paradise's vision—in the swaying streams along canal banks, their roots in fragrant musk dunes, their branches hung with glittering pearls.

The highest station of certainty—⟪ar:'روحانیت'⟫ (*rūḥāniyyat*, spirituality)—surpasses even the desire for heaven and fear of hell. When this spiritual station is attained, the soul becomes "heavenly" even while dwelling in the mortal realm. The state of Paradise is such that the soul finds satisfaction only in the overwhelming presence of its Lord, desiring nothing besides. The Qur'ān designates this state ⟪ar:'نفس المطمئنۃ'⟫ (*nafs al-muṭmaʾinna*, the soul at peace):

> ⟪quran 89:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎⟫
> *O soul at peace, return to thy Lord, well-pleased and well-pleasing!*

This soul's contentment springs from complete faith. And this Qur'ānic verse resonates throughout Maulānā ʿAlī's discourse:

> ⟪quran 87:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْآخِرَةُ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَبْقَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Yet the Hereafter is better and more enduring.*

The Hereafter is not merely a "time" when divine revelations shall be fulfilled and glad tidings realized; it is a "home" wherein all loftiest attributes—earthly and divine—shall manifest, their merest reflections visible in this world. Thus the mere mention and conception of Paradise purifies the intellect and turns it from worldly desires and pleasures. As Allāh states:

> ⟪quran 38:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَخْلَصْنَهُم بِخَالِصَةٍۢ ذِكْرَى ٱلدَّارِ ‎⟫
> *Verily, We chose them for a distinct favor: the remembrance of the Hereafter.*

In other words, pure knowledge of the Hereafter creates the conception of becoming a "Paradise" within this world, enabling a person to practice the virtuous deeds and noble character that characterize the Hereafter—thus attaining happiness in both this world and the next. This proves that such moral qualities can only be cultivated by one whose eyes have been cleared of this world's veil, one who sees and feels the life of the Hereafter whilst dwelling in mortality. Goodness and virtue are not practiced in hope of future reward; rather, goodness *itself* constitutes part of that reward. Allāh declares:

> ⟪quran 55:60⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هَلْ جَزَآءُ ٱلْإِحْسَنِ إِلَّا ٱلْإِحْسَنُ ‎⟫
> *Is there any recompense for goodness other than goodness?*

Maulānā ʿAlī teaches: "The fruit of any good deed resembles its root"—meaning the end of any action lies contained in its beginning, in the intention. Here the following verse becomes profoundly relevant:

> ⟪quran 2:25⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَبَشِّرِ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ أَنَّ لَهُمْ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ ۖ كُلَّمَا رُزِقُوا۟ مِنْهَا مِن ثَمَرَةٍۢ رِّزْقًۭا ۙ قَالُوا۟ هَذَا ٱلَّذِى رُزِقْنَا مِن قَبْلُ ۖ وَأُتُوا۟ بِهِۦ مُتَشَبِهًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ فِيهَآ أَزْوَجٌۭ مُّطَهَّرَةٌۭ ۖ وَهُمْ فِيهَا خَلِدُونَ ‎⟫
> *And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous deeds: for them are Gardens beneath which rivers flow. Whenever they are provided with fruit therefrom, they will say, "This is what we were provided before"—yet it shall be given them in likeness. And therein they shall have purified spouses, and therein they shall abide forever.*

The fruits of the Hereafter are experienced in this world in the form of all goodness, beauty, truth, and the joys they engender. All these tastes constitute a foretaste of the real sustenance of the Hereafter, to be obtained fully in Paradise. In the realm of morality, righteous deeds and the sense of their necessity (*iḥsān*, benevolence) are required not merely for salvation hereafter, but for salvation *in this world* as well. They liberate the soul outwardly from the bondage of sins and inwardly from the tyranny of ego. This liberation has been the focus and purpose of all such teachings.

---

<!-- section 7 (id=3581, raw_sort=7): That Which Is Easy for Them and Difficult for Others -->

## That Which Is Easy for Them and Difficult for Others

He declares: "Those things are easy for them and difficult for those who are heedless. They love him from whom the ignorant feel alienated." This utterance describes the perpetual effect upon the hearts of Allāh's saints. They constantly remember death and their encounter with their Lord; thus, through His aid, they renounce the world. What appears as alienating to the ignorant are the apparent hardships, sufferings, and deprivations of this life. Yet the Qur'ān testifies:

> ⟪quran 2:155-157⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَنَبْلُوَنَّكُم بِشَىْءٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْخَوْفِ وَٱلْجُوعِ وَنَقْصٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْأَمْوَلِ وَٱلْأَنفُسِ وَٱلثَّمَرَتِ ۗ وَبَشِّرِ ٱلصَّبِرِينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ إِذَآ أَصَبَتْهُم مُّصِيبَةٌۭ قَالُوٓا۟ إِنَّا لِلَّهِ وَإِنَّآ إِلَيْهِ رَجِعُونَ ‎ ‏أُو۟لَٓئِكَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَلَوَتٌۭ مِّن رَّبِّهِمْ وَرَحْمَةٌۭ ۖ وَأُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْمُهْتَدُونَ ‎⟫
> *And We shall surely test you with fear and hunger and loss of wealth and lives and fruits. Yet give glad tidings to those who patiently bear these trials—those who, when calamity befalls them, say: "Verily we belong to Allah, and to Him we shall return." Upon them are blessings from their Lord and mercy, and they are the guided ones.*

⟪ar:مھتدون⟫ These guided souls bear trials with patience, perceiving and tasting the blessings that arise from such steadfastness, grounded in true knowledge:

> ⟪quran 103:1-3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْعَصْرِ ‎ ‏إِنَّ ٱلْإِنسَنَ لَفِى خُسْرٍ ‎ ‏إِلَّا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلصَّبْرِ ‎⟫
> *By the Age: behold, man is in loss, save those who believe and do righteous deeds, and exhort one another to truth and exhort one another to patience.*

These are believers steadfast in trial, who know their origin and destiny, who hold firm to Allāh's word: "To Him we shall return." Because of this knowledge, the world's difficulties become facile for them. The heedless, by contrast, taste only their bitterness and pain. The ease concealed within these trials remains hidden from the ignorant but luminous to the wise:

> ⟪quran 94:5-6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَإِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًا ‎ ‏إِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًۭا ‎⟫
> *Verily, with hardship comes ease. Verily, with hardship comes ease.*

These wise ones not only perceive the fruit of relief that follows hardship through insight; they taste it directly. They befriend suffering and trial, whilst the ignorant recoil from them. For this reason, he declared: "Death is as dear to me as a mother's breast to a newborn child."[^cite-22] He speaks of this love for death while yet alive—as though he beholds death's reality and the blessings following it with his own eyes. He proclaimed further: "I am death's death!"—for life in this world is itself a kind of death, a hindrance and a constraint. Allāh testifies:

> ⟪quran 29:64⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمَا هَذِهِ ٱلْحَيَوٰةُ ٱلدُّنْيَآ إِلَّا لَهْوٌۭ وَلَعِبٌۭ ۚ وَإِنَّ ٱلدَّارَ ٱلْآخِرَةَ لَهِىَ ٱلْحَيَوَانُ ۚ لَوْ كَانُوا۟ يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *And this worldly life is naught but sport and diversion. Yet the Home of the Hereafter—that is the true life, if they but knew.*

### Asceticism

It bears emphasis here that these declarations do not call for renunciation of the physical world itself, but for transcendence of the world's "worldliness"—the severing of that relationship rooted in ⟪ar:'أنا'⟫ (*anā*, the ego-self) bound to temporal existence. Amīr al-Muʾminīn describes this state, which he terms ⟪ar:'زہد'⟫ (*zuhd*, asceticism), in *Nahj al-Balāgha* (⟪ar:نہج البلاغۃ⟫):

This world is a place appointed for destruction, and ruin has been decreed for its dwellers. It is sweet and alluring. Whoever pursues it hastens toward it; whoever gazes upon it becomes attached to it. Therefore, gather from it the finest provision and depart; ask for nothing save what is essential.

In another passage, he teaches that the finest provision for the Hereafter is ⟪ar:'زہد'⟫ (*zuhd*, asceticism) bound to ⟪ar:'تقوی'⟫ (*taqwā*, God-consciousness)—that is, the measure of one's provision for the next life corresponds to one's detachment from the transient things of this world:

> ⟪quran 17:18⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مَّن كَانَ يُرِيدُ ٱلْعَاجِلَةَ عَجَّلْنَا لَهُۥ فِيهَا مَا نَشَآءُ لِمَن نُّرِيدُ ثُمَّ جَعَلْنَا لَهُۥ جَهَنَّمَ يَصْلَىٰهَا مَذْمُومًۭا مَّدْحُورًۭا ‎⟫
> *Whoever desires the fleeting life, We hasten to grant him therein what We will—for whom We choose. Then We have prepared for him Hell, wherein he shall burn, disgraced and rejected.*

The following utterances of Maulānā ʿAlī epitomize this worldly contempt:

I swear by Allāh! In my sight, your world is as vile as a pig's bone gnawed in the grasp of a leper. The world is like a serpent—gentle to the touch, yet full of deadly venom. To me, this world is as the moisture that flows from a goat's nose.[^cite-23]

The magnificence of Allāh renders this world contemptible and debased. When this world is viewed in the light of the Absolute Real (⟪ar:الحق⟫), all its pleasures appear transient and trivial. The littleness of His servants becomes evident against His greatness. Maulānā ʿAlī praised a believer thus: ⟪ar-quote:کان یعظمہ فی عینی، صغار الدنیا فی عینہ⟫ "He whom the contempt of this world made great in my eyes."[^cite-24] The world was not deemed inferior to the Creator because it was useless, but because of Allāh's greatness, the Hereafter, and the absolute realities made manifest to such souls—because of which the world became diminished in their sight. For:

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And do not invoke any other god with Allah. There is no god save He. All things shall perish save His Face. His is the Command, and unto Him you shall be returned.*

The world's true value lies in this: it contains creatures of Allāh who glorify Him morning and evening, acknowledging His majesty:

> ⟪quran 17:44⟫
> ⟪ar:‏تُسَبِّحُ لَهُ ٱلسَّمَوَتُ ٱلسَّبْعُ وَٱلْأَرْضُ وَمَن فِيهِنَّ ۚ وَإِن مِّن شَىْءٍ إِلَّا يُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِهِۦ وَلَكِن لَّا تَفْقَهُونَ تَسْبِيحَهُمْ ۗ إِنَّهُۥ كَانَ حَلِيمًا غَفُورًۭا ‎⟫
> *The seven heavens and the earth and all that is therein glorify Him. There is not a thing but glorifies His Praise—yet you comprehend not their glorification. Verily, He is Ever Forbearing, Most Forgiving.*

> ⟪quran 24:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ مَن فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱلطَّيْرُ صَٓفَّتٍۢ ۖ كُلٌّۭ قَدْ عَلِمَ صَلَاتَهُۥ وَتَسْبِيحَهُۥ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ عَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا يَفْعَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *Do you not see that all in the heavens and earth glorify Allah?—the very birds with wings spread. Each knows its prayer and its glorification. And Allah is All-Knowing of what they do.*

Yet here an apparent contradiction surfaces: the world is, in one sense, a "place of ruin," and in another, a "place of good" wherein one prepares deeds for the Hereafter. In his sermons, Maulānā ʿAlī praises Allāh for the creation and natural order—peacocks, birds, even ants, dragons, and elephants. In another discourse, he uses the world's blessings to elucidate the blessings of Paradise, declaring that when the eye beholds Paradise's vistas, even the finest blessings and most exquisite scenes of this world become despised. Because of this, all worldly hardships become facile and become, moreover, a source of joy. ⟪ar:زاہدین،⟫ Through spiritual resources obtained by faith, the ascetics endure all trials. They possess knowledge granting such firm and perfect certainty that they declare: ⟪ar-quote:لو کشف الغطاء ما الزدت یقینا⟫ "Even were the veil removed, my certainty would not increase."[^cite-25]

Speaking of his sincerity, he witnesses: "I bear testimony that there is no god save Allāh. The sincerity of this my testimony has been tested, and its essence—its ⟪ar:مُعتقدٌ مصاصُہُ⟫ very marrow—is mingled with conviction."[^cite-26] In Arabic, ⟪ar:'مصاص'⟫ (*misāss*) signifies "to suck," and the subtle extract of any thing is that which contains its essence. Just as the pith of fruit is what one suckles from it, so the sincerity of his testimony is the spiritual substance of the soul—not the mental image arising from mere words, nor their apparent meaning. Words are but echoes of that spiritual substance established within the heart.

He returns to the statement that those things are easy for them which are difficult for the heedless, and they love that from which the ignorant recoil. In one sense it is "trial," in another "death" itself. For the ignorant, death is a terrifying dissolution wherein the body separates from the self—an ending of life rather than its beginning. It means separation from that which has been his center and focus throughout life. For the wise, conversely, death is salvation from suffering and encounter with Allāh; it is the completion of *tawḥīd* (*توحید*, witnessing oneness), wherein the soul merges into His transcendent realm and becomes "unified" with Him. Only one who immerses himself in this ocean can taste its sweetness. The fire of this love burns all components to ash. Those enslaved by ego remain entangled in fragmentation, inward and outward. But the wise soul remains ever focused upon remembrance of the Absolute, and the joy arising therefrom displaces the ego, shattering all illusion.

---

<!-- section 8 (id=3583, raw_sort=8): The Philosophy of Justice -->

## The Philosophy of Justice

⟪ar:أمیر المومنین⟫ Amīr al-Muʾminīn's clearest exposition of ⟪ar:'عدل'⟫ (*ʿadl*, justice) is found in the letter he inscribed to ⟪ar:'مالک اشتر بن الحارث النخئی'⟫ (*Mālik al-Ashtar*), whom he appointed as governor of Egypt. In his vision, the inclination of moral law toward justice pertains not to the external realm alone, but extends into the spiritual world itself. The principles of justice he establishes transcend procedural constraints. In his utterances, thought and action appear mutually complementary, reflective of ⟪ar:'توحید'⟫ (*tawḥīd*, the witness of Divine oneness). The lives of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and ʿAlī (peace be upon him) exemplify these principles incarnate.

On one hand, ⟪ar:امیر المونین⟫ Amīr al-Muʾminīn was himself the perfect embodiment of justice; on the other, in the foundations of his justice we discover profound spiritual lessons—how a life lived in love for Allāh naturally flowers into virtue. A life that mirrors oneself in ⟪ar:'الحق'⟫ (*al-Ḥaqq*, the Truth/the Real)! When we examine ethics ⟪ar:'أحسان'⟫ (*ihsān*, excellence) in the broad sphere of morality, we find that the synthesis of moral dimensions and qualities creates a depth that molds both into something fundamental. Common questions of right and wrong are transmuted into the singular question: "What is Reality?"

ʿAlī's spiritual understanding of *tawḥīd* (توحید) is not merely that Allāh has no parallel, but that none stands in opposition to Him. Thus every good ⟪ar:حَسَنَ⟫ deed, being an expression of Allāh's will, stands in no antithesis to moral evil. ⟪ar:'الحق'⟫ Good possesses its own singular and individual existence; by contrast, ⟪ar:'عدم'⟫ (*ʿadam*, non-being) is all that stands against it. Therefore, if good is the positive aspect, then evil is the "capacity" or "intention" toward negating the good. In other words: if goodness is an attribute of the Creator, then evil is an attribute of creation—a privation of His attributes. Allāh declares:

> ⟪quran 113:2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مِن شَرِّ مَا خَلَقَ ‎⟫
> *From the evil of what He has created.*

This verse is frequently mistranslated to suggest that Allāh created evil itself—a rendering both theologically and linguistically erroneous. Allāh states clearly that the "evil" emerging from His "creation" was revealed. That is, He created free creatures possessed of good qualities; they themselves created "evil" by negating these attributes. Therefore, one cannot say Allāh created evil. He created only the conditions wherein His creatures, though capable of choosing Truth, may choose otherwise. This proves that evil is, in reality, merely a negation of good—it possesses no independent existence. This verse may also be understood thus: "I seek refuge in the Truth from the unjust." Evil manifests only as a negation of Truth, which the heart's eye perceives as an "illusion." Just as reason can shatter any illusion, so Truth and goodness possess the power to overcome any evil. The more a soul stands as a witness before its Lord, the more it can overcome evil through the firmness of will. This maturity extends from intellect to heart, convincing it that good is more "real" than evil—a conviction strengthened ⟪ar:'الحق'⟫ through knowledge itself.

Since evil does not truly exist—it is an object that has deviated from its station—restoration and return to Truth become necessary. Therefore, in Amīr al-Muʾminīn's vision, fulfilling one's obligations and honoring the rights of all (toward Allāh, toward oneself, toward all creation) constitutes the definition of justice. Speaking to this, he declares: "Justice is the act of placing things in their proper station."[^cite-27] The more a person's actions remain in their rightful place, the more just he becomes. This essence of justice is present in a person to the degree that his actions are rooted in ⟪ar:'الحق'⟫ (*al-Ḥaqq*, the Truth/the Real). First, one must *become* ⟪ar:'الحق'⟫ good; only then can one *do* ⟪ar:'الحق'⟫ good. And to become good is to actualize ⟪ar:توحید⟫ *tawḥīd*—for He alone is One.

An analysis of the letter to ⟪ar:مالک اشتر⟫ *Mālik al-Ashtar* reveals that justice is not the name of any single attribute, but of the *sum* of all virtues—particularly the three cardinal virtues: temperance, courage, and wisdom. When these three stand in their proper places, then the self may be called just.

Ethics and spirituality intertwine, as is evident from the narration: Once, when the Messenger of Allāh (peace be upon him and his family) was seated among his companions, Gabriel (peace be upon him) came in human form and asked: "⟪ar:یا محمد (ﷺ)!⟫ Tell me of ⟪ar:'اسلام'⟫ (*islām*, submission)."[^cite-28] He replied: "⟪ar:الأسلام⟫ *Islām* is to bear witness that there is no god save Allāh and that Muḥammad is His Messenger, and to establish prayer, give *zakat*, fast during Ramaḍan, and perform the pilgrimage to the House of Allāh." Gabriel affirmed: "You have spoken truth!" He then asked: "Tell me of ⟪ar:'ایمان'⟫ (*īmān*, faith)." He replied: "Faith is belief in Allāh, His Angels, His Books, His Messengers, the Last Day, and in both reward and punishment in the Hereafter." Gabriel affirmed again: "You have spoken truth!" Then he asked: "Tell me what ⟪ar:'أحسان'⟫ (*ihsān*, excellence) is." He responded: "It is to worship Allāh as though you see Him with your own eyes; and if you cannot achieve this, then at least worship Him knowing that He sees you."[^cite-29]

---

*Note*: The literal sense of *ihsān* is "to do beautifully," derived from *hasana* (to be beautiful). In Arabic, goodness is called *ḥasan* and evil *qabīḥ*—literally, beauty and ugliness.

---

The constant presence of Allāh and consciousness of standing in His sight permeates all these grand stations. As the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared: "Worship Allāh as though you see Him."[^cite-30] Thus is the concept of *ihsān* rooted in *islām*. On one hand, ʿAlī (peace be upon him) teaches in his sermons: "Know that every deed depends upon your *niyyah* (intention)—upon how you regard 'excellence.'"[^cite-31] And on the other hand, he teaches: "Pretense, arrogance, and self-laudation are Satan's finest snares, by which he destroys ⟪ar:محسنین⟫ those of ⟪ar:احسان⟫ excellence."[^cite-32] The primary purpose of worship is the annihilation of the ⟪ar:أنا'⟫ (*anā*, ego-self), of ⟪ar:أنانیت⟫ (*anāniyyat*, egoism) in the sight of Allāh.

His first utterance calls for justice, which places all things—⟪ar:أنائیت⟫ including selfhood—in their rightful station. His second utterance discloses the root cause of all injustice: ⟪ar:کبر⟫ (*kibr*, arrogance), ⟪ar:حرس⟫ (*hirs*, greed), and ⟪ar:حسد⟫ (*hasad*, envy), which are termed the ⟪ar:'أمہات معاصی'⟫ (*ummahāt al-maʿāsī*, the mothers of transgression).


<!-- section 9 (id=3582, raw_sort=9): Letter to Malik al-Ashtar -->

## Letter to Malik al-Ashtar

This is what Allah's servant ʿAlī, Amīr al-Muʾminīn (Commander of the Faithful), has ordered Malik ibn al-Ḥārith al-Ashtar in his instrument of appointment when he made him Governor of Egypt—to collect its revenues, wage jihād against its enemies, seek the welfare of its people, and ensure the prosperity of its cities.

⟪ar-quote:هذَا مَا أَمَرَ بِهِ عَبْدُ اللهِ عَلِيٌ أَميِرُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ، مَالِكَ بْنَ الْحَارِثِ الاْشْتَرَ فِي عَهْدِهِ إِلَيْهِ، حِينَ وَلاَّهُ مِصْرَ- جِبْوةَ خَرَاجِهَا، وَجِهَادَ عَدُوِّهَا، وَاسْتِصْلاَحَ أَهْلِهَا، وَعِمَارَةَ بِلاَدِهَا⟫

He commands him to fear Allah (taqwā, religious piety), to prefer obedience to Him, and to follow what He has commanded in His Book—both obligatory and voluntary precepts. Adherence to these brings felicity, while neglect and transgression lead only to wretchedness. He orders him to support Allah the Glorified with heart, hand, and tongue, for Allah whose name is Sublime takes responsibility for helping those who help Him and protecting those who give Him support.[^cite-33] Moreover, he must break his heart away from passions and restrain it when desires surge, since the soul commands evil unless Allah shows mercy.

⟪ar-quote:أَمَرَهُ بِتَقْوَى اللهِ، وَإِيثَارِ طَاعَتِهِ، وَاتِّبَاعِ مَا أَمَرَ بِهِ فِي كِتَابِهِ- مِنْ فَرَائِضِهِ وَسُنَنِهِ، الَّتِي لاَ يَسْعَدُ أَحَدٌ إِلاَّ بِاتِّبَاعِهَا، وَلاَ يَشْقَى إِلاَّ مَعَ جُحُودِهَا وَإِضَاعَتِهَا، وَأَنْ يَنْصُرَ اللهَ سُبْحَانَهُ بَيَدِهِ وَقَلْبِهِ وَلِسَانِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ، جَلَّ اسْمُهُ، قَدْ تَكَفَّلَ بِنَصْرِ مَنْ نَصَرَهُ، وَإِعْزَازِ مَنْ أَعَزَّهُ. وَأَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَكْسِرَ نَفْسَهُ عِنْدَ الشَّهَوَاتِ، وَيَزَعَهَا عِنْدَ الْجَمَحَاتِ، فَإِنَّ النَّفْسَ أَمَّارَةٌ بِالسُّوءِ، إِلاَّ مَا رَحِمَ اللهُ⟫

## The Qualifications and Responsibilities of a Governor

Know, O Malik, that I have sent you to a land that has witnessed both just and oppressive rule. The people will scrutinize your conduct as you yourself once scrutinized your predecessors, and they will speak of you as you spoke of them. The righteous are recognized by the reputation that Allah circulates about them through the words of His servants.[^cite-34] Therefore, let the most valuable treasure with you be righteous deeds. Master your desires and guard yourself from what is unlawful, for true restraint means holding your soul between what it loves and what it dislikes.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ اعْلَمْ يَا مَالكُ، أَنِّي قدْ وَجَّهْتُكَ إِلَى بِلاَد قَدْ جَرَتْ عَلَيْهَا دُوَلٌ قَبْلَكَ، مِنْ عَدْل وَجَوْر، وَأَنَّ النَّاسَ يَنْظُرُونَ مِنْ أُمُورِكَ فِى مِثْلِ مَا كُنْتَ تَنْظُرُ فِيهِ مِنْ أُمُورِ الْوُلاَةِ قَبْلَكَ، وَيَقُولُونَ فِيكَ مَا كُنْتَ تَقُولُ فِيهِمْ،إِنَّمَا يُسْتَدَلُّ عَلَى الصَّالِحِينَ بِمَا يُجْرِي اللهُ لَهُمْ عَلَى أَلْسُنِ عِبَادِهِ. فَلْيَكُنْ أَحَبَّ الذَّخَائِرِ إِلَيْكَ ذَخِيرَةُ الْعَمَلِ الصَّالِحِ، فَامْلِكْ هَوَاكَ، وَشُحَّ بِنَفْسِكَ عَمَّا لاَ يَحِلُّ لَكَ، فَإِنَّ الشُّحَّ بِالنَّفْسِ الاْنْصَافُ مِنْهَا فَيَما أَحْبَبْتَ وَكَرِهْتَ⟫

Cultivate mercy in your heart toward the subjects and affection for them, treating them with gentleness. Do not stand over them as a ravenous beast seeking to devour them, for they are of two kinds: brothers to you in faith, or equals in creation. They will stumble and encounter afflictions; some act wrongfully intentionally, others through oversight. Grant them your pardon and forgiveness as you would wish Allah to grant you His pardon and mercy, for you stand above them, your appointed Commander stands above you, and Allah stands above him who appointed you.[^cite-35] He has entrusted their affairs to you and tested you through them.

⟪ar-quote:وَأَشْعِرْ قَلْبَكَ الرَّحْمَةَ لِلرَّعِيَّةِ، وَالْـمَحَبَّةَ لَهُمْ، وَاللُّطْفَ بِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَكُونَنَّ عَلَيْهِمْ سَبُعاً ضَارِياً تَغْتَنِمُ أَكْلَهُمْ، فَإِنَّهُمْ صِنْفَانِ- إِمَّا أَخٌ لَكَ فِي الدِّينِ، وَإمّا نَظِيرٌ لَكَ فِي الْخَلْقِ، يَفْرُطُ مِنْهُمُ الزَّلَلُ، وَتَعْرِضُ لَهُمُ الْعِلَلُ،يُؤْتَى عَلَى أَيْدِيهِمْ فِي الَعَمْدِ وَالْخَطَاَ، فَأَعْطِهِمْ مِنْ عَفْوِكَ وَصَفْحِكَ مِثْلَ الَّذِي تُحِبُّ أَنْ يُعْطِيَكَ اللهُ مِنْ عَفْوِهِ وَصَفْحِهِ، فَإِنَّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ، وَ وَالِي الاْمْرِ عَلَيْكَ فَوْقَكَ، وَاللهُ فَوْقَ مَنْ وَلاَّكَ! وَقَدِ اسْتَكْفَاكَ أَمْرَهُمْ، وَابْتَلاَكَ بِهِمْ⟫

Do not set yourself in opposition to Allah, for you have no power against His might and cannot do without His pardon and mercy. Do not regret forgiveness, nor boast of punishment. Do not hasten to act on anger when you can find an alternative. Do not say, "I have been given authority; I must be obeyed"—such words breed corruption in the heart, weaken faith, and bring one near ruin. When your authority produces arrogance or vanity, contemplate the greatness of Allah's dominion over you and His power, such as you possess over nothing. This will curb your haughtiness, cure your anger, and restore the wisdom you lost.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تَنْصِبَنَّ نَفْسَكَ لِحَرْبِ اللهِ، فَإِنَّهْ لاَيَدَيْ لَكَ بِنِقْمَتِهِ، وَلاَ غِنَى بِكَ عَنْ عَفْوِهِ وَرَحْمَتِهِ. وَلاَ تَنْدَمَنَّ عَلَى عَفْو، وَلاَ تَبْجَحَنَّ بِعُقُوبَة، وَلاَ تُسْرِعَنَّ إِلَى بَادِرَة وَجَدْتَ مِنْهَا مَنْدُوحَةً، وَلاَ تَقُولَنَّ- إِنِّي مُؤَمَّرٌ آمُرُ فَأُطَاعُ، فَإِنَّ ذلِكَ إِدْغَالٌ فِي الْقَلْبِ، وَمَنْهَكَةٌ لِلدِّينِ، وَتَقَرُّبٌ مِنَ الْغِيَرِ. وَإِذَا أَحْدَثَ لَكَ مَا أَنْتَ فِيهِ مِنْ سُلْطَانِكَ أُبَّهَةً أَوْ مَخِيلَةً، فَانْظُرْ إِلَى عِظَمِ مُلْكِ اللهِ فَوْقَكَ، وَقُدْرَتِهِ مَنْكَ عَلَى مَا لاَ تَقْدرِ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ نَفْسِكَ، فَإِنَّ ذلِكَ يُطَامِنُ إِلَيْكَ مِنْ طِمَاحِكَ، وَيَكُفُّ عَنْكَ مِنْ غَرْبِكَ،يَفِيءُ إِلَيْكَ بِمَا عَزَبَ عَنْكَ مِنْ عَقْلِكَ⟫

Beware of comparing yourself to Allah in His grandeur or likening yourself to Him in His might, for Allah humiliates every tyrant and disgraces every haughty one.[^cite-36]

⟪ar-quote:إِيَّاكَ وَمُسَامَاةَ اللهِ فِي عَظَمَتِهِ، وَالتَّشَبُّهَ بِهِ فِي جَبَرُوتِهِ، فَإِنَّ اللهَ يُذِلُّ كُلَّ جَبَّار، وَيُهِينُ كُلَّ مُخْتَال⟫

Act justly toward Allah and toward the people against yourself, your close kin, and those among your subjects for whom you feel inclination. If you do not, you will be unjust. When someone oppresses Allah's servants, Allah becomes his adversary instead of his creatures. When Allah contends with someone, He nullifies his argument and brings him into war with Him until he ceases and repents. Nothing is more conducive to reversing Allah's favor or hastening His retribution than persistence in injustice, for Allah hears the prayer of the oppressed and lies in wait for the oppressors.[^cite-37]

⟪ar-quote:أَنْصِفِ اللهَ وَأَنْصِفِ النَّاسَ مِنْ نَفْسِكَ، وَمِنْ خَاصَّةِ أَهْلِكَ، وَمَنْ لَكَ فِيهِ هَوىً مِنْ رَعِيَّتِكَ، فَإِنَّكَ إِلاَّ تَفْعَلْ تَظْلِمْ، وَمَنْ ظَلَمَ عِبَادَ اللهِ كَانَ اللهُ خَصْمَهُ دُونَ عِبَادِهِ، وَمَنْ خَاصَمَهُ اللهُ أَدْحَضَ حُجَّتَهُ، وَكَانَ لله حَرْباً حَتَّى يَنْزعَ وَيَتُوبَ. وَلَيْسَ شَيْءٌ أَدْعَى إِلَى تَغْيِيرِ نِعْمَةِ اللهِ وَتَعْجِيلِ نِقْمَتِهِ مِنْ إِقَامَة عَلَى ظُلْم، فَإِنَّ اللهَ سَميِعٌ دَعْوَةَ الْمَظْلُومِينَ، وَهُوَ لِلظَّالِمِينَ بِالْمِرْصَادِ⟫

The path you should love most is the one most equitable in upholding truth, most universal in dispensing justice, and most comprehensive in securing agreement among your subjects. The discontent of the common people erodes the satisfaction of the elite, while elite discontent may be overlooked when the common people are pleased. No class of subjects is more burdensome to a ruler in times of ease, less helpful in hardship, more averse to equitable treatment, more importunate in demands, less grateful for gifts, slower to excuse refusal, and weaker in enduring life's afflictions than the elite. The common people are the pillars of religion, the strength of the Muslims, and the defense against enemies. Your inclination and affection should therefore be toward them.

⟪ar-quote:كُنْ أَحَبَّ الاْمُورِ إِلَيْكَ أَوْسَطُهَا فِي الْحَقِّ، وَأَعَمُّهَا فِي الْعَدْلِ، وَأَجْمَعُهَا لِرِضَى الرَّعِيَّةِ، فَإِنَّ سُخْطَ الْعَامَّةِ يُجْحِفُ بِرِضَى الْخَاصَّةِ، وَإِنَّ سُخْطَ الْخَاصَّةِ يُغْتَفَرُ مَعَ رِضَى الْعَامَّةِ. وَلَيْسَ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الرَّعِيَّةِ، أَثْقَلَ عَلَى الْوَالِي مَؤُونَةً فِي الرَّخَاءِ، وَأَقَلَّ مَعُونَةً لَهُ فِي الْبَلاَءِ، وَأَكْرَهَ لِلاْنْصَافِ، وَأَسْأَلَ بِالاْلْحَافِ، وَأَقَلَّ شُكْراً عِنْدَ الاْعْطَاءِ، وَأَبْطَأَ عُذْراً عِنْدَ الْمَنْعِ، وَأَضْعَفَ صَبْراً عِنْدَ مُلِمَّاتِ الدَّهْرِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْخَاصَّةِ، وَإِنَّمَا عَمُودُ الدِّينِ، وَجِمَاعُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ، وَالْعُدَّةُ لِلاْعْدَاءِ، الْعَامَّةُ مِنَ الاْمَّةِ، فَلْيَكُنْ صِغْوُكَ لَهُمْ، وَمَيْلُكَ مَعَهُمْ⟫

Those among your subjects most distant from you and most hateful in your view should be those who eagerly search out others' faults, for people do have failings, and the ruler is most suited to cover them. Do not expose what remains hidden from you, for your duty is only to reform what is manifest, while Allah will judge what is hidden. Cover faults as much as you can—Allah will cover your faults from your subjects. Release the people from every knot of hatred and sever all causes of enmity. Feign ignorance of ambiguities. Do not hasten to confirm the report of a slanderer, for slander is deception clothed in the garb of good counsel.
