⟪ar-quote:وَلْيَكُنْ أَبْعَدَ رَعِيَّتِكَ مِنْكَ، وَأشْنَأَهُمْ عِنْدَكَ، أَطْلَبُهُمْ لِمَعَائِبِ النَّاسِ، فإنَّ في النَّاسِ عُيُوباً، الْوَالِي أَحَقُّ مَنْ سَتَرَهَا، فَلاَ تَكْشِفَنَّ عَمَّا غَابَ عَنْكَ مِنْهَا، فَإنَّمَا عَلَيْكَ تَطْهِيرُ مَا ظَهَرَ لَكَ، وَاللهُ يَحْكُمُ عَلَى مَا غَابَ عَنْكَ، فَاسْتُرِ الْعَوْرَةَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتَ يَسْتُرِ اللهُ مِنْكَ ما تُحِبُّ سَتْرَهُ مِنْ رَعِيَّتِكَ. أَطْلِقْ عَنِ النَّاسِ عُقْدَةَ كُلِّ حِقْد، وَاقْطَعْ عَنْكَ سَبَبَ كُلِّ وِتْر، وَتَغَابَ عَنْ كلِّ مَا لاَ يَضِحُ لَكَ، وَلاَ تَعْجَلَنَّ إِلَى تَصْدِيقِ سَاع، فَإِنَّ السَّاعِيَ غَاشٌ،⟫

Do not include in your consultations a miser who would deter you from generosity and threaten you with poverty, nor a coward who would weaken you in your affairs, nor a greedy person who would make evil acquisition appear beautiful. These three qualities—miserliness, cowardice, and greed—are different dispositions united only by a person's poor opinion of Allah.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تُدْخِلَنَّ فِي مَشُورَتِكَ بَخِيلاً يَعْدِلُ بِكَ عَنِ الْفَضْلِ، وَيَعِدُكَ الْفَقْرَ، وَلاَ جَبَاناً يُضعِّفُكَ عَنِ الاْمُورِ، وَلاَ حَرِيصاً يُزَيِّنُ لَكَ الشَّرَهَ بِالْجَوْرِ، فَإِنَّ الْبُخْلَ وَالْجُبْنَ وَالْحِرْصَ غَرَائِزُ شَتَّى يَجْمَعُهَا سُوءُ الظَّنِّ بِاللهِ⟫

The worst minister is one who served mischievous rulers before you and participated in their wrongdoings. Such a one should not be your intimate advisor, for they are abettors of sin and companions of oppression. Rather, seek from among others those with similar insight and effectiveness but without such sins and burdens. These are those who have never assisted an oppressor in oppression nor a sinner in sin. They will be less taxing on you and more supportive, more considerate toward you, and least inclined to others' company. Make them your intimate companions in private and in public.

⟪ar-quote:شَرُّ وُزَرَائِكَ مَنْ كَانَ لِلاْشْرَارِ قَبْلَكَ وَزِيراً، وَمَنْ شَرِكَهُمْ فِي الاْثَامِ، فَلاَ يَكُونَنَّ لَكَ بِطَانَةً، فَإِنَّهُمْ أَعْوَانُ الاْثَمَةِ، وَإِخْوَانُ الظَّلَمَةِ، وَأَنْتَ وَاجِدٌ مِنْهُمْ خَيْرَ الْخَلَفِ مِمَّنْ لَهُ مِثْلُ آرَائِهِمْ وَنَفَاذِهِمْ، وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ مِثْلُ آصَارِهِمْ وَأَوْزَارِهِمْ وَ آثَامِهِمْ، مِمَّنْ لَمْ يُعَاوِنْ ظَالِماً عَلَى ظُلْمِهِ، وَلاَ آثِماً عَلَى إِثْمِهِ، أُولئِكَ أَخَفُّ عَلَيْكَ مَؤُونَةً، وَأَحْسَنُ لَكَ مَعُونَةً، وَأَحْنَى عَلَيْكَ عَطْفاً، وَأَقَلُّ لِغَيْرِكَ إِلْفاً، فَاتَّخِذْ أُولئِكَ خَاصَّةً لِخَلَوَاتِكَ وَحَفَلاَتِكَ⟫

Among them, favor most those who speak bitter truth to you openly and support you least in actions Allah disapproves in His friends, even if such actions accord with your desires. Attach yourself to the God-fearing and the truthful; educate them so they do not praise you falsely or glorify deeds you did not perform. Excessive praise breeds arrogance and draws one near to vanity.[^cite-38]

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ لْيَكُنْ آثَرُهُمْ عِنْدَكَ أَقْوَلَهُمْ بِمُرِّ الْحَقِّ لَكَ، وأَقَلَّهُمْ مُسَاعَدَةً فِيَما يَكُونُ مِنْكَ مِمَّا كَرِهَ اللهُ لاِوْلِيَائِهِ، وَاقِعاً ذلِكَ مِنْ هَوَاكَ حَيْثُ وَقَعَ. وَالْصَقْ بِأَهْلِ الْوَرَعِ وَالصِّدْقِ، ثُمَّ رُضْهُمْ عَلَى أَلاَّ يُطْرُوكَ وَلاَ يُبَجِّحُوكَ بِبَاطِل لَمْ تَفْعَلْهُ، فَإِنَّ كَثْرَةَ الاْطْرَاءِ تُحْدِثُ الزَّهْوَ، وَتُدْنِي مِنَ الْعِزَّةِ⟫

The virtuous and the vicious must not occupy equal standing before you, for this discourages the virtuous from virtue and encourages the vicious toward vice. Hold each to the role they have chosen for themselves. Know that nothing more secures a ruler's favorable reputation with his subjects than beneficence toward them, lightening their burdens, and refraining from imposing unbearable hardships. Therefore, conduct yourself in such a way that you earn your subjects' favorable esteem, for such regard will relieve you of great anxieties. The one most deserving of your good opinion is he whom you have treated well, and the one most deserving of your poor opinion is he whom you have treated poorly.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ يَكُونَنَّ الْـمُحْسِنُ وَالْمُسِيءُ عِنْدَكَ بِمَنْزِلَة سَوَاء، فَإِنَّ فِي ذلِكَ تَزْهِيداً لاِهْلِ الاْحْسَانِ فِي الاْحْسَانِ،تَدْرِيباً لاِهْلِ الاْسَاءَةِ عَلَى الاْسَاءَةِ، وَأَلْزِمْ كُلاًّ مِنْهُمْ مَا أَلْزَمَ نَفْسَهُ. وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ شَيْءٌ بِأَدْعَى إِلَى حُسْنِ ظَنِّ وَال بِرَعِيَّتِهِ مِنْ إحْسَانِهِ إِلَيْهِمْ، وَتَخْفِيفِهِ الْمُؤُونَاتِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَتَرْكِ اسْتِكْرَاهِهِ إِيَّاهُمْ عَلَى مَا لَيْسَ لهُ قِبَلَهُمْ، فَلْيَكُنْ مِنْكَ فِي ذلِكَ أَمْرٌ يَجَتَمِعُ لَكَ بِهِ حُسْنُ الظَّنِّ بِرَعِيَّتِكَ، فَإِنَّ حُسْنُ الظَّنِّ يَقْطَعُ عَنْكَ نَصَباً طَوِيلاً، وَإِنَّ أَحَقَّ مَنْ حَسُنَ ظَنُّكَ بِهِ لَمَنْ حَسُنَ بَلاَؤُكَ عِنْدَهُ، وَإِنَّ أَحَقَّ مَنْ سَاءَ ظَنُّكَ بِهِ لَمَنْ سَاءَ بَلاَؤُكَ عِنْدَهُ⟫

Do not abrogate the upright practices of earlier leaders of this community through which unity was achieved and the subjects prospered. Do not innovate practices that harm those established traditions, for the reward of those who instituted them continues, while you bear the burden of what you have undone. Increase your deliberation with scholars and discussion with the wise to strengthen the prosperity of your realm and to continue what your predecessors established.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تَنْقُضْ سُنَّةً صَالِحَةً عَمِلَ بِهَا صُدُورُ هذِهِ الاْمَّةِ، وَاجْتَمَعتْ بِهَا الاْلْفَةُ، وَصَلَحَتْ عَلَيْهَا الرَّعِيَّةُ،لاَ تُحْدِثَنَّ سُنَّةً تَضُرُّ بِشَيء مِنْ مَاضِي تِلْكَ السُّنَنِ، فَيَكُونَ الاْجْرُ بِمَنْ سَنَّهَا، وَالْوِزْرُ عَلَيْكَ بِمَا نَقَضْتَ مِنْهَا. وَأَكْثِرْ مُدَارَسَةَ الَعُلَمَاءِ، وَمُنَافَثَةَ الْحُكَمَاءِ، فِي تَثْبِيتِ مَا صَلَحَ عَلَيْهِ أَمْرُ بِلاَدِكَ،⟫

Know that the subjects form strata; none can prosper except by supporting others, and none can be self-sufficient. Among them are the soldiers of Allah, the scribes serving the common people and the elite, the judges administering justice, the administrators of fairness and clemency, those who pay the poll tax (jizyah) and land tax (kharāj) from the protected non-Muslims and the Muslim commons, the merchants and artisans, and the lowest stratum of the needy and the destitute. Allah has fixed the portion of each and set forth His precepts concerning the limits and obligations of each in His Book and the Sunna of His Prophet, a covenant preserved among us.

⟪ar-quote:وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الرَّعِيَّةَ طَبَقَاتٌ لاَ يَصْلُحُ بَعْضُهَا إلاَّ بِبَعْض، وَلاَ غِنَى بِبَعْضِهَا عَنْ بَعْض- فَمِنْهَا جُنُودُ اللهِ،مِنْهَا كُتَّابُ الْعَامَّةِ وَالْخَاصَّةِ، وَمِنْهَا قُضَاةُ الْعَدْلِ، وَمِنهَا عُمَّالُ الاْنْصَافِ وَالرِّفْقِ، وَمِنْهَا أَهْلُ الْجِزْيَةِ وَالْخَراجِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الذِّمَّةِ وَمُسْلِمَةِ النَّاسِ، وَمِنْهَا التُّجَّارُ وَأَهْلُ الصِّنَاعَاتِ، وَمِنهَا الطَّبَقَةُ السُّفْلَى مِنْ ذَوِي الْحَاجَةِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ، وَكُلٌّ قَدْ سَمَّى اللهُ سَهْمَهُ، وَوَضَعَ عَلَى حَدِّهِ وَفَرِيضَتِهِ فِي كِتَابِهِ أَوْ سُنَّةِ نَبِيِّهِ (صلى الله عليه وآله)عَهْداً مِنْهُ عِنْدَنَا مَحْفُوظاً⟫

The army is, by Allah's will, the fortress of the subjects, the ornament of authority, the strength of faith, and the means of security. The subjects cannot exist without them, yet the army cannot be sustained except by the revenues Allah appoints, through which they gain strength to fight enemies, depend upon for their welfare, and meet their needs. Nor can these two classes sustain themselves without a third: judges, administrators, and scribes—those who establish contracts, gather revenues, and are entrusted with both general and particular affairs.[^cite-39]

⟪ar-quote:فَالْجُنُودُ، بِإِذْنِ اللهِ، حُصُونُ الرَّعِيَّةِ، وَزَيْنُ الْوُلاَةِ، وعِزُّ الدِّينِ، وَسُبُلُ الاْمْنِ، وَلَيْسَ تَقُومُ الرَّعِيَّةُ إِلاَّ بِهِمْ. ثُمَّ لاَ قِوَامَ لِلْجُنُودِ إِلاَّ بِمَا يُخْرِجُ اللهُ لَهُمْ مِنَ الْخَرَاجِ الَّذِي يَقْوَوْنَ بِهِ فِي جِهَادِ عَدُوِهِمْ، وَيَعْتَمِدُونَ عَلَيْهِ فِيَما أصْلَحهُمْ، وَيَكُونُ مِنْ وَرَاءِ حَاجَتِهِمْ. ثُمَّ لاَ قِوَامَ لِهذَيْنِ الصِّنْفَيْنِ إِلاَّ بِالصِّنْفِ الثَّالِثِ مِنَ الْقُضَاةِ وَالْعُمَّالِ وَالْكُتَّابِ، لِمَا يُحْكِمُونَ مِنَ الْمَعَاقِدِ، وَيَجْمَعُونَ مِنَ الْمَنَافِعِ، وَيُؤْتَمَنُونَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ خَوَاصِّ الاْمُورِ وَعَوَامِّهَا⟫

All these classes cannot exist without merchants and artisans who provide their necessities, maintain their markets, and spare them from having to do everything with their own hands. Then follows the lowest stratum of the needy and destitute, to whom the provision of support and assistance is obligatory. In Allah's wisdom, there is sufficiency for all, and each person has a right upon the ruler according to what promotes their welfare. The ruler acquits himself of the obligations Allah has placed upon him only through diligence, seeking Allah's help, training himself in steadfast adherence to truth, and enduring patiently, whether the burden be light or heavy.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ قِوَامَ لَهُمْ جَمِيعاً إِلاَّ بِالتُّجَّارِ وَذَوِي الصِّنَاعَاتِ، فِيَما يَجْتَمِعُونَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ مَرَافِقِهِمْ، وَيُقِيمُونَهُ مِنْ أَسْوَاقِهِمْ، وَيَكْفُونَهُمْ مِنَ التَّرَفُّقِ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ ممّا لاَ يَبْلُغُهُ رِفْقُ غَيْرِهِمْ. ثُمَّ الطَّبَقَةُ السُّفْلَى مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَاجَةِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ الَّذِينَ يَحِقُّ رِفْدُهُمْ وَمَعُونَتُهُمْ. وَفِي اللهِ لِكُلّ سَعَةٌ، وَلِكُلٍّ عَلَى الْوَالِي حَقٌ بِقَدْرِ مَا يُصْلِحُهُ. وَلَيْسَ يَخْرُجُ الْوَالِي مِنْ حَقِيقَةِ مَا أَلْزَمَهُ اللهُ مِنْ ذلِكَ إِلاَّ بِالاْهْتِمامِ وَالاسْتِعَانَةِ بِاللهِ، وَتَوْطِينِ نَفْسِهِ عَلَى لُزُومِ الْحَقِّ، وَالصَّبْرِ عَلَيْهِ فِيَما خَفَّ عَلَيْهِ أَوْ ثَقُلَ⟫

## The Army

Place in command of your forces a man of sincere devotion to Allah, His Messenger, and your Imam. Among them, select one whose breast is pure and whose forbearance is greatest—one slow to anger, patient with excuses, compassionate toward the weak, firm against the strong. Violence should not provoke him to fury, nor should weakness cause him to falter.[^cite-40]

⟪ar-quote:فَوَلِّ مِنْ جُنُودِكَ أَنْصَحَهُمْ فِي نَفْسِكَ لله وَلِرَسُولِهِ وَلاِمَامِكَ، وَأَنْقَاهُمْ جَيْباً، وَأَفْضَلَهُمْ حِلْماً مِمَّنْ يُبْطِىءُ عَنِ الْغَضَبِ، وَيَسْتَرِيحُ إِلَى الْعُذْرِ، وَيَرْأَفُ بِالضُّعَفَاءِ، وَيَنْبُو عَلَى الاْقْوِيَاءِ، وَمِمَّنْ لاَ يُثِيرُهُ الْعُنْفُ، وَلاَ يَقْعُدُ بِهِ الضَّعْفُ⟫

Associate with men of noble character from distinguished families and righteous houses with good traditions, then men of courage, valor, generosity, and clemency, for they are repositories of honor and wellsprings of virtue. Care for their affairs as parents care for their children. Do not regard any effort you expend to strengthen them as excessive, nor consider any kindness you show them, however small, as insignificant, for such courtesies prompt them to offer sincere counsel and foster favorable regard for you. Do not neglect their minor affairs in attending to their major ones, for they benefit from your small kindnesses and cannot do without your great ones.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ الْصَقْ بَذَوِي الْمُرُوءَاتِ وَالاْحْسَابِ، وَأَهْلِ الْبُيُوتَاتِ الصَّالِحَةِ، وَالسَّوَابِقِ الْحَسَنَةِ، ثُمَّ أَهْلِ النَّجْدَةِ وَالشَّجَاعَةِ، وَالسَّخَاءِ وَالسَّماحَةِ، فَإِنَّهُمْ جِمَاعٌ مِنَ الْكَرَمِ، وَشُعَبٌ مِنَ الْعُرْفِ. ثُمَّ تَفَقَّدْ مِنْ أُمُورِهِمْ مَا يَتَفَقَّدُهُ الْوَالِدَانِ مِنْ وَلَدِهِمَا، وَلاَ يَتَفَاقَمَنَّ فِي نَفْسِكَ شَيْءٌ قَوَّيْتَهُمْ بِهِ، وَلاَ تَحْقِرَنَّ لُطْفاً تَعَاهَدْتَهُمْ بِهِ وَإِنْ قَلَّ، فَإِنَّهُ دَاعِيَةٌ لَهُمْ إِلَى بَذْلِ النَّصِيحَةِ لَكَ، وَحُسْنِ الظَّنِّ بِكَ. وَلاَ تَدَعْ تَفَقُّدَ لَطيِفِ أُمُورِهِمُ اتِّكَالاً عَلَى جَسِيمِهَا، فَإِنَّ لِلْيَسِيرِ مِنْ لُطْفِكَ مَوْضِعاً يَنْتَفِعُونَ بِهِ، وَلِلْجَسِيمِ مَوْقِعاً لاَ يَسْتَغْنُونَ عَنْهُ.⟫

The commander whom you favor most should be one who treats them fairly with his support and benefits them from his resources, extending provisions to their families who remain behind. Thus their sole concern becomes the struggle against the enemy. Your kindness toward them will incline their hearts toward you. The most prized achievement for rulers is the establishment of justice in their lands and the emergence of their subjects' affection. Such affection manifests only when hearts are clean; sincere counsel comes only when leaders are protected; and positions must not be regarded as burdensome, nor must one anxiously await the end of a commander's tenure. Broaden your hopes for them, continue in praising them, and recount the deeds of the valiant among them, for remembrance of noble actions stirs the courageous and arouses the reluctant, if Allah wills.

⟪ar-quote:وَلْيَكُنْ آثَرُ رُؤوسِ جُنْدِكَ عِنْدَكَ مَنْ وَاسَاهُمْ فِي مَعُونَتِهِ، وَأَفْضَلَ عَلَيْهِمْ مِنْ جِدَتِهِ بِمَا يَسَعُهُمْ يَسَعُ مَنْ وَرَاءَهُمْ مِنْ خُلُوفِ أَهْلِيهِمْ حَتَّى يَكُونَ هَمُّهُمْ هَمّاً وَاحِداً فِي جِهَادِ الْعَدُوِّ، فَإِنَّ عَطْفَكَ عَلَيْهِمْ يَعْطِفُ قُلُوبَهُمْ عَلَيْكَ. وَإِنَّ أَفْضَلَ قُرَّةِ عَيْنِ الْوُلاَةِ اسْتِقَامَةُ الْعَدْلِ فِي الْالبِلاَدِ، وَظُهُورُ مَوَدَّةِ الرَّعِيَّةِ، وَإِنَّهُ لاَ تَظْهَرُ مَوَدَّتُهُمْ إِلاَّ بَسَلاَمَةِ صُدُورِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَصِحُّ نَصِيحَتُهُمْ إِلاّ بِحِيطَتِهِمْ عَلَى وُلاَةِ أُمُورِهِمْ، وَقِلَّةِ اسْتِثْقَالِ دُوَلِهِمْ، وَتَرْكِ اسْتِبْطَاءِ انْقِطَاعِ مُدَّتِهِمْ. فَافْسَحْ فِي آمَالِهِمْ، وَوَاصِلْ فِي حُسْنِ الثَّنَاءِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَتَعْدِيدِ مَا أَبْلى ذَوُالْبَلاَءِ مِنْهُمْ، فَإِنَّ كَثْرَةَ الذِّكْرِ لِحُسْنِ أَفْعَالِهِمْ تَهُزُّ الشُّجَاعَ، وَتُحَرِّضُ النَّاكِلَ، إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ⟫

Acknowledge each person's performance and do not attribute one person's achievement to another. Do not withhold reward below the level of their service. High rank should not lead you to magnify small deeds, nor low rank to minimize great ones.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ اعْرِفْ لِكُلِّ امْرِىء مِنْهُمْ مَا أَبْلى، وَلاَ تَضُمَّنَّ بَلاَءَ امْرِىء إِلَى غَيْرِهِ، وَلاَ تُقَصِّرَنَّ بِهِ دُونَ غَايَةِ بَلاَئِهِ، وَلاَ يَدْعُوَنَّكَ شَرَفُ امْرِىء إِلَى أَنْ تُعْظِمَ مِنْ بَلاَئِهِ مَا كَانَ صَغِيراً، وَلاَضَعَةُ امْرِىء إِلَى أَنْ تَسْتَصْغِرَ مِنْ يَلاَئِهِ مَاكَانَ عَظيِماً⟫

Refer to Allah and His Prophet matters that cause you anxiety and issues that seem ambiguous, for Allah the Sublime has addressed those whom He wishes to guide, saying:

> ⟪quran 4:59⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوٓا۟ أَطِيعُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ وَأَطِيعُوا۟ ٱلرَّسُولَ وَأُو۟لِى ٱلْأَمْرِ مِنكُمْ ۖ فَإِن تَنَزَعْتُمْ فِى شَىْءٍۢ فَرُدُّوهُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِ وَٱلرَّسُولِ إِن كُنتُمْ تُؤْمِنُونَ بِٱللَّهِ وَٱلْيَوْمِ ٱلْآخِرِ ۚ ذَلِكَ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَحْسَنُ تَأْوِيلًا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Obey Allah and obey the Messenger and those in authority among you. And if you dispute in anything amongst yourselves, refer it to Allah and His Messenger if you believe in Allah and in the Last Day. That is better and more suitable for final determination.*

## Justice and Oppression

The substance of justice lies in the Hereafter, wherein all things stand established in their true ranks and places, as they do in this world. In the governmental and social sphere, justice flows from piety and righteousness.[^cite-41] The ruler possesses rights over his subjects just as the subjects possess rights over the ruler. A ruler cannot be righteous unless his subjects are righteous, and conversely. When subjects fulfill the ruler's rights and the ruler fulfills theirs, truth is honored, the paths of religion prevail, and the standards of justice are firmly established.

Consider the life of Amīr al-Muʾminīn as the embodiment of these divine principles. When his caliphate was established following ʿUthmān's assassination, he was counseled to retain his predecessor's governors temporarily, deferring their removal until his government was consolidated. Though he acknowledged the worldly wisdom in this strategy, he responded: "I cannot doubt that your counsel offers worldly benefit, yet truth itself demands otherwise. How can I retain governors whose wickedness and corruption are known to me?" He immediately deposed Muʿāwiya and all other appointed officials, choosing fidelity to divine principle over political expediency.[^cite-42]

Historians may regard this as a political miscalculation, yet it reflects his absolute priority of the Hereafter over worldly comfort. Whenever worldly advantage came at the expense of religious principle, he rejected it utterly. As he himself stated, "When people abandon a portion of their faith for worldly gain, Allah opens the gates of greater tribulation upon them in this world." His refusal to retain ʿUthmān's officials—no matter how strategically advantageous—was precisely such a choice. This attitude manifests clearly throughout his letter to Malik al-Ashtar, most strikingly in his warnings against tyranny and oppression.

Such exhortations are not addressed only to naturally just rulers, but to all who believe in justice's philosophy yet harbor the potential to be drawn toward oppression. The intoxication of power can transform even the just ruler into a tyrant. The capacity for evil dwells within every human being, and when combined with worldly resources and the absence of divine support, this potential becomes actual.

At the outset of his letter, he commands Malik: "Give priority to the obedience of Allah above all else! Obey the commandments in His Book, for those who follow them prosper, while those who disobey and abandon them perish." This preamble is no mere notification—it is transformative. True obedience to Allah grants spiritual freedom by liberating the soul from its own tyranny. As the Qur'an states:

> ⟪quran 12:53⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ وَمَآ أُبَرِّئُ نَفْسِىٓ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلنَّفْسَ لَأَمَّارَةٌۢ بِٱلسُّوٓءِ إِلَّا مَا رَحِمَ رَبِّىٓ ۚ إِنَّ رَبِّى غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *"I do not exonerate myself. Indeed, the soul incites toward evil, except upon whom my Lord has mercy. Surely my Lord is Forgiving and Merciful."*

This verse clarifies the relationship between divine mercy (raḥma) and the self (nafs). Without Allah's mercy, the soul inclines irresistibly toward sin and evil. Yet through His grace, the soul is freed from the grip of desire and returns to its original nature—satisfied and peace-giving. The Qur'an describes this perfected state:

> ⟪quran 89:27-29⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎ ‏ٱرْجِعِىٓ إِلَىٰ رَبِّكِ رَاضِيَةًۭ مَّرْضِيَّةًۭ ‎ ‏فَٱدْخُلِى فِى عِبَدِى ‎⟫
> *"O soul at peace! Return to your Lord, well-pleased and well-pleasing. Enter among My servants!"*

Nature (fiṭra) is both the beginning and end of the soul, for the self is fashioned upon the divine nature, and its return is toward that same primordial state.

## Spirituality and Moral Character

In his First Sermon, Amīr al-Muʾminīn declares:

---

⟪ar-quote:وَاصْطَفى سُبْحَانَهُ مِنْ وَلَدِهِ أَنْبيَاءَ أَخَذَ عَلَى الْوَحْيِ مِيثَاقَهُم، وَعَلَى تَبْليغِ الرِّسَالَةِ أَمَانَتَهُمْ، لَمَّا بَدَّلَ أَكْثَرُ خَلْقِهِ عَهْدَ اللهِ إِلَيْهِمْ، فَجَهِلُوا حَقَّهُ، واتَّخَذُوا الاْنْدَادَ مَعَهُ، وَاجْتَالَتْهُمُ الشَّيَاطِينُ عَنْ مَعْرفَتِهِ، وَاقتَطَعَتْهُمْ عَنْ عِبَادَتِهِ، فَبَعَثَ فِيهمْ رُسُلَهُ، وَوَاتَرَ إِلَيْهِمْ أَنْبِياءَهُ،**لِيَسْتَأْدُوهُمْ مِيثَاقَ فِطْرَتِهِ**، وَيُذَكِّرُوهُمْ مَنْسِيَّ نِعْمَتِهِ، وَيَحْتَجُّوا عَلَيْهِمْ بَالتَّبْلِيغِ، **وَيُثِيرُوا لَهُمْ دَفَائِنَ الْعُقُولِ**، وَيُرُوهُمْ آيَاتِ الْمَقْدِرَةِ⟫

Allah selected prophets from His creation and took their pledge for revelation and their trust in bearing His Message. When most of His creatures perverted Allah's covenant with them, forgot His rights, took associates with Him, and Satan turned them away from knowing Him and separated them from His worship, Allah sent His Messengers and followed them with His prophets to call them back to the covenant of His creation (fiṭra), to remind them of His forgotten bounties, to argue with them through preaching, to **awaken in them the buried treasures of reason**, and to show them the signs of His power.

---

These buried treasures are the universal knowledge planted in every soul on the eternal day of covenant (yawm al-mīthāq), constituting the primordial nature (fiṭra) and innate disposition toward all goodness. The Prophet (upon him be peace) therefore taught, "The noblest deed should be your most cherished treasure, for it is not merely the root of all virtuous acts but the very essence of all creation."[^cite-43] In one place, he praises Allah:

> By Thy majesty that fills all existence, by Thy names that are the foundation of all being, by Thy knowledge that encompasses all things, by the light of Thy face by which all things are illuminated.

From this perspective, every good moral quality (akhlāq ḥasan) in this world reflects one of the divine attributes (ṣifāt ilāhiyya)—each corresponding to one of Allah's Most Beautiful Names (al-asmāʾ al-ḥusnā). Through moral excellence, monotheism is established such that cultivating virtue attracts the divine substance itself, while that same divine substance becomes the very essence of goodness. Thus each virtuous quality relates ultimately to itself and to the expression of divine oneness (tawḥī


<!-- section 13 (id=3596, raw_sort=13): کبر اور غرور سے بچنے کی نصیحت -->

## Warning Against Pride and Arrogance

He warns the owner of wickedness: "Do not prepare your soul for war with Allah!" What actions constitute such a war against the Divine? Upon careful examination, one discovers that this passage addresses attitudes whose outward manifestations may appear evil, yet whose inner dimensions contradict the spirit of those very actions. Arrogance (kibr) exemplifies this inward opposition perfectly, and Maulana ʿAli has cautioned against it in numerous places throughout his teachings. When a ruler succumbs to arrogance, he usurps one of the supreme attributes belonging to Allah alone. He claims entitlement to a station worthy only of the Divine, for ⟪ar:'المتکبر'⟫ (al-Mutakabbir, the Mighty One) is a name that belongs to Him alone. To boast before the people and display one's greatness outwardly amounts to inward rebellion against Allah and denial of His ⟪ar:أحدیت⟫ (aḥadiyyah, unity and uniqueness). This concealed denial—when viewed through the lens of spiritual realities—constitutes waging war against Allah. Enmity toward ⟪ar:الحق⟫ (al-Ḥaqq, the Truth) becomes the hidden substance that an arrogant ruler displays to his subjects in every form of haughtiness, conceit, and oppression.[^cite-33] The ruler's delusion of superiority over those beneath him is, in essence, a declaration of rebellion against the One above him. Thus the oppressor not only brings upon himself the just wrath of the Creator through his oppression of creatures, but actively opposes the Creator through his own deeds. The root of this worldly evil is a spiritual defect arising from denial of the Lord's ⟪ar:أحدیت⟫ (who possesses absolute power and authority), His ⟪ar:حقانیت⟫ (ḥaqq-āniyyah, truthfulness and justice), and from heedlessness of the Qur'anic verse:

> ⟪quran 40:16⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَوْمَ هُم بَرِزُونَۖ لَا يَخْفَىٰ عَلَى ٱللَّهِ مِنْهُمْ شَىْءٌۭۚ لِّمَنِ ٱلْمُلْكُ ٱلْيَوْمَۖ لِلَّهِ ٱلْوَحِدِ ٱلْقَهَّارِ ‎⟫
> *The Day when they will (all) come out, nothing of them will be hidden from Allah. Whose is the kingdom this Day? (Allah Himself will reply to His Question): It is Allah's the One, the Irresistible!*

This verse—designated as ⟪ar:'الیوم'⟫ (al-yawm, the Day)—refers not solely to the eschatological Day of Judgment, but to each and every day. In his celebrated sermon known as ⟪ar:'القاصیۃ'⟫ (al-Qāṣiyyah), Maulana ʿAli describes the humiliation of the arrogant Iblis, observing that he was the first to confront Allah in the arena of pride, and thus became the fountainhead and origin of all arrogance that followed. When Allah commanded him to prostrate before Adam, Iblis flatly refused. Filled with overwhelming pride, he deemed himself superior to Adam, declaring: "I am created of fire, and man is created of clay." Because of this arrogance, Iblis not only became the first enemy of Allah, but also assumed the role of ⟪ar:أمام المتعصبین و صلف المستکبرین⟫ (imām al-mutaʿasṣibīn wa-ṣilf al-mustakbirīn, leader of the fanatical and the arrogant) among all proud ones who came after him.[^cite-34] Beware the sickness wrought by his insinuations, his whispers and deceits! Always clothe yourself in the garment of humility! Trample self-praise beneath your feet! Cast off the chains of pride from your neck, and fortify yourselves in the secure fortress of humble submission.

This demonstrates that humility (tawāḍuʿ) stands as the supreme weapon against the devil, for his true purpose is to cultivate arrogance within the human heart. Pride is not merely a vice in itself; it acts as a lethal poison to every ⟪ar:خصال محمودۃ⟫ (khiṣāl maḥmūdah, praiseworthy quality), transforming what is good into evil. Thus it is said: "A sin that brings you grief is better than a good deed that fills you with pride." Moments of praise and self-exaltation present Satan's finest opportunities for assault upon the soul.

*Verses referenced in this section (curated linkage from KASHKOLE. TopicAyats—7 of 7 not already cited above):*

> ⟪quran 7:181⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمِمَّنْ خَلَقْنَآ أُمَّةٌۭ يَهْدُونَ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَبِهِۦ يَعْدِلُونَ ‎⟫
> *And of those whom We have created, there is a community who guides (others) with the truth, and establishes justice therewith.*

> ⟪quran 7:182⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا۟ بِـَٔايَتِنَا سَنَسْتَدْرِجُهُم مِّنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *Those who reject Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.), We shall gradually seize them with punishment in ways they perceive not.*

> ⟪quran 9:85⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تُعْجِبْكَ أَمْوَلُهُمْ وَأَوْلَدُهُمْ ۚ إِنَّمَا يُرِيدُ ٱللَّهُ أَن يُعَذِّبَهُم بِهَا فِى ٱلدُّنْيَا وَتَزْهَقَ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَهُمْ كَفِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *And let not their wealth or their children amaze you. Allah's Plan is to punish them with these things in this world, and that their souls shall depart (die) while they are disbelievers.*

> ⟪quran 17:81⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَقُلْ جَآءَ ٱلْحَقُّ وَزَهَقَ ٱلْبَطِلُ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلْبَطِلَ كَانَ زَهُوقًۭا ‎⟫
> *And say: "Truth (i.e. Islamic Monotheism or this Quran or Jihad against polytheists) has come and Batil (falsehood, i.e. Satan or polytheism, etc.) has vanished. Surely! Batil is ever bound to vanish."*

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*

> ⟪quran 55:26⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎⟫
> *Whatsoever is on it (the earth) will perish.*

> ⟪quran 55:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫
> *And the Face of your Lord full of Majesty and Honour will abide forever.*

<!-- section 14 (id=3601, raw_sort=14): شرک خفی -->

## Hidden Shirk

Although the outward meaning of shirk (association with Allah) denotes the worship of idols, there exists another dimension: the worship of false gods concealed within the self, manifesting as intentions, attitudes, inclinations, pride, display, boasting, and deception. To this the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) alluded when he said, "Shirk is hidden within my Community like the crawling of a black ant upon a black stone in a black night."[^cite-35] Similarly, he declared: "Know that even the slightest trace of hypocrisy constitutes shirk." For to act in pursuit of others' praise rather than for Allah's sake is to associate partners with Allah in one's intention. Whoever acts for other than Allah, Allah entrusts that servant to those others.

Due to the corruption of Iblis's inner arrogance, he committed the sin of outward disobedience, and this disobedience sealed his fate of degradation. Iblis was humiliated because of his rebellion against Allah, and he rebelled out of arrogance. This reveals that pride itself is ignominy, a seed of destruction bearing bitter fruit. Observe how Allah abased him! To be arrogant is in truth to be debased, and self-aggrandizement is verily self-abasement. This is why Maulana ʿAli counseled Malik al-Ashtar: "Do not declare, 'I hold authority; I command and am obeyed.'" For such a notion creates discord in the heart and corrodes religion itself. From this admonition one comprehends also that for the outward form of religion to remain sound, the inner intentions and conceptions must be purified. Therefore he urged that when power ascends to the head, faith descends from the heart; and to preserve faith in this world, it must emerge from the heart and manifest as humility—another manifestation of keeping all things in their rightful station (ʿadl).

He then counseled Malik al-Ashtar further: "When your position incites you to arrogance and vainglory, then contemplate the greatness of Allah above whom you stand." This meditation will help you overcome your base desires and restore your intellect by sheltering you from the rigidity of the self. The relationship between intellect (ʿaql) and humility deserves reflection here. That faculty of intellect which becomes distracted by arrogance and pretense is precisely the faculty that comprehends the reality of Allah and perceives the branches flowing from that reality. In Arabic, arrogance is termed ⟪ar:'مَخِلا'⟫ (mikhallā), which derives from the root *khayāl* (imagination, deception). Thus pride is an "imagining" deeply connected to the illusory, deceptive dimension of the world. Arrogance is a severe form of suspicion arising from disorder of the intellect, perceived as evil and recognized as corruption. It concerns not merely thinking oneself great, but also ⟪ar:الحق⟫ (belittling the Truth) and denigrating others. Only a ⟪ar:ولی اللہ⟫ (walī Allāh, friend of Allah) can truly grasp the reality contained in the following verses and extract from them that humility which erases ⟪ar:'أنائیت'⟫ (anāʾiyyah, self-assertion and egoism)—the very root from which all arrogance, ostentation, and pride spring forth, and which feeds every form of oppression:

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*

> ⟪quran 55:26-27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎ ‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫
> *Whatsoever is on it (the earth) will perish. And the Face of your Lord full of Majesty and Honour will abide forever.*

> ⟪quran 17:81⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَقُلْ جَآءَ ٱلْحَقُّ وَزَهَقَ ٱلْبَطِلُ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلْبَطِلَ كَانَ زَهُوقًۭا ‎⟫
> *And say: "Truth (i.e. Islamic Monotheism or this Quran or Jihad against polytheists) has come and Batil (falsehood, i.e. Satan or polytheism, etc.) has vanished. Surely! Batil is ever bound to vanish."*

With this understanding, one now perceives the force of his declaration: "Beware of imitating Allah and confronting Him, for Allah despises every wrongdoer and humiliates every arrogant one." Whoever denies Allah and His creation their due, shall discover on the Day of Resurrection that not only Allah's creation but Allah Himself stands as his adversary. Man remains in a state of war with Allah until he abandons his oppression and turns in repentance before the Divine. Even should he escape in this world, no escape awaits him in the Hereafter.

The longer the oppressor continues in his injustice, the more his soul blackens, the deeper it becomes soaked in torment. The Qur'an presents this reality through the concept of ⟪ar:'استدراج'⟫ (istidraj, gradual seduction and punishment), which describes the degrees of chastisement. This verse illuminates not only the stages of punishment but clarifies the distinction between those who uphold the Truth through justice and those who perpetrate wrong:

> ⟪quran 7:181-182⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمِمَّنْ خَلَقْنَآ أُمَّةٌۭ يَهْدُونَ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَبِهِۦ يَعْدِلُونَ ‎ ‏وَٱلَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا۟ بِـَٔايَتِنَا سَنَسْتَدْرِجُهُم مِّنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *And of those whom We have created, there is a community who guides (others) with the truth, and establishes justice therewith. Those who reject Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.), We shall gradually seize them with punishment in ways they perceive not.*

Such punishment is not confined to poverty, sickness, and suffering, but may manifest even through worldly success, wealth, and children—as Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 9:85⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تُعْجِبْكَ أَمْوَلُهُمْ وَأَوْلَدُهُمْ ۚ إِنَّمَا يُرِيدُ ٱللَّهُ أَن يُعَذِّبَهُم بِهَا فِى ٱلدُّنْيَا وَتَزْهَقَ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَهُمْ كَفِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *And let not their wealth or their children amaze you. Allah's Plan is to punish them with these things in this world, and that their souls shall depart (die) while they are disbelievers.*

The wrongdoer can simultaneously be called a ⟪ar:'مسلمان'⟫ (Musalmān, Muslim by outer profession) and a ⟪ar:'کافر'⟫ (kāfir, denier and concealer of truth), for through his denial—meaning his concealment of truth from himself and from others in his deeds—he hides all goodness flowing from it.[^cite-36]

<!-- section 15 (id=3597, raw_sort=15): اخلاقی و روحانی ضمیر -->

## Moral and Spiritual Conscience

Another form of waging war against Allah is rebellion against the voice of conscience within oneself. The soul that recognizes and understands its moral obligations speaks to itself as the voice of the inner conscience (ḍamīr). The conscience is, in essence, the voice of an awakened and aware soul.

> ⟪quran 91:7-8⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَنَفْسٍۢ وَمَا سَوَّىٰهَا ‎ ‏فَأَلْهَمَهَا فُجُورَهَا وَتَقْوَىٰهَا ‎⟫
> *And by Nafs (Adam or a person or a soul, etc.), and Him Who perfected him in proportion; Then He showed him what is wrong for him and what is right for him;*

This verse instructs us that the soul (nafs) that corrects and guides toward the right path is itself the "conscience," upon which both righteous and base arguments exert their force. A morally awakened soul will be inspired toward goodness, while a soul debased through negligence will be moved toward evil. Allah Almighty has implanted within every soul, in the midst of the conscience, that capacity indicated by the verse above. For this reason, every soul not only distinguishes between good and evil, but also recognizes instinctively its own ⟪ar:'عبدیت'⟫ (ʿabdiyyah, servitude and dependence) and Allah's ⟪ar:'الہیت'⟫ (ilāhiyyah, divinity and lordship). The Qur'an commemorates the moment when Allah created humanity and took from them a covenant concerning His lordship:

> ⟪quran 7:172⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِۢ بَنِىٓ آدَمَ مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّتَهُمْ وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ۖ قَالُوا۟ بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ ۛ أَن تَقُولُوا۟ يَوْمَ ٱلْقِيَمَةِ إِنَّا كُنَّا عَنْ هَذَا غَفِلِينَ ‎⟫
> *And (remember) when your Lord brought forth from the Children of Adam, from their loins, their seed (or from Adam's loin his offspring) and made them testify as to themselves (saying): "Am I not your Lord?" They said: "Yes! We testify," lest you should say on the Day of Resurrection: "Verily, we have been unaware of this."*

This demonstrates that the wrongdoer is one who breaks his covenant with Allah and enthrones ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫ (nafs al-ammārah bi-al-suʾ, the soul that commands toward evil) as his lord in place of belief in Allah as true Lord. For this reason, ʿAli (upon whom be peace) advised Malik al-Ashtar: "Do not say, 'I command, and obey me,'—for this is the path of ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫ (the commanding soul), whose dominance extends over body, emotion, imagination, intellect, intention, passion, and consciousness alike."[^cite-37] The path to justice toward oneself lies in ⟪ar:مجاہدۃ النفس⟫ (mujāhadat al-nafs, struggle against the lower self)—first removing one's own defects. Thus he said: "If you desire to reform others, you must first reform yourself, for to attempt the improvement of others' souls while evil resides within yourself is the greatest transgression."

Before Malik al-Ashtar, ⟪ar:محمد بن ابی بکر⟫ (Muḥammad ibn Abī Bakr) had been appointed by him as ruler of Egypt. To him too he gave counsel: "I have appointed you as guardian over the people of Egypt. It is thereby incumbent upon you to wage war upon your lower self and to safeguard your religion!" This utterance of his is remarkable. He granted authority to Muḥammad ibn Abī Bakr and imposed two obligations upon him: first, to master the self and its desires; second, to protect religion itself. The greater the power and authority one possesses, the more stringent becomes the responsibility to govern the self and restrain its impulses. For should the soul become enslaved to desire and use its wielded power to gratify those desires, man destroys not only himself but religion as well. The outward practice of a Muslim's faith depends entirely upon the inner integrity of the soul for its very survival. This too represents another manner of maintaining all things in their rightful place. When power ascends to one, the Qur'an describes the soul that generates arrogance and awakens the desire for dominance and sovereignty in these terms:

> ⟪quran 96:6-7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كَلَّآ إِنَّ ٱلْإِنسَنَ لَيَطْغَىٰٓ ‎ ‏أَن رَّآهُ ٱسْتَغْنَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Nay! Verily, man does transgress all bounds (in disbelief and evil deed, etc.). Because he considers himself self-sufficient.*

The more a soul is deceived by its apparent self-sufficiency and withdraws from reliance upon Allah, the more it will imagine itself divine—a delusion that constitutes its gravest injustice. Such a soul becomes the very person of whom Allah speaks:

> ⟪quran 45:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ وَأَضَلَّهُ ٱللَّهُ عَلَىٰ عِلْمٍۢ وَخَتَمَ عَلَىٰ سَمْعِهِۦ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَجَعَلَ عَلَىٰ بَصَرِهِۦ غِشَوَةًۭ فَمَن يَهْدِيهِ مِنۢ بَعْدِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أَفَلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Have you seen him who takes his own lust (vain desires) as his ilah (god), and Allah knowing (him as such), left him astray, and sealed his hearing and his heart, and put a cover on his sight. Who then will guide him after Allah? Will you not then remember?*

Conversely, the more a person acquires knowledge of his own ⟪ar:نقص⟫ (naqṣ, deficiency and wretchedness) and recognizes his profound neediness before Allah, the more loosens the stranglehold of ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫ around his neck. For only the soul that commands others toward evil can command itself toward evil; whereas the soul humbled before Allah naturally treats its fellows with gentleness, mercy, and justice.

He declared: "In your estimation, your deeds should be the most contemptible, the most unjust, and most unacceptable to people, because the reproach of the people diminishes the approval of the people." Note how he has insisted upon the approval of "ordinary human beings"! The one who abases himself in the sight of Allah will walk among the common folk, whereas the proud seeks only the company of the arrogant. Thus one truly comprehends the verse:

> ⟪quran 35:15⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلنَّاسُ أَنتُمُ ٱلْفُقَرَآءُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِۖ وَٱللَّهُ هُوَ ٱلْغَنِىُّ ٱلْحَمِيدُ ‎⟫
> *O mankind! it is you who stand in need of Allah, but Allah is Rich (Free of all wants and needs), Worthy of all praise.*

In this regard, the life of Amīr al-Muʾminīn, Master of the Believers, stands as an argument. Once, when ⟪ar:آثم بن زیاد⟫ (relatives of a dervish) complained to him that he lived in unnecessary poverty, he summoned them and exhorted them to care for their families and not reject the gifts Allah had bestowed. They replied: "O Alī! You speak thus to us, yet you yourself are wrapped in a rough woolen cloak and eat dry bread?" He answered: "Woe to you! I am not like you! Allah has made it obligatory upon ⟪ar:ائمۃ الحق⟫ (the Imāms of Truth) to live their worldly lives at the level of the poorest among their people, so that they might experience the poverty of the poor and not fall prey to greed and avarice."

This account reveals that it is imperative for a ruler to conduct his worldly affairs at the standard of the poorest of his subjects. He chose for himself the least he could obtain. This stemmed from his profound connection with ⟪ar:'الحق'⟫ (al-Ḥaqq, the Truth), in the light of which every material possession in the world became despicable, contemptible, and worthless in his sight.[^cite-38]

<!-- section 16 (id=3587, raw_sort=16): عدل اور ہمدردی -->

## Justice and Compassion

Feeling the sufferings of the poor awakens in a person the consciousness of his dependence upon his Lord, which permits him to walk through life between hope and fear, held in the mercy of Allah. Living such a life, human nature (Fiṭrah) treats his fellows with sympathy and tenderness. The capacity for empathy stands in no contradiction to the requirements of justice; rather, it constitutes an essential dimension of justice, for it not only maintains all things in their rightful station but accords with the nature of the universe itself—indeed, it is one of the supreme attributes of Truth. For this reason, Allah has begun each surah of the Qur'an with *Bismillāh al-raḥmān al-raḥīm* (In the name of Allah, the Merciful, the Compassionate), therein mentioning His mercy and forbearance. We observe the same comportment in the lives of the Prophet (upon him be peace and blessings) and Amīr al-Muʾminīn that they perpetually treated the people of Allah with mercy. They did so not from personal sentiment, but as a duty demanded by Allah, as He declared:

> ⟪quran 7:156⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ وَٱكْتُبْ لَنَا فِى هَذِهِ ٱلدُّنْيَا حَسَنَةًۭ وَفِى ٱلْآخِرَةِ إِنَّا هُدْنَآ إِلَيْكَ ۚ قَالَ عَذَابِىٓ أُصِيبُ بِهِۦ مَنْ أَشَآءُ ۖ وَرَحْمَتِى وَسِعَتْ كُلَّ شَىْءٍۢ ۚ فَسَأَكْتُبُهَا لِلَّذِينَ يَتَّقُونَ وَيُؤْتُونَ ٱلزَّكَوٰةَ وَٱلَّذِينَ هُم بِـَٔايَتِنَا يُؤْمِنُونَ ‎⟫
> *And ordain for us good in this world, and in the Hereafter. Certainly we have turned unto You." He said: (As to) My Punishment I afflict therewith whom I will and My Mercy embraces all things. That (Mercy) I shall ordain for those who are the Muttaqun (pious - see V.2:2), and give Zakat; and those who believe in Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs and revelations, etc.);*

> ⟪quran 6:54⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذَا جَآءَكَ ٱلَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِـَٔايَتِنَا فَقُلْ سَلَمٌ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَىٰ نَفْسِهِ ٱلرَّحْمَةَ ۖ أَنَّهُۥ مَنْ عَمِلَ مِنكُمْ سُوٓءًۢا بِجَهَلَةٍۢ ثُمَّ تَابَ مِنۢ بَعْدِهِۦ وَأَصْلَحَ فَأَنَّهُۥ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *When those who believe in Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.) come to you, say: "Salamun 'Alaikum" (peace be on you); your Lord has written Mercy for Himself, so that, if any of you does evil in ignorance, and thereafter repents and does righteous good deeds (by obeying Allah), then surely, He is Oft­Forgiving, Most Merciful.*

Similarly, we find in the sayings of Maulana ʿAli abundant passages concerning mercy. He declared: "Mercy brings down upon you the mercy of Allah, and you shall receive mercy as you extend mercy to others. I am astonished at one who expects mercy from above yet shows no mercy to those beneath him."

According to this principle, the more a person embodies compassion in his spiritual thoughts and moral conduct toward others, the closer he draws to the Almighty. In society, justice demands that compassion be extended wherever possible. Of course, at times when no other recourse remains, severe punishment may be necessary. For this reason, in his letter to Malik al-Ashtar, ʿAli instructed him to punish those officials found guilty of misappropriating wealth, so that divine justice might be vindicated. In another epistle to his cousin, whom he appointed as governor of Basra, he wrote with solemn oath: "I swear by Allah in complete sincerity that if word reaches me that you have usurped even the least or the greatest portion of Muslim wealth, I shall inflict upon you a punishment that will diminish your substance, fracture your spine, and obliterate your reputation!"[^cite-39]

Likewise, whenever anyone petitioned him for a favor, he would respond with rigor, even if they were his own kinfolk. Once his brother Aqīl requested additional funds from the public treasury; ʿAli placed a burning iron rod upon his hand. As Aqīl cried out in agony, he said: "Brother Aqīl, if you cannot endure this small fire, how shall I bear the blazing fire of Allah's Hell to which you are inviting me?" Similarly, when he learned that his cousin ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿAbbās had misappropriated Muslim wealth, he declared to him: "Fear Allah and return to the people what belongs to them. If you do not, and Allah grants me power over you, I shall strike you with my sword such that the jinn will recognize it. By Allah, even if al-Ḥasan and al-Ḥusayn were to do the same, they would receive no concession from me!"

This demonstrates that regardless of one's rank or station, all remain equal before justice. This conduct of his differed markedly from that of earlier caliphs, who distributed governorships among their relatives and plundered Muslim resources. As ʿAli observed, the spring camel feeds on soft buds. Allah declares in the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 4:135⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ كُونُوا۟ قَوَّمِينَ بِٱلْقِسْطِ شُهَدَآءَ لِلَّهِ وَلَوْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِكُمْ أَوِ ٱلْوَلِدَيْنِ وَٱلْأَقْرَبِينَ ۚ إِن يَكُنْ غَنِيًّا أَوْ فَقِيرًۭا فَٱللَّهُ أَوْلَىٰ بِهِمَا ۖ فَلَا تَتَّبِعُوا۟ ٱلْهَوَىٰٓ أَن تَعْدِلُوا۟ ۚ وَإِن تَلْوُۥٓا۟ أَوْ تُعْرِضُوا۟ فَإِنَّ ٱللَّهُ كَانَ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ خَبِيرًۭا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Stand out firmly for justice, as witnesses to Allah, even though it be against yourselves, or your parents, or your kin, be he rich or poor, Allah is a Better Protector to both (than you). So follow not the lusts (of your hearts), lest you may avoid justice, and if you distort your witness or refuse to give it, verily, Allah is Ever Well­Acquainted with what you do.*

The following passage from his letter merits particular attention, wherein he has elevated compassion into a universal context by establishing all humanity upon equal footing. Within this statement lies a remedy for all manner of prejudice and sectarian division. He writes:

⟪ar-quote:وَأَشْعِرْ قَلْبَكَ الرَّحْمَةَ لِلرَّعِيَّةِ، وَالْـمَحَبَّةَ لَهُمْ، وَاللُّطْفَ بِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَكُونَنَّ عَلَيْهِمْ سَبُعاً ضَارِياً تَغْتَنِمُ أَكْلَهُمْ، فَإِنَّهُمْ صِنْفَانِ- إِمّا أَخٌ لَكَ فِي الدِّينِ، وَإمّا نَظِيرٌ لَكَ فِي الْخَلْقِ، يَفْرُطُ مِنْهُمُ الزَّلَلُ، وَتَعْرِضُ لَهُمُ الْعِلَلُ، يُؤْتَى عَلَى أَيْدِيهِمْ فِي الَعَمْدِ وَالْخَطَاَ، فَأَعْطِهِمْ مِنْ عَفْوِكَ وَصَفْحِكَ مِثْلَ الَّذِي تُحِبُّ أَنْ يُعْطِيَكَ اللهُ مِنْ عَفْوِهِ وَصَفْحِهِ، فَإِنَّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ، وَ وَالِي الاْمْرِ عَلَيْكَ فَوْقَكَ، وَاللهُ فَوْقَ مَنْ وَلاَّكَ! وَقَدِ اسْتَكْفَاكَ أَمْرَهُمْ، وَابْتَلاَكَ بِهِمْ⟫

"Habituate your heart to mercy for the subjects, to affection and kindness toward them. Never be toward them as a ravening beast seeking to devour them, for they are of two kinds: either your brother in religion or one like you in creation. They will slip and falter; illnesses will befall them. Acts may issue from their hands, whether intentional or through error. Extend to them your forgiveness and forbearance as you would desire Allah to extend His forgiveness and forbearance to you. Know that you stand above them; the Commander of the Believers stands above you; and Allah stands above him whom He has appointed. He has entrusted you with their affairs and tested you through them."

By mentioning Allah's mercy, you have drawn attention to the Divine compassion that encompasses all humankind. Every person—no matter how great a ruler or king—is a slave of Allah and dwells in complete dependence upon His mercy. Therefore, if a person perceives that he rules over another human being, he must remember that he himself lies submissive before Allah. This consciousness will render him kind and sympathetic toward those beneath him and will draw Allah's mercy toward him. He reminded Malik al-Ashtar that although he holds authority, he remains a human being like all others.

Once Maulana ʿAli observed a blind mendicant asking alms but receiving nothing. He was informed the man was Christian. ʿAli responded: "You have taken so much from him that he has grown old and infirm, and now you refuse him sustenance?" From that day forward, he should be provided for from the public treasury. His action teaches that both Muslims and non-Muslims stand equal in matters of justice. Social justice and religious equality flow from mercy; therefore, mercy becomes an imperative duty upon the believers.

He reminded Malik al-Ashtar that his rule is not an honor from Allah but a trial and test, revealing what he himself believed about authority during his caliphate. He declared in a sermon: "Had Allah not made binding upon scholars the duty to forbid injustice and support the oppressed, I would have cast aside the reins of this caliphate, and you would see that this world is to me no more valuable than the nasal discharge of a goat!" Here one discerns a resemblance to Platonic thought: a true philosopher rules solely for the welfare of the people, viewing authority not as honor but as an inescapable duty whose sole aim is the establishment of justice. For the founding and restoration of any society rests upon this single attribute alone.

From his teachings we learn that governance operates under the principle of the welfare of the downtrodden. When Allah has granted one of His servants knowledge and consciousness of justice, his obligation increases proportionately. The more abundant God's grace upon a person, the greater his duty to show favor to creation. In one of his sermons he proclaims: "Allah's grace does not increase for His servant until His right becomes weighty in his eyes."

<!-- section 17 (id=3588, raw_sort=17): اللہ کے بارے میں خوش گمانی -->

## Good Opinion of Allah

We now turn to that section of Amīr al-Muʾminīn's letter in which he advises Malik al-Ashtar regarding the appointment of ministers and counselors. He cautioned against miserliness and cowardice, declaring: "Surely, stinginess, cowardice, and greed all arise from distrust of Allah (suʾ al-ẓann bi-Allāh)." This misconception springs from failure to grasp the Divine Fitrah (human nature), and ignorance of Fitrah flows from inadequate knowledge of Allah's attributes. From this perspective, all human corruption traces to deterioration of the intellect caused by weakness of faith. Conversely, robust faith generates proper trust in Allah, a keen intellect, and profound comprehension of the Divine Reality. This comprehension illuminates the divine attributes within the soul. One should not imagine that, because these attributes belong to Allah, one ought not to aspire toward them. Rather, one should take these qualities as exemplar and guide for one's own life, and labor to remove the defects of the soul. This does not signify rivalry with the Divine Greatness, but rather the goal of approximating the Divine character. Such spiritual development is achieved through the worship of Allah. In other words, one should be generous because Allah is Generous; merciful because Allah is Merciful and Compassionate. Yet simultaneously, one must establish within oneself humility and devotion, and hold firm the conviction that one can never cultivate within oneself any quality worthy of standing equal to the Divine attributes!

All of Allah's attributes speak to man's complete dependence and neediness before Allah, and to the Oneness and Undivided Nature of the Divine. In this manner, a relationship obtains between Allah and His servant—positive in aspect and negating in aspect. Positive, as Maulana ʿAli expressed when he said that whoever fails to show mercy to another, Allah withholds mercy from him. And negating, as Allah declared:

> ⟪quran 35:15⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلنَّاسُ أَنتُمُ ٱلْفُقَرَآءُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِۖ وَٱللَّهُ هُوَ ٱلْغَنِىُّ ٱلْحَمِيدُ ‎⟫
> *O mankind! it is you who stand in need of Allah, but Allah is Rich (Free of all wants and needs), Worthy of all praise.*

Thus between these two poles there is synthesis: man's virtues and noble qualities are reflections of Allah's divine attributes, while his consciousness that he stands in utter non-existence before the Divine Majesty remains unshaken. He is simultaneously the representative (khalīfah) of Allah and His slave (ʿabd Allāh). His servitude confines him within the limits of slavery lest he transgress and become an associate in the glory of Allah, while his representation reminds him that consciousness of servitude to Allah must not permit him to forget his obligation toward Allah's creation—an obligation the Divine has enjoined upon him. This equilibrium between representation and slavery, between Allah and His servants, exemplifies once more the principle of maintaining all things in their rightful station, and it creates harmony between moral practice and the purification of the soul.[^cite-40]

<!-- section 18 (id=3590, raw_sort=18): شہر اور معاشرا -->

## City and Society

In this section of his letter, ʿAli enumerates the various classes of society—the military, the administrators and scribes, the judiciary, the officials, the tax collectors, the peasants, the merchants, the artisans, and the destitute—and delineates their responsibilities and rights. The guidance he offers concerning them may be understood as justice made manifest and operative. The ruler must fulfill the rights of all people belonging to these classes, recognizing that to do so is to act in accordance with one's duty toward Allah. This is because Allah has established all these classes, determined their stations and livelihoods, set the boundaries of their roles, and taken from them a covenant to abide by the Qur'an and Sunnah.

The ruler's obligation toward society constitutes an aspect of his covenant with Allah, as he declared:

> ⟪quran 13:19-20⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ أَفَمَن يَعْلَمُ أَنَّمَآ أُنزِلَ إِلَيْكَ مِن رَّبِّكَ ٱلْحَقُّ كَمَنْ هُوَ أَعْمَىٰٓ ۚ إِنَّمَا يَتَذَكَّرُ أُو۟لُوا۟ ٱلْأَلْبَبِ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ يُوفُونَ بِعَهْدِ ٱللَّهِ وَلَا يَنقُضُونَ ٱلْمِيثَقَ ‎⟫
> *Shall he then who knows that what has been revealed unto you (O Muhammad PBUH) from your Lord is the truth be like him who is blind? But it is only the men of understanding that pay heed. Those who fulfill the Covenant of Allah and break not the Mîthaq (bond, treaty, covenant);*

And again:

> ⟪quran 17:34⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَقْرَبُوا۟ مَالَ ٱلْيَتِيمِ إِلَّا بِٱلَّتِى هِىَ أَحْسَنُ حَتَّىٰ يَبْلُغَ أَشُدَّهُۥ ۚ وَأَوْفُوا۟ بِٱلْعَهْدِ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلْعَهْدَ كَانَ مَسْـُٔولًۭا ‎⟫
> *And come not near to the orphan's property except to improve it, until he attains the age of full strength. And fulfil (every) covenant. Verily! the covenant, will be questioned about.*

Following this, he advises the ruler to seek the companionship of scholars and wise persons who may bring prosperity to his governance and extend blessing throughout his realm, surpassing even the accomplishments of his predecessors. He then addresses each class individually, designating the ruler as the center around which all circles revolve. The center, he observes, is none other than the link that binds the circle and, through it, the entire society to Allah.

Regarding the military, he speaks first, describing them as a fortress for the people. For the selection of the military commander, he prescribes: "Choose one who is most sincere to Allah, His Messenger, and the Imam of the Age—whose heart is pure and unblemished, who is forbearing, slow to anger, quick to forgive, gentle with the weak, and firm with the strong, one who does not lose his resolve in intensity nor who is stalled by weakness." Examined closely, all these qualities shine prominently in the personality and character of the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him). His emphasis upon compassion, gentleness, and forbearance deserves note, for these are virtues not commonly associated with warfare, where fierceness and the readiness to die are prized. Yet what is needed is a courage that is fierce only toward enemies while displaying mercy toward one's own people, as the Qur'an attests:

> ⟪quran 48:29⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مُّحَمَّدٌۭ رَّسُولُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ وَٱلَّذِينَ مَعَهُۥٓ أَشِدَّآءُ عَلَى ٱلْكُفَّارِ رُحَمَآءُ بَيْنَهُمْ ۖ تَرَىٰهُمْ رُكَّعًۭا سُجَّدًۭا يَبْتَغُونَ فَضْلًۭا مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ وَرِضْوَنًۭا ۖ سِيمَاهُمْ فِى وُجُوهِهِم مِّنْ أَثَرِ ٱلسُّجُودِ ۚ ذَلِكَ مَثَلُهُمْ فِى ٱلتَّوْرَىٰةِ ۚ وَمَثَلُهُمْ فِى ٱلْإِنجِيلِ كَزَرْعٍ أَخْرَجَ شَطْـَٔهُۥ فَـَٔازَرَهُۥ فَٱسْتَغْلَظَ فَٱسْتَوَىٰ عَلَىٰ سُوقِهِۦ يُعْجِبُ ٱلزُّرَّاعَ لِيَغِيظَ بِهِمُ ٱلْكُفَّارَ ۗ وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ مِنْهُم مَّغْفِرَةًۭ وَأَجْرًا عَظِيمًۢا ‎⟫
> *Muhammad (PBUH) is the Messenger of Allah, and those who are with him are severe against disbelievers, and merciful among themselves. You see them bowing and falling down prostrate (in prayer), seeking Bounty from Allah and (His) Good Pleasure. The mark of them (i.e. of their Faith) is on their faces (foreheads) from the traces of (their) prostration (during prayers). This is their description in the Taurat (Torah). But their description in the Injeel (Gospel) is like a (sown) seed which sends forth its shoot, then makes it strong, it then becomes thick, and it stands straight on its stem, delighting the sowers that He may enrage the disbelievers with them. Allah has promised those among them who believe (i.e. all those who follow Islamic Monotheism, the religion of Prophet Muhammad PBUH till the Day of Resurrection) and do righteous good deeds, forgiveness and a mighty reward (i.e. Paradise).*

Regarding the judges, he next prescribes their qualities: they must not be bewildered by intricate matters, must not be worn thin by constant litigation, must stand as mountains in truth, must not be content with superficial resolution, must excel in debate and argument, and must be seekers of truth, protected from reputation and desire. He observes, quite rightly, that such individuals are exceedingly rare. He further advises that judges be generously compensated so that financial need does not drive them toward corruption.

Concerning the learned and wise, he counsels that their integrity be tested before appointment to office, without bias in selection, and that their conduct be scrutinized even after installation, with severe punishment for any misuse of authority.

As for the peasants who till the earth and those who collect the revenue, he instructs: "Be more solicitous about cultivation than about revenue collection, for revenue depends upon cultivation. Whoever imposes taxation without inspecting the state of agriculture destroys the people." He explains that destruction of the earth flows from destruction of those who inhabit it, and poverty descends upon them when the desire to accumulate wealth dominates the hearts of the wise, when they doubt their own survival, and when they cannot benefit from worthy examples. To doubt one's survival is to imagine that one will dwell forever and face no reckoning. Allah addresses such people:

> ⟪quran 104:1-4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيْلٌۭ لِّكُلِّ هُمَزَةٍۢ لُّمَزَةٍ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِى جَمَعَ مَالًۭا وَعَدَّدَهُۥ ‎ ‏يَحْسَبُ أَنَّ مَالَهُۥٓ أَخْلَدَهُۥ ‎ ‏كَلَّا ۖ لَيُنۢبَذَنَّ فِى ٱلْحُطَمَةِ ‎⟫
> *Woe to every slanderer and backbiter. Who has gathered wealth and counted it, He thinks that his wealth will make him last forever! Nay! Verily, he will be thrown into the crushing Fire.*

When a person forgets that all things perish, greed for accumulation takes root within him, and instead of acquiring true spiritual treasures, he wastes his life hoarding false material riches, thus giving birth to oppression.

Regarding the appointment of officials and representatives, he advises: do not appoint those who merely display good character, but examine their history and seek the public's assessment of them, granting office only to those with established reputations for trustworthiness.

As for the merchants, he declares they are people who bring great benefit to society and should therefore receive the finest treatment. Generally peace-loving by nature, they should be left to conduct their business freely, yet the evils that arise among them—hoarding, miserliness, and fraud—must be checked.

### The Poor and the Neediest

Concerning the poor, the disabled, the orphans, and the aged, Amīr al-Muʾminīn observes that these are the people most desperately in need of the ruler's justice, yet who cannot stretch forth their hands in petition. He declared: "The ruler must pay special attention to these people if he wishes Allah to forgive him on the Day of Resurrection." He should appoint a particular officer charged with attending to their needs and presenting their affairs before him. He then states: "This is a burden for the ruler, but Allah lightens it for those whose gaze is fixed upon the Hereafter, who school themselves in patience, and who possess certainty in what Allah has promised them."

Here again he has bound this difficult matter to the spiritual dimension, teaching that if one's vision extends beyond this world toward the afterlife, even the most arduous task becomes manageable. Those whose desires remain confined to worldly gain, however, will fall prey to negligence toward the poor. For from a worldly perspective, aiding the poor offers no political advantage, bringing no apparent benefit to the ruler in his expenditure of public resources. Yet when this perspective is accompanied by consciousness of Allah's all-encompassing justice, His abundant mercy, and the desire to attain the Hereafter through aid to these people, the task becomes light, and rulers of such caliber engage in sincere and steadfast support to the destitute.

This approach transcends mere generosity and almsgiving. A person who brings the concept of aiding the poor to its full perfection will not become enslaved to selfish desire, petty ambition, or negligence—whether willful or inadvertent. And having cultivated this quality, the next virtue described by Maulana ʿAli—patience—is born spontaneously within him, for his actions are no longer confined to personal exertion and desire alone, but are accompanied by divine grace flowing from the roots of faith. Consequently, such people place trust in Allah's reward, His justice, and His promise of mercy, and the ruler's commitment to aid the poor and establish justice for them becomes steadfast and unwavering.

These moral realities of the Hereafter lie hidden from the eyes of worldly rulers, obscured by their veiled prejudices and manifest corruptions. Such oppressors neither believe in the blessings of the Hereafter nor in its punishments and chastisements. They are called oppressors because they violated the demands of divine justice and denied that supreme attribute of mercy which constitutes the essence of the Divine Nature.


<!-- section 19 (id=3591, raw_sort=19): نیت کی اہمیت -->

## The Importance of Intention

The most vital element underlying all divine commandments is intention (niyyat). Even when the establishment of justice in the world encounters the impermanence of worldly conditions and cannot be fully realized, the sincere intention of the actor becomes the foundation of moral life itself, filling the heart with the taste of divine grace. When belief in God's promise is genuine and unwavering—when one truly accepts that the divine word is true—this conviction produces a profound effect upon the soul: it transforms the personal desire to act justly into an unconditional necessity, and converts what might otherwise be merely desirable into an inviolable reality. Here we see that morality finds its true strength through spirituality; once this ground is secure, all the commandments of the Sharīʿah (divine law) become bearable and even joyful. Thereafter, the person establishes justice not in hope of future reward in the Hereafter, but from gratitude for what God has already granted. Indeed, the Qur'ān speaks of the blessings of Paradise as if they have already been bestowed upon the believers—as though what shall occur has already come to pass:

> ⟪quran 108:1-2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَعْطَيْنَكَ ٱلْكَوْثَرَ ‎ ‏فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَٱنْحَرْ ‎⟫
> *Verily, We have granted you (O Muhammad (Peace be upon him)) Al-Kauthar (a river in Paradise); Therefore turn in prayer to your Lord and sacrifice (to Him only).*
> indeed We have given you abundance, so perform the prayer to your Lord and sacrifice.
> — **Quran 108:1-2 (inline widget)**

In commentary upon this principle, Mawlānā ʿAlī distinguishes three categories of worship: there is a group that worships God from desire for Paradise—this is mercantile worship; another group worships from fear of Hell—this is the worship of slaves; and a third worships from gratitude alone—this is the worship of the free.[^cite-40] For this reason he declared in one place:

> ⟪ar-quote:یا الہی ما عبدتک من شوق جنتک ولا من خوف النارک بل وجدت مستحق لی العبادۃ فالعبدتک⟫
> "O Allah, I do not worship You in passion for Paradise, nor in fear of Hellfire, but I have found You worthy of worship, and so I worship You."

A person is absolved from the deficiencies of outward action through the sincerity of inward intention; his deed does not rise or fall according to its results, but according to the purity of his intention alone. Justice is not established for worldly gain, but for the sake of justice itself, because the just action forms the essential purpose of the just person. Justice does not belong to God as something He performs; rather, He *is* justice itself. For this reason, the just person acts justly to align with the will of God—not merely to obey a command, and not from worldly appetite. The Qur'ān declares:

> ⟪quran 92:17-21⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَسَيُجَنَّبُهَا ٱلْأَتْقَى ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِى يُؤْتِى مَالَهُۥ يَتَزَكَّىٰ ‎ ‏وَمَا لِأَحَدٍ عِندَهُۥ مِن نِّعْمَةٍۢ تُجْزَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِلَّا ٱبْتِغَآءَ وَجْهِ رَبِّهِ ٱلْأَعْلَىٰ ‎ ‏وَلَسَوْفَ يَرْضَىٰ ‎⟫
> *And Al-Muttaqun (the pious and righteous - see V.2:2) will be far removed from it (Hell). He who spends his wealth for increase in self-purification, And have in his mind no favour from anyone for which a reward is expected in return, Except only the desire to seek the Countenance of his Lord, the Most High; He surely will be pleased (when he will enter Paradise).*
> And away from it is the God-fearing one who gives his wealth so that he may be purified; and no soul has any favour against it, but he who is recompensed only with the Countenance of his Lord, the Most High, and he shall soon be well-pleased.
> — **Quran 92:17-21 (inline widget)**

This passage defines al-abrār (the righteous), and all the learned are unanimous that these verses were revealed in honor of Mawlānā ʿAlī and his household when they fasted for three days and gave the bread of their own table to the poor, the needy, and the orphans:

> ⟪quran 76:8-9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيُطْعِمُونَ ٱلطَّعَامَ عَلَىٰ حُبِّهِۦ مِسْكِينًۭا وَيَتِيمًۭا وَأَسِيرًا ‎ ‏إِنَّمَا نُطْعِمُكُمْ لِوَجْهِ ٱللَّهِ لَا نُرِيدُ مِنكُمْ جَزَآءًۭ وَلَا شُكُورًا ‎⟫
> *And they give food, inspite of their love for it (or for the love of Him), to Miskin (poor), the orphan, and the captive, (Saying): "We feed you seeking Allah's Countenance only. We wish for no reward, nor thanks from you.*
> And they feed the needy, and the orphan, and the captive, out of love for Him. Whatever We feed you, it is only for the sake of Allah; it is not for us to take any retribution from you, nor to be grateful.
> — **Quran 76:8-9 (inline widget)**

An action becomes truly acceptable when it is wholly for God's sake, when it requires neither praise nor blame from any creature, when it is neither weakened by external difficulty nor strengthened by internal consequence.[^cite-41] This relationship between intention and action illuminates ʿAlī's saying that his heart dwells in heaven whilst his body labors in the world. Here we must observe a crucial distinction: worldly morals prove strong or weak through their visible results—if good fruit appears, the person persists; if not, he abandons the effort. But the action of one who fixes his sight upon the Hereafter is sustained by the sincerity of intention alone. This does not mean avoiding diligent works; rather, sincere intention means that whatever the outcome, the person continues striving for goodness and never wearies or ceases. Conversely, any action that falters under circumstance or shrinks to mere formalism reveals a defect in intention. Pure intention demands relentless, unremitting exertion toward its purpose.

The just person never despairs, never abandons the quest for justice. His purpose is not to achieve justice for some external result, but the spiritual fulfillment of his own justice through understanding that his physical existence is bound to circumstance and ultimately to God's pleasure. Yet such a person does not tire from fruitlessness; his effort remains constant, as certain as the permanence of God's blessings. His actions are strengthened by the divine attribute of justice itself.[^cite-42]

As Christ taught, when the principles of justice are considered separately from spirituality, personal idealism arises—idealism that is buffeted by external consequences and therefore broken by hardship and despair. But when spirituality is joined to justice, the indestructible divine attribute supports it and grants it the power of fulfillment. In proportion as one's principles rest upon spiritual knowledge, despair cannot touch him when difficulties mount. We find this exemplified in the life of Amīr al-Muʾminīn (Commander of the Faithful) himself: when he assumed the throne of apparent caliphate, successive waves of war and rebellion arose, preventing him from advancing all the principles and strategies he envisioned. Yet despite these trials, he never fell into disappointment, dejection, or depression—never did his effort and quest in establishing justice waver. He used to say that no deed is ordinary if piety (taqwā) is united with it. Despair is separated from the pious person, for he remains conscious of the truth. This piety becomes his way out from the injustices of this world, as ʿAlī said: ⟪ar-quote:من یتق اللہ یجعل لہ مخرجا من الفتن وا نور من الظلم⟫ "Whoever fears Allah, Allah will make for him a way out from trials and light in darkness."

<!-- section 20 (id=3592, raw_sort=20): عبادت کی فضیلت -->

## The Excellence of Worship

We now arrive at that crucial passage in the letter wherein the Master describes the essence of all virtues: worship (ʿibādah). At the outset he counsels that the ruler should perform the duties of prayer. Here he tells the one addressed that after discharging all administrative tasks, he must devote the best portion of his time to labor for God's sake—and this labor is worship and dedication. Mālik al-Ashtar has been specifically commanded to purify his faith through obligatory acts of worship and to purify his devotion. By purifying one's faith, the aim is to clarify and refine the innermost substance of the relationship with God through worship—a relationship that belongs to the individual and his Lord alone. The depth and quality of this relationship marks the measure of all human virtue.

He says: "Know that every action of yours depends upon your worship." By worship, he does not mean only the outward bowing and prostration, but the inner sincerity (ikhlās) connected to and animating these outward forms. The sincerity, intensity, and fulfillment of this prayer accomplish its purpose. He instructs: "Devote the strength of your night and day to God, and complete the deeds by which you draw near to Him, and perform them without fatigue, and take your body to its limits." The crucial word here is *closeness* (qurb)—that closeness attained through dedication arising from the depths of the heart in the solitude of the darkest hours. That is, all outward action is governed by the pure intention to surrender oneself to God. When a person's inner life is illuminated by the light of prayer, its rays shine forth also in outward life. For this reason, he asked Mālik to dedicate the finest portion of his time to God. Every moment of the ruler's time belongs to God, if the intention behind his action is sound and if the people are thereby protected. At that moment, one perceives that the fountains of obligatory and supererogatory prayer overflow and their effects manifest in the outward deeds of life. The hadīth (tradition) of the Messenger of God relates this beautiful truth:

"My servant does not draw near to Me through anything more beloved to Me than the obligatory duties. My servant continues to draw near to Me through supererogatory acts until I love him. When I love him, I am his hearing by which he hears, his sight by which he sees, his hand by which he grasps, and his feet by which he walks."[^cite-43]

To see and act through God means to perceive things according to their true nature and then to act accordingly—which is to establish justice, that is, to keep all things in their proper place. It is essential to note in this hadīth that both obligatory and supererogatory prayers are means of drawing near to God; yet the station of divine action (al-fiʿl al-ilāhī) is attained through acts of worship, not through obligatory prayer alone. As ʿAlī says, take your actions to the limits of your body. This shows that there is no benefit in mechanical, careless worship. He said, "The example of one who prays without *ijtihād* (diligent striving) is like one who shoots an arrow without a bow."

As noted earlier, in order to connect with God and achieve true unification (tawḥīd) with Him, complete integration of the self is required, and prayer is the place where the deep dimensions of the human soul are revealed, cultivated, and unified. Therefore, the fulfillment of prayer is not by tongue and body alone, but by the whole of soul and body together. God says:

> ⟪quran 24:36⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فِى بُيُوتٍ أَذِنَ ٱللَّهُ أَن تُرْفَعَ وَيُذْكَرَ فِيهَا ٱسْمُهُۥ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ فِيهَا بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ ‎⟫
> *In houses (mosques), which Allah has ordered to be raised (to be cleaned, and to be honoured), in them His Name is glorified in the mornings and in the afternoons or the evenings,*
> in houses which Allah has commanded to be venerated and His name to be remembered therein, glorifying Him in the mornings and evenings.
> — **Quran 24:36 (inline widget)**

Regarding closeness to God, ʿAlī said: "Indeed, God has made remembrance (dhikr) for hearts, through which they hear when deaf and see when blind."[^cite-44] In every age there are special servants of God to whom He speaks in their thoughts, addressing them through the essence of their intellect. They diffuse the light of God in their hearts, ears, and eyes and summon people to remembrance of the days of God.

The importance of dhikr (remembrance) becomes clear through your own statement, by which consciousness of truth is created. By dhikr, you do not mean only the invocation of a specific divine name, but rather the constant, unwavering awareness of God—the essence of all worship, meditation, and contemplation. The purpose is not merely to remember God or to chant His name, but to contemplate His divine realities through both the outward and inward manifestations of His Names. In another passage, Mawlānā ʿAlī speaks of dhikr:

"There are those who have taken remembrance of this world in such a way that neither commerce nor livelihood turns them from remembrance of God. They spend the days of their lives in it. They exhort people to justice, and they themselves stand firm in justice. That is, they themselves show people how all things are kept in their proper place and explain how all things are kept in their proper place." Spirituality is not something separate from action; rather, it is a connection to moral depths that arise from relationship—a relationship established through worship in general and through remembrance in particular. Just as sincerity of intention has been shown to be the essential substance, so now it is known that sincerity is paramount in prayer, which takes the body to its limits. If the attribute of justice is in the very essence of God, then the closer a person draws to God through prayer and remembrance, the more just he becomes and develops in himself positive capacities—spirituality, intellect, and virtue. Justice is both the cause of worship and its consequence. Thus is the bond between worship and justice made clear. Justice teaches us to keep all things in their proper place. Therefore, justice toward God is fulfilled through prayer and remembrance, and justice toward oneself and others is the fruit of the closeness attained through worship of God, and from this closeness all virtues spring forth.

Amīr al-Muʾminīn has emphasized both the outward prayer and its inward origin (dhikr). Plato taught that the highest knowledge is knowledge of the Good (al-khayr), for all goodness and righteousness spring from it. If a person acquires all the knowledge of the world yet does not acquire knowledge of the Good, he has acquired nothing. He compared virtue to the Sun, saying that what the Sun accomplishes for sight, virtue accomplishes for the intellect and existence.

Once Zaylaʿ al-Yamanī asked ʿAlī: "O ʿAlī, have you seen the object of your sincerity?" He replied, "If I had not seen him, I would not have worshipped him." The questioner asked, "How did you see him?" He answered, "He cannot be seen with the eyes of the flesh, but the heart sees him with the truth of faith."[^cite-45] From this statement we know that dhikr is of supreme importance, for through it the heart is purified and clarified. However, dhikr does not refer to knowledge of outward forms; rather, it is knowledge of the Creator of these forms, described in Islam as the divine attribute of al-Muṣawwir (the Fashioner). Yet this remembrance cannot be expressed in words like other sciences. It requires tireless worship and labor day and night. It is like a spark created by the friction of hard work; but once this lamp is kindled, it never dies again and continues to sustain itself throughout life.

The essence of justice in Amīr al-Muʾminīn's letter is this: in order for any society to establish justice, it must grasp these Islamic concepts not merely through intellect but through the heart, for the heart is connected to inner realities and only the heart can perceive them by the light of God. This is impossible without His grace. The prophetic requirement of justice is that all components of human life—worship, morality, and action—be woven in harmony with one another on the principle of monotheism (tawḥīd). The realm of ethics cannot be separated from the realm of spirituality, for in ʿAlī's view, true virtue is that which is original, fortified, and directed toward truth. Therefore, these requirements of justice in the soul can only be created through worship whose spirituality is carried through remembrance. This final analysis alone proves that remembrance establishes the measure of human virtue.


<!-- section 21 (id=3602, raw_sort=21): ذکر اللہ -->

## Remembrance of Allah

Ali al-Hajwiri, the author of *Kashf al-Mahjoob*, writes of the Commander of the Faithful regarding his mastery of spiritual realities. One of the greatest luminaries among the Prophetic descendants was the Imam, drowned in the tempestuous sea of trials and consumed by the flames of divine love. He stands as a chief among the saints and the purified ones (*muqtadā awliyāʾ wa-l-asfiyāʾ*, the leaders of the Friends of God and the Pure).
