His station on this spiritual path was grand and singular. He possessed complete mastery of all the realities of the higher world—a mastery so profound that even Junaid, the celebrated Sufi master, declared: "Ali is our master in the knowledge of principles and foundations" (*Shaykhunā fī Uṣūl wa-l-Balāyā*).[^cite-46] Ali stands as the Imam of all intellectual and practical domains. The Sufis interpret knowledge of this path as a matter of principle and recognize its practice as the endurance of calamities with steadfast virtue.

His forbearance amid affliction recalls the saying of the Commander of the Faithful (*Amīr al-Muʾminīn*), wherein he declared his love for those from whom the ignorant turn away. What the Sufis cherish—and from which the masses recoil in aversion—is worship in its deepest sense: an exclusive attentiveness to the Creator that excludes all other creatures from the heart. Such worship becomes a form of death in life, wherein the worshipper sacrifices kinship and all worldly occupations upon the altar of divine attention. They annihilate themselves utterly for the sake of Truth.

The word *dhikr* (remembrance) carries extraordinary eloquence in its meaning and admits no perfect substitute in other tongues. It encompasses the senses of remembrance, reflection, petition, repetition, glorification (*tasbīḥ*), and recitation. Yet it bears also the connotation of mention, statement, praise, celebration, renown, honor, and admonition. God Himself has designated the Qur'an as *dhikr*—the Remembrance.[^cite-47]

The most penetrating definition appears in the lexicon of al-Raghib al-Isfahani, who writes that remembrance is the power by which a person preserves knowledge and safeguards understanding. Though memory (*tadhakkur*) refers to the past recalled, remembrance (*dhikr*) refers to the present realization of what is brought to mind. *Dhikr* denotes the presence of something within one's consciousness and speech—the actualization of knowledge through utterance and inward presence. Thus there exist two forms of *dhikr*: the remembrance of the heart and the remembrance of the tongue, each divisible further into two kinds. One is the *dhikr* bound by time, possessing defined periods; the other is the *dhikr* unbounded, eternal and unceasing. The remembrance of God becomes truly possible only through the presence and awakening of the heart.

The remembrance of Allah is a consciousness that absorbs the divine presence, yet simultaneously it constitutes a process operating within spiritual discipline. In this paradox lies its dual nature: *dhikr* is both the objective to be attained and the means of attainment, both the knowledge sought and the action flowing from that knowledge. For the Sufis and saints, *zikr* becomes a methodical system through which the hearts absorb what the intellect comprehends, transforming the abstract imaginative object into the concrete existence of spiritual realities.[^cite-48] If prayer (*salāt*) establishes the foundation of worship, then the remembrance of Allah surpasses it in excellence, as the Qur'an proclaims:

> ⟪quran 29:45⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱتْلُ مَآ أُوحِىَ إِلَيْكَ مِنَ ٱلْكِتَبِ وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ تَنْهَىٰ عَنِ ٱلْفَحْشَآءِ وَٱلْمُنكَرِ ۗ وَلَذِكْرُ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ يَعْلَمُ مَا تَصْنَعُونَ ‎⟫
> Recite what has been revealed to thee of the Book, and be steadfast in prayer. Verily, prayer restrains from indecency and evil; and the remembrance of Allah is greater; and Allah is aware of what you do.

Numerous prophetic traditions celebrate the virtue of *dhikr*. The Messenger of God once asked his companions: "Shall I not inform you of the purest of your deeds, that which elevates you highest in rank before your Lord, which surpasses the gift of gold and silver, and exceeds in merit the encounter with your enemies in battle?" They replied, "Tell us, O Messenger of God!" And he said, "It is your remembrance of Allah, constantly and with devotion." Similarly, Maulana Ali declared: "Remember Allah perpetually, for He illuminates the hearts, and remembrance is the finest worship." Imam Jaʿfar al-Ṣādiq likewise taught: "Our Shīʿa are those who, in their solitude, remember Allah abundantly."

### Remembrance of Allah Strengthens Hearts

Let us return now to the sermon of the Commander of the Faithful, wherein he declared that the remembrance of Allah is a burning (*ḥarq*) for the hearts—a consuming fire that purifies and illuminates. At the beginning of this sermon, he recited verses from the Qur'an concerning divine light:

> ⟪quran 24:35-37⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ ٱللَّهُ نُورُ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ ۚ مَثَلُ نُورِهِۦ كَمِشْكَوٰةٍۢ فِيهَا مِصْبَاحٌ ۖ ٱلْمِصْبَاحُ فِى زُجَاجَةٍ ۖ ٱلزُّجَاجَةُ كَأَنَّهَا كَوْكَبٌۭ دُرِّىٌّۭ يُوقَدُ مِن شَجَرَةٍۢ مُّبَرَكَةٍۢ زَيْتُونَةٍۢ لَّا شَرْقِيَّةٍۢ وَلَا غَرْبِيَّةٍۢ يَكَادُ زَيْتُهَا يُضِىٓءُ وَلَوْ لَمْ تَمْسَسْهُ نَارٌۭ ۚ نُّورٌ عَلَىٰ نُورٍۢ ۗ يَهْدِى ٱللَّهُ لِنُورِهِۦ مَن يَشَآءُ ۚ وَيَضْرِبُ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْأَمْثَلَ لِلنَّاسِ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ بِكُلِّ شَىْءٍ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎ ‏فِى بُيُوتٍ أَذِنَ ٱللَّهُ أَن تُرْفَعَ وَيُذْكَرَ فِيهَا ٱسْمُهُۥ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ فِيهَا بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ ‎ ‏رِجَالٌۭ لَّا تُلْهِيهِمْ تِجَارَةٌۭ وَلَا بَيْعٌ عَن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ وَإِقَامِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةِ وَإِيتَآءِ ٱلزَّكَوٰةِ ۙ يَخَافُونَ يَوْمًۭا تَتَقَلَّبُ فِيهِ ٱلْقُلُوبُ وَٱلْأَبْصَرُ ‎⟫
> Allah is the Light of the heavens and the earth. The parable of His Light is as a niche wherein is a lamp, the lamp in glass, the glass as it were a pearlaceous star lit from a blessed olive-tree, neither of the east nor of the west whose oil would almost shine forth though fire touched it not. Light upon Light! Allah guideth to His Light whom He will, and Allah setteth forth parables for mankind, and Allah is Knower of all things. In houses which Allah hath permitted to be exalted, and wherein His Name is remembered, therein glorify Him morning and evening—men whom neither merchandise nor sale beguileth from remembrance of Allah and establishment of prayer and paying of the poor-due. They fear a Day when hearts and eyes will overturn.

When the Imam reached the passage concerning "men whom neither trade nor commerce distracts from the remembrance of Allah," he expanded upon its meaning with these words:

Verily, Allah has established the remembrance of Allah as a polish (*janīla*) for the hearts, by means of which they may hear when deafened, see when blinded, and submit when they resist. In every age, Allah has appointed servants to whom He speaks through the wellspring of their thoughts and intellects. He spreads the light of guidance through their hearing, their sight, and the light that rises within their hearts, and calls people to the sacred days of remembrance. Among them is a group who prefer the remembrance of Allah to all else in this world, such that neither commerce nor trade divert them from *dhikr*. They expend the days of their lives in this remembrance. They live as if already departed to the Hereafter, yet they dwell in this world—living simultaneously in both realms.

The connection between the burning of the hearts and the verse of divine light grows luminous. The hidden light within the heart is revealed through *dhikr*. The light of inner consciousness becomes radiant through the light of external remembrance, becoming ⟪ar:نُور عَلَىٰ نُور⟫ (light upon light). When the heart becomes illuminated by this divine radiance, the effect spreads to all other faculties, and they too are kindled by this light, whereby the meaning becomes clear: the burning ⟪ar:نُور⟫ (light) manifests as ⟪ar:عَلَىٰ نُور⟫ (upon light). To burn means to be purified, to be revealed, to be brought forth into luminosity. Allah says in the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 92:1-2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلَّيْلِ إِذَا يَغْشَىٰ ‎ ‏وَٱلنَّهَارِ إِذَا تَجَلَّىٰ ‎⟫
> By the night when it envelopeth, and by the day when it shineth forth.

In these verses, Allah swears by the night as it envelops—when it emerges into being from nothingness. And He swears by the day as it brightens—when it appears in radiance where before was darkness. Elsewhere He states:

> ⟪quran 91:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلنَّهَارِ إِذَا جَلَّىٰهَا ‎⟫
> And by the day when it illuminateth it.

That is, through the remembrance of Allah, the consciousness dormant within the heart awakens and manifests itself in the form of righteous action. The heart's role merits deep contemplation: on one hand, it receives divine light through *dhikr* and reflects this radiance upon all other faculties; on the other hand, *dhikr* awakens the hidden consciousness buried in its depths, revealing truths that reason alone cannot penetrate. Maulana Ali spoke of this hidden consciousness when he referred to ⟪ar:دفائن العقول⟫ (the buried treasures of the intellect). Thus it becomes evident that the true purpose of *dhikr* is the purification of the heart—the Amir al-Badan (the commander of the body) and the center of genuine spiritual vision.

Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 7:179⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنَا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيرًۭا مِّنَ ٱلْجِنِّ وَٱلْإِنسِ ۖ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌۭ لَّا يَفْقَهُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ أَعْيُنٌۭ لَّا يُبْصِرُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ آذَانٌۭ لَّا يَسْمَعُونَ بِهَآ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ كَٱلْأَنْعَمِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْغَفِلُونَ ‎⟫
> And verily We have created many of the jinn and mankind for Hell. They have hearts wherewith they understand not, eyes wherewith they see not, and ears wherewith they hear not. These are as cattle; nay, they are further astray. These are the heedless.

Here Allah employs the word *ghāfilūn* (the heedless), which stands as the opposite of *dhikr* (remembrance). The heedless are those who have forgotten. The following verse describes the mystical practice of *dhikr* itself:

> ⟪quran 7:180⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْأَسْمَآءُ ٱلْحُسْنَىٰ فَٱدْعُوهُ بِهَا ۖ وَذَرُوا۟ ٱلَّذِينَ يُلْحِدُونَ فِىٓ أَسْمَٓئِهِۦ ۚ سَيُجْزَوْنَ مَا كَانُوا۟ يَعْمَلُونَ ‎⟫
> Unto Allah belong the Most Beautiful Names. Invoke Him by them, and leave those who blaspheme His Names; they shall be requited for what they do.

The relationship between remembrance and the heart becomes crystalline in the following verses:

> ⟪quran 13:28⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَتَطْمَىِٕنُّ قُلُوبُهُم بِذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۗ أَلَا بِذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ تَطْمَىِٕنُّ ٱلْقُلُوبُ ‎⟫
> Those who believe and whose hearts rest secure in the remembrance of Allah. Is it not in the remembrance of Allah that hearts find rest?

> ⟪quran 50:37⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ فِى ذَلِكَ لَذِكْرَىٰ لِمَن كَانَ لَهُۥ قَلْبٌ أَوْ أَلْقَى ٱلسَّمْعَ وَهُوَ شَهِيدٌۭ ‎⟫
> Verily in that is a lesson for him who hath a heart, or giveth ear with a present mind.

> ⟪quran 8:2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّمَا ٱلْمُؤْمِنُونَ ٱلَّذِينَ إِذَا ذُكِرَ ٱللَّهُ وَجِلَتْ قُلُوبُهُمْ وَإِذَا تُلِيَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ آيَتُهُۥ زَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَنًۭا وَعَلَىٰ رَبِّهِمْ يَتَوَكَّلُونَ ‎⟫
> The believers are only those whose hearts quake when Allah is mentioned, and when His revelations are recited unto them it increaseth their faith, and in their Lord they put their trust.

> ⟪quran 39:22⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَمَن شَرَحَ ٱللَّهُ صَدْرَهُۥ لِلْإِسْلَمِ فَهُوَ عَلَىٰ نُورٍۢ مِّن رَّبِّهِۦ ۚ فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْقَسِيَةِ قُلُوبُهُم مِّن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ فِى ضَلَلٍۢ مُّبِينٍ ‎⟫
> Is he whose breast Allah hath expanded for Islam, so that he followeth a light from his Lord, [as he whose breast is straitened]? Nay, woe unto those whose hearts are hardened against the remembrance of Allah. Those are in plain error.

> ⟪quran 39:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱللَّهُ نَزَّلَ أَحْسَنَ ٱلْحَدِيثِ كِتَبًۭا مُّتَشَبِهًۭا مَّثَانِىَ تَقْشَعِرُّ مِنْهُ جُلُودُ ٱلَّذِينَ يَخْشَوْنَ رَبَّهُمْ ثُمَّ تَلِينُ جُلُودُهُمْ وَقُلُوبُهُمْ إِلَىٰ ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ ذَلِكَ هُدَى ٱللَّهِ يَهْدِى بِهِۦ مَن يَشَآءُ ۚ وَمَن يُضْلِلِ ٱللَّهُ فَمَا لَهُۥ مِنْ هَادٍ ‎⟫
> Allah hath revealed the fairest of statements, a Scripture consistent, wherein is reiteration. The skins of those who fear their Lord do creep at it, then their skins and their hearts soften at the remembrance of Allah. That is the guidance of Allah wherewith He guideth whom He will, and he whom Allah sendeth astray, for him there is no guide.

These verses reveal that remembrance is intimately bound to the heart, which transforms consciousness into reality. The heart requires continuous enrichment through *dhikr*. The Prophet declared: "For everything there is a polish; the polish of the heart is the remembrance of Allah." This hadith points to a systematic process integrating awareness with action, returning us to the prophetic instruction to "worship Allah as if you see Him." On one level, *dhikr* serves the purification of thought and contemplation; on another, it constitutes regular action manifesting as various forms of glorification ⟪ar:تسبیح⟫, magnification ⟪ar:تمجید⟫, praise ⟪ar:تحمید⟫, and sanctification ⟪ar:تقدیس⟫, and the declaration of divine unity ⟪ar:تحلیل⟫—all expressions of remembrance that remove the rust of forgetfulness from the heart's surface.

The Messenger of Allah described such devoted souls as "the people of remembrance." He said, "Verily, Allah possesses angels who traverse the roads seeking those who remember Allah. When they encounter such a group, they call to one another: 'Come! Here is that which you seek!'"

If we now consider that ⟪ar:بصیرت⟫ (spiritual vision)—what the heart perceives through *dhikr*—is purified and revived by faith, then we approach understanding what Maulana Ali meant when he stated that this insight is obtained through divine inspiration (*ilhām*), and that this insight is no less than the vision of Allah Himself. In another place, he calls the pure heart the locus of seeing God and declares, "Whoever purifies his heart sees Allah." The connection between purity of heart and *dhikr* emerges plainly in his prayer: "Where are those whose deeds are performed purely for Allah's sake, who cleanse their hearts through remembrance of Allah so that it becomes a dwelling place for Allah?" His utterance accords with the hadith in which the Prophet taught: "My servant continues drawing near to Me through supererogatory works until I love him; and when I love him, I become his hearing with which he hears, his sight with which he sees, his hand with which he grasps, and his feet with which he walks."[^cite-49] That is, human perception and action become integrated into the divine reality, whereby the heart attains spiritual insight. When such a station is reached, the heart—the seat of consciousness—transcends the realm of physicality, and its inner essence becomes bound to the Truth. From this point onward, it beholds as Allah beholds, until at last it beholds Allah Himself.

Abu Talib al-Makki, a celebrated Sufi master, wrote that if it is indeed true that the divine enters into human feelings through human action, then the highest spiritual consciousness would manifest not as the sight *of* Allah but as the sight that *is* Allah's own—vision mediated through the purified heart. Maulana Ali explicates this philosophy and declares: ⟪ar-quote:أعرف اللہ با اللہ⟫ "Know Allah through Allah." In this ultimate analysis, Allah becomes both the Seer and the Seen, as the Qur'an states:

> ⟪quran 85:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَشَاهِدٍۢ وَمَشْهُودٍۢ ‎⟫
> And by the witnessing Day and by that which is witnessed.

The Seen is the inner essence of human consciousness; the Witness is the divine reality itself. Thus, a person's profound faith renders Allah present perpetually and everywhere. As Maulana Ali proclaimed in his sermon: "By Thy greatness that pervadeth all things, by Thy names that are the foundation of all things, by Thy knowledge that encompasseth all things, by the light of Thy countenance through which all things are illuminated."

Nothing can subsist without its foundation. The Name of Allah—or the totality of His Names—provides that very foundation. To perceive things correctly is to perceive the divine attributes that constitute their true reality; all objects are but physical reflections and manifestations of these Names and divine self-disclosures. When the heart is purified through *dhikr*, it perceives Allah everywhere. The presence of Allah in all things appears in two places in the Qur'an: once from Allah's perspective and once from humanity's:

> ⟪quran 2:115⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْمَشْرِقُ وَٱلْمَغْرِبُ ۚ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا۟ فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ وَسِعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> Unto Allah belong the East and the West. Whithersoever ye turn, there is the Face of Allah. Lo! Allah is All-Embracing, All-Knowing.

> ⟪quran 41:53⟫
> ⟪ar:‏سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ حَتَىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ ۗ أَوَلَمْ يَكْفِ بِرَبِّكَ أَنَّهُۥ عَلَىٰ كُلِّ شَىْءٍۢ شَهِيدٌ ‎⟫
> We shall show them Our portents on the horizon and within themselves until it will be manifest unto them that it is the Truth. Doth not thy Lord suffice, since He is Witness over all things?

The heart purified by *dhikr* discerns these signs in all places and in all things. Yet such vision does not entail the reduction of Allah to human sensible phenomena. Maulana Ali stated: "Allah is in all things, though not by proximity; and He is apart from all things, though not by separation." God's presence in creation does not result from spatial nearness, nor does it diminish the divine transcendence. Allah is infinitely closer to us than we are to ourselves, and incomparably more distant, as He declared:

> ⟪quran 50:16⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا ٱلْإِنسَنَ وَنَعْلَمُ مَا تُوَسْوِسُ بِهِۦ نَفْسُهُۥ ۖ وَنَحْنُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ حَبْلِ ٱلْوَرِيدِ ‎⟫
> We created man and We know what his soul whispereth unto him, and We are nearer unto him than his jugular vein.

> ⟪quran 112:4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَمْ يَكُن لَّهُۥ كُفُوًا أَحَدٌۢ ‎⟫
> And there is none comparable unto Him.

No existence can remain severed from Allah, yet neither does it possess intrinsic connection to the divine. All objects exist by entering and exiting simultaneously—sustained by Being yet ever contingent. His presence with all things and within all things does not diminish His divinity; His distance from all things does not remove Him from them. As Maulana Ali said, "Allah is One—not in numerical terms, but in the sense that He admits of no equal." What is singular admits no enumeration; to count Allah is to commit the sin of *shirk* (association of partners with God).

The Imam clarifies that no existence is possible apart from His existence. He alone truly is; all else is illusion. The radical doctrine of *tawḥīd* (*the declaration of divine unity*), which excludes all otherness, necessarily means that every creation besides Allah is a false deity, for they too appear singular yet stand in opposition to Allah's absolute Oneness. All praise belongs to Allah, who is hidden in the secret essence of things and whose essence manifests through the existence of creatures. The eye that beholds cannot contain Him, yet the eye that sees Him not cannot deny His reality; nor can the heart that acknowledges His reality deny His ineffability. He is the height above which nothing rises, yet the nearness beyond which nothing draws closer. Allah has not made the intellect capable of comprehending His attributes, though He has not withheld their knowledge from it.

One might ask: how is it possible that we cannot even grasp His attributes, yet knowledge of Him remains possible? The answer lies in another dimension of *dhikr*: to remember and to recognize. Man combines the components of knowledge that already exist within his consciousness but which he has forgotten. Through remembrance, he recognizes what he once knew and lost. This is not a fragmentation of knowledge requiring reassembly into a picture. Rather, it resembles awakening after sleep, enlightenment after the veils of innate forgetfulness have lifted.

Maulana Ali states in his first sermon: "⟪ar-quote:اول الدین معرفتہ⟫The first of religion is its knowledge." The word "first" (*awwal*) denotes priority—the foundation, the beginning. The meaning of knowledge (*maʿrifat*) encompasses not merely the acquisition of new understanding but the recognition of what already is.[^cite-50] This reveals that Allah has already placed the knowledge of Truth within human consciousness. Man recognizes this knowledge through *dhikr* and acknowledges what he already knew yet had forgotten. In the same sermon, he continues:

⟪ar-quote:فَبَعَثَ فِيهمْ رُسُلَهُ، وَوَاتَرَ إِلَيْهِمْ أَنْبِياءَهُ، لِيَسْتَأْدُوهُمْ مِيثَاقَ فِطْرَتِهِ، وَيُذَكِّرُوهُمْ مَنْسِيَّ نِعْمَتِهِ، وَيَحْتَجُّوا عَلَيْهِمْ بَالتَّبْلِيغِ، وَيُثِيرُوا لَهُمْ دَفَائِنَ الْعُقُولِ، وَيُرُوهُمْ آيَاتِ الْمَقْدِرَةِ⟫ 

"Allah sent forth from among them His Messengers and caused His Prophets to follow in succession, that they might restore to them the covenant of the natural disposition (*fiṭrat*), remind them of the blessings they had forgotten, establish proof against them through the Summons, stir up for them the buried treasures of intellect, and show them the signs of divine power."

These buried treasures represent the knowledge that Allah placed in the depths of human consciousness—knowledge to which Allah Himself bore witness at the moment of creation, as He declares:

> ⟪quran 7:172⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِن بَنِىٓ آدَمَ مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّتَهُمْ وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ۖ قَالُوا۟ بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ ۛ أَن تَقُولُوا۟ يَوْمَ ٱلْقِيَمَةِ إِنَّا كُنَّا عَنْ هَذَا غَفِلِينَ ‎⟫
> And when thy Lord brought forth from the Children of Adam, from their reins, their seed, and made them testify of themselves, (saying): Am I not your Lord? They said: Yea, verily we testify!

This divine reality can be understood as the Divine Spirit that Allah breathed into Adam:

> ⟪quran 32:9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ثُمَّ سَوَّىٰهُ وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِن رُّوحِهِۦ ۖ وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ ٱلسَّمْعَ وَٱلْأَبْصَرَ وَٱلْأَفْـِٔدَةُ ۚ قَلِيلًۭا مَّا تَشْكُرُونَ ‎⟫
> Then He fashioned him and breathed of His Spirit into him, and appointed for you hearing and sight and hearts.

Knowledge itself entered the human being through this bestowal of spirit. Moreover:

> ⟪quran 2:31⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَعَلَّمَ آدَمَ ٱلْأَسْمَآءَ كُلَّهَا ثُمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ عَلَى ٱلْمَلَٓئِكَةِ فَقَالَ أَنۢبِـُٔونِى بِأَسْمَآءِ هَٓؤُلَٓآءِ إِن كُنتُمْ صَدِقِينَ ‎⟫
> And He taught Adam all the names, then displayed them to the angels and said: Inform Me of the names of these, if ye are truthful.

And:

> ⟪quran 30:30⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَأَقِمْ وَجْهَكَ لِلدِّينِ حَنِيفًۭا ۚ فِطْرَتَ ٱللَّهِ ٱلَّتِى فَطَرَ ٱلنَّاسَ عَلَيْهَا ۚ لَا تَبْدِيلَ لِخَلْقِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ ذَلِكَ ٱلدِّينُ ٱلْقَيِّمُ وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَ ٱلنَّاسَ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> So set thy face to the religion, a man of pure faith—Allah's natural disposition whereupon He hath created mankind. There is no changing the creation of Allah. That is the right religion, but most men know not.

This demonstrates that the knowledge of Allah has been woven into the true nature (*fiṭrat*) of humanity—the very nature from which Allah took covenant at creation, as mentioned in the previous verse. When Imam al-Bāqir was asked about this natural disposition, he explained it to mean that Allah created creatures according to the measure of *tawḥīd*—the declaration that there is no deity but Allah—such that they testified that Allah is their Lord. This shows that knowledge of God is the explication of human nature itself. Accordingly, as Maulana Ali declared, the knowledge of Allah cannot remain hidden from the human intellect.

Yet although this knowledge remains eternal within human intellect, it becomes obscured through heedlessness—the antithesis of remembrance. This obscurity cannot be remedied by external learning alone. Only when the awareness of *dhikr* and inner consciousness wells up from the heart and connects with external revelation does this divine knowledge become unveiled to heart and intellect, awakening the treasures that lay buried in the depths of understanding.

Maulana Ali states: "Praise be to Allah, who is known without vision." This statement contains an apparent contradiction, which his next words deepen: "Through creatures the Creator appears to the intellect; through creatures He is hidden from the eyes." Here lies mention of the veil (*hijāb*) born from creation itself. In a sense, all creatures serve as veils, for they conceal divine revelations within themselves; yet simultaneously, by their very existence, they testify to their Creator. Therefore, he says: "⟪ar-quote:لا تحجبہ الحجب⟫No veil can hide Him." The veil is compelled to reveal its Observer; by manifesting its own existence to the veil, the veil is forced to reflect that which it contains. The Master of the Universe declares: "⟪ar-quote:لو کشف الغطاء ما ازدت یقینا⟫If the curtain were lifted, it would not increase my certainty!"—for certainty dwells in the heart purified by *dhikr*, a heart that can now see after having been blind.

The Imam adds to this paradox: "The veil between Him and His creation is their very creation itself, so that distinction may be maintained between Creator and created, the infinite and the finite, and between the Lord and His servant."

All these creatures—all the veils fashioned by creation—exemplify the divine attribute of Al-Zahir (the Manifest), insofar as they are apparent, visible, clear, and observable. They express the divine reality through the existence that Allah grants them—manifest creations through which Allah shows forth a portion of His hidden treasures. He displays the 'outward' reality ⟪ar:الظاہر⟫ of the world whilst concealing the inward mystery ⟪ar:الباطن⟫ within this very expression. Therefore, the veil of the creature is in truth the manifestation of the Creator. Yet what do these outer veils conceal? The *Tawḥīd* (the Oneness) of Allah—for this constitutes ⟪ar:الحق⟫ (the Truth), the very essence and foundation of existence. As noted before, the divine attributes of Allah constitute the basis of all creation. This confirms that at the heart of all existence lies a single Truth, and that the essence of creation is itself the divine attributes. To associate a creature with Allah is to commit *shirk*. Therefore, the perception of divine Oneness protects us from this grave error. Hence the necessity of ever maintaining distinction between Creator and creature, infinite and finite, Lord and servant.

The veil of creation guards nature from the pantheistic confusion that would reduce infinite divinity to finite human forms. Similarly, *Tanzīh* (transcendence—the purification of Allah from all limitations) and *Taṣbīḥ* (the affirmation of divine attributes) function as veils, yet they illuminate one another when viewed together. These opposing attributes—transcendence and immanence—remain veils so long as they appear separate; but when beheld in the spiritual vision of *tawḥīd*, in which the manifest and the non-manifest are unified, they reveal each other's truth. When, conversely, one emphasizes exclusively Allah's manifestation (*ẓuhūr*), this itself becomes a veil, for it conceals the divine inwardness. Similarly, insisting solely on the inner aspect (*bāṭin*) becomes an obscuring veil that renders us unable to perceive the manifestation of Allah that dwells within His cosmos. In other words, veils arise not only from creation itself but from the limitations of human conceptualization and the finite expression of infinite divine attributes within them. For this reason, the negation of divine attributes becomes necessary. Through such negation, consciousness learns to grasp divinity and begins to perceive beyond the veil that cannot conceal it.

When Abu Saʿd al-Kharāz, a celebrated Sufi, was asked, "How did you come to know God?" he replied by observing that he perceived Allah as the One who unites the opposites. He then recited this verse:

> ⟪quran 57:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هُوَ ٱلْأَوَّلُ وَٱلْآخِرُ وَٱلظَّهِرُ وَٱلْبَاطِنُ ۖ وَهُوَ بِكُلِّ شَىْءٍ عَلِيمٌ ‎⟫
> He is the First and the Last, the Manifest and the Hidden, and He hath knowledge of all things.

Spiritual inspiration enables the seeker to perceive apparently disparate phenomena as unified within the light of monotheism. At this profound level of consciousness, the process of reintegration begins: knowledge of the Truth awakens, and the heart begins to perceive Allah through the vision granted by faith itself. Only facts possess such magnificence—truths concealed in the depths of belief. Only the heart enriched by remembrance can perceive and comprehend these facts, these truths that vindicate the reality of God.


<!-- section 22 (id=3603, raw_sort=22): ذکر اللہ عبادت کی معراج ہے -->

## Remembrance of Allah as the Ascent of Worship

The Qur'an repeatedly emphasizes the centrality of remembrance—*dhikr* (ذکر)—in the life of the believer. Allah Most High declares:

> ⟪quran 76:25⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ بُكْرَةًۭ وَأَصِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *And remember the Name of your Lord every morning and afternoon.*

and again:

> ⟪quran 73:8⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ وَتَبَتَّلْ إِلَيْهِ تَبْتِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *And remember the Name of your Lord and devote yourself to Him with a complete devotion.*

The believers are commanded with unmistakable urgency:

> ⟪quran 33:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ذِكْرًۭا كَثِيرًۭا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Remember Allah with much remembrance.*

The mode of this remembrance is prescribed with precise spiritual refinement. Allah instructs the faithful to invoke their Lord:

> ⟪quran 7:55⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱدْعُوا۟ رَبَّكُمْ تَضَرُّعًۭا وَخُفْيَةً ۚ إِنَّهُۥ لَا يُحِبُّ ٱلْمُعْتَدِينَ ‎⟫
> *Invoke your Lord with humility and in secret. He likes not the aggressors.*

and further:

> ⟪quran 7:205⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُر رَّبَّكَ فِى نَفْسِكَ تَضَرُّعًۭا وَخِيفَةًۭ وَدُونَ ٱلْجَهْرِ مِنَ ٱلْقَوْلِ بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ وَلَا تَكُن مِّنَ ٱلْغَافِلِينَ ‎⟫
> *And remember your Lord by your tongue and within yourself, humbly and with fear without loudness in words in the mornings, and in the afternoons and be not of those who are neglectful.*

These verses converge upon a single truth: remembrance must arise from the depths of the soul, clothed in humility and reverence, expressed with a subdued tongue, and sustained both morning and evening. Yet beneath the specificity of manner lies a more fundamental principle—that such remembrance must occur *frequently* and *continuously*. The intensity and constancy of remembrance, exemplified in the lives of the Prophet Muhammad (upon whom be blessings and peace) and the Commander of the Faithful, ʿAlī ibn Abī Ṭālib, finds affirmation in the words of Sūrat al-Muzammil:

> ⟪quran 73:20⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ إِنَّ رَبَّكَ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّكَ تَقُومُ أَدْنَىٰ مِن ثُلُثَىِ ٱلَّيْلِ وَنِصْفَهُۥ وَثُلُثَهُۥ وَطَآئِفَةٌۭ مِّنَ ٱلَّذِينَ مَعَكَ ۚ وَٱللَّهُ يُقَدِّرُ ٱلَّيْلَ وَٱلنَّهَارَ ۚ عَلِمَ أَن لَّن تُحْصُوهُ فَتَابَ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ فَٱقْرَءُوا۟ مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ ٱلْقُرْآنِ ۚ عَلِمَ أَن سَيَكُونُ مِنكُم مَّرْضَىٰ ۙ وَآخَرُونَ يَضْرِبُونَ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ يَبْتَغُونَ مِن فَضْلِ ٱللَّهِ ۙ وَآخَرُونَ يُقَتِلُونَ فِى سَبِيلِ ٱللَّهِ ۖ فَٱقْرَءُوا۟ مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنْهُ ۚ وَأَقِيمُوا۟ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ وَآتُوا۟ ٱلزَّكَوٰةَ وَأَقْرِضُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ قَرْضًا حَسَنًۭا ۚ وَمَا تُقَدِّمُوا۟ لِأَنفُسِكُم مِّنْ خَيْرٍۢ تَجِدُوهُ عِندَ ٱللَّهِ هُوَ خَيْرًۭا وَأَعْظَمَ أَجْرًۭا ۚ وَٱسْتَغْفِرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۢ ‎⟫
> *Verily, your Lord knows that you do stand (to pray at night) a little less than two-thirds of the night, or half the night, or a third of the night, and so do a party of those with you, And Allah measures the night and the day. He knows that you are unable to pray the whole night, so He has turned to you (in mercy). So, recite you of the Quran as much as may be easy for you. He knows that there will be some among you sick, others travelling through the land, seeking of Allah's Bounty; yet others fighting in Allah's Cause. So recite as much of the Quran as may be easy (for you), and perform As-Salat (Iqamat-as-Salat) and give Zakat, and lend to Allah a goodly loan, and whatever good you send before you for yourselves, you will certainly find it with Allah, better and greater in reward. And seek Forgiveness of Allah. Verily, Allah is Oft-Forgiving, Most-Merciful.*

The opening of the same sūra enjoins the Prophet to remembrance in the most exalted terms:

> ⟪quran 73:8⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ وَتَبَتَّلْ إِلَيْهِ تَبْتِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *And remember the Name of your Lord and devote yourself to Him with a complete devotion.*

Here, the discourse deepens. The word "Lord" (*rabb*) encompasses both the sustainer and the source of all existence, while "His Name" (*asmāʾuhu*)—the divine attributes and designations—represents the accessible facets of an incomprehensible totality. To devote oneself to His Name is to establish complete severance (*tabaʿtul*) from all else, turning wholly toward Allah Himself through the prism of His revealed attributes. For Allah, transcendent and exalted, exceeds all linguistic forms and conceptual frameworks; yet He becomes accessible to human understanding precisely through these Names—Names not fabricated by human artifice but chosen and revealed by Allah for His own self-disclosure.[^cite-51] Thus, ignorance of these Names constitutes, in truth, a heedlessness toward Allah Himself. The Qur'an illustrates this danger unmistakably:

> ⟪quran 58:19⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱسْتَحْوَذَ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلشَّيْطَنُ فَأَنسَىٰهُمْ ذِكْرَ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ حِزْبُ ٱلشَّيْطَنِ ۚ أَلَآ إِنَّ حِزْبَ ٱلشَّيْطَنِ هُمُ ٱلْخَسِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Shaitan (Satan) has overtaken them. So he has made them forget the remembrance of Allah. They are the party of Shaitan (Satan). Verily, it is the party of Shaitan (Satan) that will be the losers!*

and again:

> ⟪quran 63:9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ لَا تُلْهِكُمْ أَمْوَلُكُمْ وَلَآ أَوْلَدُكُمْ عَن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ وَمَن يَفْعَلْ ذَلِكَ فَأُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْخَسِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Let not your properties or your children divert you from the remembrance of Allah. And whosoever does that, then they are the losers.*

The relationship between devotion and the Names of the Divine is illuminated through a saying of the Commander of the Faithful: ⟪ar-quote:من أحب شئی لھج بذکرہ⟫ "Whosoever loves something mentions it with passion and constancy." The word *lahija*—to be devoted, to repeat, to cleave to[^cite-52]—captures the persistence of the lover's tongue. Thus must the believer mention Allah's Name continually, with heart and tongue joined in unison. The Prophet (upon whom be blessings and peace) gave voice to this in supplication: ⟪ar-quote:لھِجَ بہ لسانِ من ذکرک⟫ "My tongue has devoted itself wholly to Your remembrance," and implored: ⟪ar-quote:عِج الِّساَنِ بِذِکرِکَ لَھِجاً⟫ "Make my tongue eager and persistent in Your remembrance." In yet another prayer, the Messenger described the commemoration of Allah in terms of its salvific power: ⟪ar-quote:یا من اسمہ دواؤٌ و ذکرہ شفاؤٌ⟫ "O Thou whose Name is a remedy and whose remembrance is healing."[^cite-53]

Here we encounter a subtle but crucial distinction. The Name of Allah is not merely a word or label among others; rather, it functions as a cure—a spiritual medicine—for the disease of error and negligence that has taken root in human nature from creation itself. Just as a drug must be ingested and absorbed to heal bodily ailment, so too must the Names of Allah be actively invoked and repeated, not merely contemplated. The Qur'an itself is termed a *dhikr* (remembrance), and the command to "remember the Qur'an often" means to recite it continually with the tongue. In this fashion, the Messenger presented dhikr as a deed, an action integral to spiritual life. ʿAbdullāh ibn Basr reports that a man once approached the Prophet (upon whom be blessings and peace), saying: "O Messenger of Allah, the laws of Islam are many and overwhelming. Grant me a single practice I may hold fast to!" The Prophet replied: "Let your tongue forever be moist with the remembrance of Allah." This counsel encapsulates the entire discipline.

Consider further this verse from Sūrat al-Aḥzāb:

> ⟪quran 33:41-43⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ذِكْرًۭا كَثِيرًۭا ‎ ‏وَسَبِّحُوهُ بُكْرَةًۭ وَأَصِيلًا ‎ ‏هُوَ ٱلَّذِى يُصَلِّى عَلَيْكُمْ وَمَلَٓئِكَتُهُۥ لِيُخْرِجَكُم مِّنَ ٱلظُّلُمَتِ إِلَى ٱلنُّورِۚ وَكَانَ بِٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ رَحِيمًۭا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Remember Allah with much remembrance. And glorify His Praises morning and afternoon. He it is Who sends Salat (His blessings) on you, and His angels too (ask Allah to bless and forgive you), that He may bring you out from darkness (of disbelief and polytheism) into light (of Belief and Islamic Monotheism). And He is Ever Most Merciful to the believers.*

In this passage, the remembrance of believers is coupled with glorification, then yoked to prayer (*ṣalāt*) and the descent of divine mercy—the movement from darkness to illumination. The interconnection of these spiritual realities cannot be overstated. Allah Himself declares:

> ⟪quran 2:152⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَٱذْكُرُونِىٓ أَذْكُرْكُمْ وَٱشْكُرُوا۟ لِى وَلَا تَكْفُرُونِ ‎⟫
> *Therefore remember Me (by praying, glorifying, etc.). I will remember you, and be grateful to Me (for My countless Favours on you) and never be ungrateful to Me.*

Here lies a reciprocal covenant: the servant's remembrance of Allah draws forth Allah's remembrance of that servant. The Commander of the Faithful teaches that whoever mentions Allah revives his own heart and illuminates his inmost substance (*albāb*, the seat of intellect and discernment).[^cite-54] This invocation resonates with Qur'anic passages that address "those possessed of understanding" (*awlī al-albāb*):

> ⟪quran 3:190-191⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ فِى خَلْقِ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱخْتِلَفِ ٱلَّيْلِ وَٱلنَّهَارِ لَآيَتٍۢ لِّأُو۟لِى ٱلْأَلْبَبِ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ يَذْكُرُونَ ٱللَّهَ قِيَمًۭا وَقُعُودًۭا وَعَلَىٰ جُنُوبِهِمْ وَيَتَفَكَّرُونَ فِى خَلْقِ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ رَبَّنَا مَا خَلَقْتَ هَذَا بَطِلًۭا سُبْحَنَكَ فَقِنَا عَذَابَ ٱلنَّارِ ‎⟫
> *Verily! In the creation of the heavens and the earth, and in the alternation of night and day, there are indeed signs for men of understanding. Those who remember Allah (always, and in prayers) standing, sitting, and lying down on their sides, and think deeply about the creation of the heavens and the earth, (saying): "Our Lord! You have not created (all) this without purpose, glory to You! (Exalted be You above all that they associate with You as partners). Give us salvation from the torment of the Fire.*

The verse discloses plainly the inseparable bond between remembrance and contemplation (*tafakkur*). When the act of dhikr quickens the heart, it awakens consciousness and sharpens the capacity to witness the signs—the *āyāt*—of Allah displayed in creation and in the human soul. Let love mingle with this contemplation, as the Prophet taught: "Whosoever loves something mentions it with passion." Then there unfolds a living circle of faith, each element nourishing the others. Deep meditation upon the Names of Allah opens the eye to their beauty; beauty begets love; love impels the tongue to mention the Names; constant mention unlocks the secrets veiled within Allah's verses. Contemplation thus quickens remembrance, and remembrance deepens contemplation—a perpetual spiral of spiritual ascent.

## The Primacy and Universality of Dhikr

Dhikr stands as the summit of all acts of worship. While other devotions—standing, bowing, prostration—are circumscribed by specific postures, times, and places, remembrance transcends such boundaries. It requires no particular location, no special hour, no prescribed gesture. Dhikr may arise at any moment, in any setting, while walking or eating, in solitude or company; it is not an isolated practice but rather a quality to be woven into the fabric of daily existence. The Imam Jaʿfar al-Ṣādiq (upon whom be peace) taught: "Every action has a limit which, once attained, ceases; except the remembrance of Allah—for it knows no ceiling, no terminus."[^cite-55] Allah has indeed ordained certain religious duties; the one who fulfills them reaches their measure and their end. The faster, completing thirty days, has satisfied the fast; yet the rememberer of Allah is never finished, never satiated. As the Prophet's grandson, Muḥammad al-Bāqir (upon whom be peace), exemplified—he would eat while engaged in dhikr, would walk while remembering, binding the sacred into every moment.

This principle illuminates a remarkable Qur'anic passage concerning those whom neither commerce nor commerce distracts from the remembrance of Allah:

> ⟪quran 70:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَلَىٰ صَلَاتِهِمْ دَآئِمُونَ ‎⟫
> *Those who remain constant in their Salat (prayers);*

Here, a profound identification occurs: those in a state of unbroken ritual prayer are, in substance, those in ceaseless remembrance of Allah. The Qur'an itself binds prayer and remembrance as a single reality:

> ⟪quran 20:14⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّنِىٓ أَنَا ٱللَّهُ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّآ أَنَا۠ فَٱعْبُدْنِى وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ لِذِكْرِىٓ ‎⟫
> *"Verily! I am Allah! La ilaha illa Ana (none has the right to be worshipped but I), so worship Me, and perform As-Salat (Iqamat-as-Salat) for My Remembrance.*

The imperative is clear: establish prayer *for* My remembrance—the external ritual gains its soul, its meaning, through the inner dhikr that animates it. The Commander of the Faithful declares that unceasing remembrance of Allah is the sustenance of the soul and the key to prayer itself (*miftāḥ al-ṣalāt*). Yet this relationship becomes fully transparent only when we attend to a final verse of extraordinary significance:

> ⟪quran 29:45⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱتْلُ مَآ أُوحِىَ إِلَيْكَ مِنَ ٱلْكِتَبِ وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ تَنْهَىٰ عَنِ ٱلْفَحْشَآءِ وَٱلْمُنكَرِ ۗ وَلَذِكْرُ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ يَعْلَمُ مَا تَصْنَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *Recite (O Muhammad PBUH) what has been revealed to you of the Book (the Quran), and perform As-Salat (Iqamat-as-Salat). Verily, As-Salat (the prayer) prevents from Al-Fahsha' (i.e. great sins of every kind, unlawful sexual intercourse, etc.) and Al-Munkar (i.e. disbelief, polytheism, and every kind of evil wicked deed, etc.) and the remembering (praising, etc.) of (you by) Allah (in front of the angels) is greater indeed. And Allah knows what you do.*

Prayer is characterized here as a guardianship, a protective threshold—formal, circumscribed, bound to prescribed hours and movements. Yet simultaneously, Allah proclaims: *al-dhikr allāh akbar*—"the remembrance of Allah is greater." Greater in what sense? As the soul exceeds the body in rank and reality. The soul does not negate embodied existence; rather, it sustains it, vivifies it, renders it meaningful. So too does dhikr not supersede prayer; rather, dhikr is the spiritual essence within which prayer achieves its true purpose. When remembrance is absent, prayer becomes mere gesture; when dhikr quickens the heart, prayer becomes a living communion with the Divine. In this lies the pinnacle of worship: that the servant remember Allah not merely in prescribed moments, but in the very marrow of existence itself.


<!-- section 23 (id=3604, raw_sort=23): ذکر اللہ کی حقیقت -->

## The Reality of the Remembrance of Allah

We now turn to examine the fruit of the remembrance of Allah and its principal aim: realization—that transformative process by which divine truth becomes a living reality within human consciousness. ⟪ar:تَوَحٌُد⟫ This realization resembles a profound self-integration (tawhīd, divine unification), wherein the soul becomes unified with its own essential nature, fundamentally distinct from ordinary monotheism, which connotes merely intellectual acknowledgment of divine unity. We approach an understanding of this fruit by contemplating its contrary—heedlessness, forgetfulness, distraction—for truth is often clarified through the examination of its negation.

Allah condemns most severely the prayer of those who dissemble, those who pray whilst neglecting the heart's presence, as the divine word declares:

> ⟪quran 107:4-6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْمُصَلِّينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَآءُونَ ‎⟫
> *So woe unto those performers of Salat (prayers) (hypocrites), Who delay their Salat (prayer) from their stated fixed times, Those who do good deeds only to be seen (of men),*
> — **Quran 107:4-6**

Similarly, Maulana Ali forbade all invocation of Allah tainted by negligence and ostentation. Yet he revealed a paradox: when negligence is purged from remembrance, a perfect invocation emerges—one in which the individual becomes utterly oblivious to himself. Thus did Maulana Ali unite two seemingly contradictory principles: that heedlessness must be absent from *dhikr* (remembrance), and that such focused attention must deepen until the rememberer forgets his own existence and experiences *al-fanāʾ fi-l-dhikr* (annihilation in remembrance).[^cite-56] He proclaimed:

> Do not invoke Allah carelessly, nor forget Him in your heedlessness. Rather, remember Him with perfect presence—a remembrance wherein heart and tongue are one, and the concealed intention aligns with the outward word. Yet know that you shall never remember Him truly until you become heedless of your own soul in this remembrance!

This teaching embodies the innermost secret of Sufism. Every authentic spiritual path converges upon two realities: *sidq* (sincerity) and *ikhlās* (purity of intention). On one hand, *dhikr* vivifies the heart, engendering that transparency of intention from which true sincerity flows; on the other, sincerity itself becomes the virtue that perfects and sustains the remembrance. In this perfected state, the utterance of the tongue achieves absolute harmony with the intention of the heart—not the slightest divergence between word and inner reality. This unity between tongue and heart signifies that divine truth, released upon the tongue, becomes the echo of the heart's glorification: the heart, which is the mirror of spiritual reality (*rūḥāniyyah*) and the locus wherein all moral and spiritual virtues are born.[^cite-57]

When the soul becomes wholly purified and transparent, unified with the intellect's utterances and the tongue's articulation, it becomes a vessel for the spiritual realities embedded within human nature—realities that shine forth in the heart through the remembrance of Allah, then manifest themselves in outward conduct. These virtues—*al-akhlāq al-rūḥāniyyah wa-l-akhlāqiyyah*—are what illuminate authentic *dhikr*. Without them, the external performance of remembrance remains bereft of life and meaning. The ignorant are those who neglect the striving for sincerity and turn away from the *al-jihād al-akbar* (the Greater Struggle), that inward combat through which the soul's commands are fulfilled.

Maulana Ali's words open before us a gateway to the true reality of *dhikr*, through which we advance toward divine truth. To attain this loftiest station, the *fanāʾ al-nafs* (annihilation of the self)—complete self-effacement—becomes requisite. To perceive unity with the Absolute, one must remove the veil of selfhood that stands between truth and the consciousness. Knowledge begins with self-denial and culminates in the annihilation of the self. Thus does the reality of *dhikr* demand a revolutionary forgetting. Herein we discern that humanity ascends from perfection toward a higher reality: from human excellence (*kamāl insānī*) toward divine truth (*al-Haqq*). 

The first stage comprises the elimination of hypocrisy and the cultivation of sincerity, integrity, and wholeness—virtues that produce human perfection while the individual's identity remains intact. This harmony of intention and action constitutes what we call *perfection* (kamāl). Yet this remembrance occurs through the human being himself and therefore occupies a lower rank. In true realization, the self's identity does not survive, for the rememberer has become oblivious to himself. Here the focus shifts entirely away from the *dhākir* (the one who remembers) toward the *madhkūr* (the One remembered). The reality of *dhikr* becomes one with the divine truth itself. At such a moment, it may be said inwardly that it is Allah Himself who remembers through the tongue of humanity—appearing outwardly as human utterance. At this station, human existence becomes as a deception erased by the remembrance itself.[^cite-58]

In this light, we return to the sacred *hadīth qudsī*: "My servant ceases not to draw near to Me through voluntary acts (*nawāfil*) until I love him." Now we comprehend that by *nawāfil* is meant the remembrance of Allah. Observe carefully: Allah Himself is the root of every act of the rememberer. Allah witnesses and hears the deeds of those whom He loves. Yet Allah does not alter His own nature to enter into human intention and action. Rather, He becomes one with that intention and action. In other words, divine realities become unveiling to the rememberer whose self has been obliterated, enabling him to perceive beyond the suspicion of outward existence and to comprehend the inner meanings (*bāṭin*) of the Qur'an's verses. As the Book declares:

> ⟪quran 37:96⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *"While Allah has created you and what you make!"*
> — **Quran 37:96**

And again:

> ⟪quran 8:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَلَمْ تَقْتُلُوهُمْ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهَ قَتَلَهُمْ ۚ وَمَا رَمَيْتَ إِذْ رَمَيْتَ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهُ رَمَىٰ ۚ وَلِيُبْلِىَ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْهُ بَلَآءً حَسَنًا ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *You killed them not, but Allah killed them. And you (Muhammad PBUH) threw not when you did throw but Allah threw, that He might test the believers by a fair trial from Him. Verily, Allah is All-Hearer, All-Knower.*
> — **Quran 8:17**

This truth was exemplified by the Prophet (peace be upon him) and Maulana Ali. In battle, an arrow pierced Ali's ankle as he prostrated in prayer. He instructed those nearby: "Remove this arrow only when I enter the state of prostration during my prayer." They obeyed. When he emerged from prayer, he asked: "Has it been extracted?" It was then revealed that he had felt nothing. Such is the apex of remembrance—the physical existence of humanity, all sensation bound to the body, vanishes entirely.

As the Messenger of Allah declared: "Virtue (*ihsān*) is to worship Allah as though you see Him, and if you do not see Him, verily He sees you." The depth of this *hadīth* becomes apparent when we attend carefully to its phrasing: the vision of Allah cannot be attained so long as any creature remains within the field of perception (*nadhar*). In the account of Moses:

> ⟪quran 7:143⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَمَّا جَآءَ مُوسَىٰ لِمِيقَتِنَا وَكَلَّمَهُۥ رَبُّهُۥ قَالَ رَبِّ أَرِنِىٓ أَنظُرْ إِلَيْكَ ۚ قَالَ لَن تَرَىٰنِى وَلَكِنِ ٱنظُرْ إِلَى ٱلْجَبَلِ فَإِنِ ٱسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُۥ فَسَوْفَ تَرَىٰنِى ۚ فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّىٰ رَبُّهُۥ لِلْجَبَلِ جَعَلَهُۥ دَكًّۭا وَخَرَّ مُوسَىٰ صَعِقًۭا ۚ فَلَمَّآ أَفَاقَ قَالَ سُبْحَنَكَ تُبْتُ إِلَيْكَ وَأَنَا۠ أَوَّلُ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ ‎⟫
> *And when Musa (Moses) came at the time and place appointed by Us, and his Lord spoke to him, he said: "O my Lord! Show me (Yourself), that I may look upon You." Allah said: "You cannot see Me, but look upon the mountain if it stands still in its place then you shall see Me." So when his Lord appeared to the mountain, He made it collapse to dust, and Musa (Moses) fell down unconscious. Then when he recovered his senses he said: "Glory be to You, I turn to You in repentance and I am the first of the believers."*
> — **Quran 7:143**

The brilliance of divine reality (*al-Haqq*) overwhelmed Moses into unconsciousness. Allah did not manifest upon Moses but upon the mountain—a manifestation that human fragility could not endure.

On one occasion, a companion of the Prophet—Abū al-Dardāʾ—saw Maulana Ali lying motionless in a garden of Medina, his body seemingly lifeless. Concerned, Abū al-Dardāʾ hastened to the house of Fāṭimah (the Prophet's daughter) to inform her. She replied: "My husband Ali has not passed away; rather, he has become overwhelmed by *khawf* (awe and reverence for God's magnificence). This state visits him often." Here, *khawf* denotes not mere fear but profound recognition of divine greatness. The Qur'an speaks of this perfection of reverence:

> ⟪quran 79:40-41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِۦ وَنَهَى ٱلنَّفْسَ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰ ‎ ⟫
> *But as for him who feared standing before his Lord, and restrained himself from impure evil desires, and lusts.*
> — **Quran 79:40-41**

Though all earthly fear inspires flight, this divine reverential awe draws the soul toward its Beloved. In Sufi understanding, when a creature fears a creature, it flees; when it fears Allah, it hastens toward Him. The Qur'an confirms this:

> ⟪quran 9:118⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَعَلَى ٱلثَّلَثَةِ ٱلَّذِينَ خُلِّفُوا۟ حَتَّىٰٓ إِذَا ضَاقَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلْأَرْضُ بِمَا رَحُبَتْ وَضَاقَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَظَنُّوٓا۟ أَن لَّا مَلْجَأَ مِنَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَّآ إِلَيْهِ ثُمَّ تَابَ عَلَيْهِمْ لِيَتُوبُوٓا۟ ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ هُوَ ٱلتَّوَّابُ ٱلرَّحِيمُ ‎⟫
> *And (He did forgive also) the three [who did not join the Tabuk expedition] left (i.e. he did not give his judgement in their case, and their case was suspended for Allah's Decision) till for them the earth, vast as it is, was straitened and their own selves were straitened to them, and they perceived that there is no fleeing from Allah, and no refuge but with Him.*
> — **Quran 9:118**

Maulana Ali's state exemplified his spiritual love and the union of his consciousness with divine reality. Thus did Maulana Fāṭimah recognize these episodes as signs of his advanced station.

Surely, among the divine attributes is a *sharāb* (spiritual wine) reserved for the saints (*awliyāʾ*). When they drink thereof, they become intoxicated with divine nearness; in their intoxication, they find delight; in their delight, they are blessed; in blessing, they experience *fanāʾ* (dissolution); through dissolution, they attain freedom; through freedom, purity. When they seek divine truth, they find; when they find, they arrive; when they arrive, they become unified with Him in such manner that no distinction separates them from their Beloved.[^cite-59]

The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) declared: "There come upon them moments of divine knowledge so profound that neither angel nor prophet can bear them." This state of supreme monotheism is the fruit of all devotion—the most intoxicating of all intoxications. The rememberer journeys toward this wine. In the beginning, it appears that the servant drinks the wine of remembering Allah's names, and the servant remembers Allah. Yet in the furthest reaches of realization, Allah Himself drinks the wine of the servant's name and begins to remember it. This occurs when a soul has utterly annihilated itself in the remembrance of Allah. Maulana Ali taught: "The remembrance of Allah is not mere speech, nor is it mere thought." Rather, the *madhkūr* (the One remembered) is first, and the *dhākir* (the rememberer) is second—that is, *awwalan min al-madhkūr wa-thānīan min al-dhākir* (Allah is the First in remembrance, and humanity's remembrance is but a reflection).[^cite-60]

Allah is the primary rememberer; humanity's remembrance is the reflection and consequence of divine remembrance. The Qur'an states: "Remember Me, and I shall remember you." Indeed, if we penetrate deeply into the reality of *dhikr*, we discern that the divine command *kun* (Be!)—the word through which all creation sprang into existence—itself constitutes a remembrance. Allah spoke the name of possibility and called it forth, manifesting existence from absolute nothingness. Allah remembered creation, and creation became His remembrance. The Qur'an poses:

> ⟪quran 76:1⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هَلْ أَتَىٰ عَلَى ٱلْإِنسَنِ حِينٌۭ مِّنَ ٱلدَّهْرِ لَمْ يَكُن شَيْـًۭٔا مَّذْكُورًا ‎⟫
> *Has there not been over man a period of time, when he was nothing to be mentioned?*
> — **Quran 76:1**

Here humanity is named as something Allah brought into being through creative remembrance. Its prior non-mention indicates an era when Allah had not yet commanded it from non-being into existence. At that primordial moment, humanity was known only to Allah. Thus the remembrance of Allah precedes human existence itself; God's invocation of humanity surpasses humanity's invocation of God. While humanity remembers Allah through His names, Allah remembers humanity through the word *kun*. Yet this utterance was not momentary and fleeting—it continues to resonate within the human soul until the Day of Judgment, testifying to divine sovereignty. Through this eternal word, Allah breathed into human existence the breath of being itself.

When Ḥazrat Kāmil inquired of Amīr al-Muʾminīn: "What is reality (*al-ḥaqīqah*)?" he answered: "Reality is the name of unveiling Allah's glory, untainted by any veils of creatures." In the light of unveiling, the name of the annihilation of the feared self becomes *al-ḥaqīqah*. The name of complete union with the attribute of monotheism is *al-ḥaqīqah*—a light emanating from the horizon of eternity, whose rays illuminate the sanctuary of divine unity. By "sanctuary," he refers to the human heart as the place wherein Allah manifests His names, which give life and sustenance to the soul. The soul is the locus of divine manifestation (*taʾallī*), the place where Allah reveals Himself in a particular manner.

Ibn al-ʿArabī writes in his *Futūḥāt al-Makkiyyah*: "All praise belongs to Him who created things from naught and negated them, bringing them into existence through the attention of His words. As the Divine Word attends to possible objects, the attributes of creation come into being. The spirit of potentiality is breathed into existence, which is connected to the body. The heart within that body is the name of Allah that bestows life upon it." Every servant bears a name derived from his Lord, so that the servant becomes the body and the Lord becomes the heart. This teaching echoes Maulana Ali's declaration: "Remembrance burns in hearts." The divine name descending from on high reflects upon the name resonating within the heart. This reflection occurs when the rust of the heart is cleared away by the burning of divine remembrance—the union of an outer light with an inner light, exemplifying the Qur'anic verse of light: *nūr ʿalā nūr* (light upon light).

The question then arises: what distinguishes the divine names, which are the source of all creation, from those names specifically mentioned in the Qur'an? On one hand, all creation is the Book of Allah (*Kitāb Allah*), and all manifestations are the words of this book. Yet on the other hand, certain names have been revealed in the Qur'an for us to glorify. Why this distinction? The Qur'an itself provides an answer:

> ⟪quran 17:110⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلِ ٱدْعُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ أَوِ ٱدْعُوا۟ ٱلرَّحْمَنَ ۖ أَيًّۭا مَّا تَدْعُوا۟ فَلَهُ ٱلْأَسْمَآءُ ٱلْحُسْنَىٰ ۚ وَلَا تَجْهَرْ بِصَلَاتِكَ وَلَا تُخَافِتْ بِهَا وَٱبْتَغِ بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ سَبِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *Say (O Muhammad PBUH): "Invoke Allah or invoke the Most Beneficent (Allah), by whatever name you invoke Him (it is the same), for to Him belong the Best Names.*
> — **Quran 17:110**

Allah instructs believers to invoke only those names revealed in the Qur'an—names utterly distinct from the names of idols:

> ⟪quran 53:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنْ هِىَ إِلَّآ أَسْمَآءٌۭ سَمَّيْتُمُوهَآ أَنتُمْ وَآبَآؤُكُم مَّآ أَنزَلَ ٱللَّهُ بِهَا مِن سُلْطَنٍ ۚ إِن يَتَّبِعُونَ إِلَّا ٱلظَّنَّ وَمَا تَهْوَى ٱلْأَنفُسُ ۖ وَلَقَدْ جَآءَهُم مِّن رَّبِّهِمُ ٱلْهُدَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *They are but names which you have named, you and your fathers, for which Allah has sent down no authority. They follow but a guess and that which they themselves desire.*
> — **Quran 53:23**

The names of idols resemble worldly appearances that are self-explanatory, signs having no connection with reality. But Allah's names maintain an intrinsic relationship with His essence; they constitute the very reality of creation. Thus these names possess not merely informative power but transformative power—the capacity to unveil divine greatness and reality within the human heart and intellect. For this reason, Allah's existence is inescapable: no existence lies outside the scope of His being. Yet rust upon the heart obscures this divine presence, even though the heart itself is Allah's creation.

Therefore, one must purify the heart from within through divine remembrance, so that the inner and outer realities become unveiled. The divine names (*al-asmāʾ al-ilāhiyyah*) represent the pinnacle of manifestations—they encompass all appearances while transcending them. This inner and outer substance resembles the relationship between light and shadow: both manifest from a single essence, yet remain distinct. As Ibn al-ʿArabī taught, the existence of Truth is a fixed light, and all creation is its shadow.

Maulana Ali proclaimed in his supplication: "I invoke You by all the names You have chosen for Yourself." The fact that Allah Himself designated these names testifies to their might and efficacy. He declared further: "You shall never invoke Him until you forget yourselves in His remembrance." What, then, is meant by this forgetting of self and obliviousness to it? It is impossible for a conscious being to be entirely oblivious to his existence during remembrance. Yet if one strives to forget himself, his very striving prevents that forgetting. Thus this self-forgetfulness signifies a complete concentration of attention upon Allah's names—such that no space remains within soul, psyche, intellect, or being where divine remembrance does not dwell, leaving no place where the ego can establish itself. This capacity to dissolve (*fanāʾ*) is bestowed by Allah's grace when a person labors to remove the rust obscuring the heart—that rust which deprives one of the vision of Allah's unity, which has no equal. The Qur'an records Allah's address to His Prophet:

> ⟪quran 87:6-7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏سَنُقْرِئُكَ فَلَا تَنسَىٰٓ ‎ ⟫
> *We shall make you to recite (the Quran), so you (O Muhammad (Peace be upon him)) shall not forget (it).*
> — **Quran 87:6-7**

And:

> ⟪quran 18:24⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُر رَّبَّكَ إِذَا نَسِيتَ ‎⟫
> *And remember your Lord when you forget.*
> — **Quran 18:24**

When a person forgets all that is not Allah, he becomes capable of remembering Allah alone. If Allah dwells in the palace of affirmation, humanity dwells in the palace of negation. When this negation (the creature) is itself negated, complete affirmation of Allah results—as the multiplication of negatives yields a positive.

The Creator declares: "I am the death of death!" Rūmī captured Maulana Ali's teachings thus: "I have drawn the sword for Allah's sake; I am Allah's servant, not bound to my body's commands. I am the Lion of Allah, not the lion of desire! My deeds witness my faith. In battle, I am Allah's sword, wielded by His hand. I have cast the burden of my soul from my path. I have forgotten all except Allah. Allah is my sun, and I am His reflection. I am a knowing one! I am the veil between Allah and His creation. I am filled with pearls of divine unity as a sword adorned with gems. I do not slay in battle—I grant eternal life in the Hereafter!"

Allah's movement toward His servant becomes possible only through the negation of the servant's existence. This negation is the nothingness from which Allah created existence. He brought humanity forth from non-being; now humanity must annihilate itself to find Allah. Humanity negates the substance that never truly existed (for human existence is borrowed, contingent), and through this negation acknowledges what eternally abides. As the Qur'an states:

> ⟪quran 55:26-27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎ ⟫
> *Whatsoever is on it (the earth) will perish.*
> — **Quran 55:26-27**

Every creature possesses two aspects: the divine dimension, which constitutes its true reality, and the mortal dimension, which is perishable. The Face of Allah—the immortal divine reality—is not merely one divine dimension but the very reality subsisting within all things. Allah says:

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ ⟫
> *Everything will perish save His Face.*
> — **Quran 28:88**

Al-Ghazālī writes that objects do not perish only upon reaching a particular moment or place; they exist in a state of continual perdition, for nothing except Allah possesses intrinsic perfection. Every creature subsists through the Face of Allah—through divine sustenance—manifested as existence. Its being derives not from itself but from the Face of Allah; therefore, the Face of Allah is reality, and all else is illusion.

The Sufi master then writes: "Nothing remains in them except the remembrance of Allah; they no longer possess the power to remember themselves." When a person reaches this station, he dwells simultaneously in *fanāʾ* (annihilation) and *baqāʾ* (subsistence). Yet even the sense of annihilation vanishes, because the soul becomes heedless of itself and negligent of its own dissolution. Should one retain awareness of one's own annihilation, one remains aware of oneself.

Al-Qushayrī writes: "Whoever has not tasted the loneliness of *fanāʾ* shall not be nourished by the remembrance of Allah." This loneliness refers to the soul's intimacy with itself, manifesting as self-praise, desire, and egocentrism. This intimacy cannot be removed save through divine remembrance. Herein lies the reality of *dhikr*: that the Lord encapsulates in a single sentence: *forget yourself in the remembrance of Allah*. The Qur'an declares:

> ⟪quran 2:198⟫
> ⟪ar:‏لَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَن تَبْتَغُوا۟ فَضْلًۭا مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ ۚ فَإِذَآ أَفَضْتُم مِّنْ عَرَفَتٍۢ فَٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ عِندَ ٱلْمَشْعَرِ ٱلْحَرَامِ ۖ وَٱذْكُرُوهُ كَمَا هَدَىٰكُمْ ‎⟫
> *Then when you leave 'Arafat, remember Allah (by glorifying His Praises, i.e. prayers and invocations, etc.) at the Mash'ar-il-Haram. And remember Him (by invoking Allah for all good, etc.) as He has guided you.*
> — **Quran 2:198**

Here, guidance denotes elevation in the station of remembrance. The first is *dhikr al-lisān* (remembrance of the tongue), bound to the self. Then comes *dhikr al-qalb* (remembrance of the heart), bound to worship and releasing divine grace. Thereafter is *dhikr al-sirr* (remembrance of the secret), pertaining to the sight of worship from which divine truths are unveiled. Then *dhikr al-rūḥ* (remembrance of the spirit), wherein the spirit contemplates the divine essence in the light emanating from that sight. Finally, *dhikr al-khafī* (the hidden remembrance), pertaining to the beauty of the divine source, and *dhikr al-aṣl* (the remembrance of the origin), the true vision transcending duality.

Maulana Ali declared:

> Do not abandon remembrance because you do not sense Allah's presence within it, for it is better that you not perceive Him in your remembrance than that you forget Him. He shall lead you from negligence to the Prophet, and thence to a remembrance wherein all vanishes save the One remembered. Verily, for Allah this is not difficult.

Ibn al-ʿAjībah writes in his *Ḥikam* that the more one is annihilated in Allah's name, the more one errs in knowledge of the origin. He states: "The name of Allah is the joy of my heart and the coolness of my eyes." True happiness flows ever from the essence of a thing, not from its name alone. Imam Jaʿfar al-Ṣādiq (peace be upon him) taught:[^cite-61]

The name of Allah is separate from His essence; everything upon which His name appears is a creation, and thus separate from Allah. Everything that is described is created, and the Creator cannot be encompassed within the limits of His creation's names. There are ninety-nine names of God. Were name and essence identical, each name would constitute a separate god. But Allah is He to whom the names point, and they are distinct from Him and from creation.

Each name points to a quality whilst identifying that quality; yet each name also possesses its own distinct identity. Thus *al-Raḥīm* (the Merciful), *al-Karīm* (the Generous), and *al-Sattār* (the Veiler) identify Allah, yet each name has an identity separate from the others. The separation of these names indicates their limitation. Though each is real in itself, before Allah they become as imagined realities—their station before Him becomes *ḥaqīqah al-khayāl* (imagined reality). The true reality of all names returns to the Self—Allah alone. From one perspective, name and essence differ; from another, they are one. In one sense, the name is merely a divine attribute of the essence; in another, it is a name expressed through words. Thus *al-Raḥīm* derives from mercy (*raḥmah*), and *al-Karīm* from generosity (*karam*). In this understanding, name and essence become identical.

The attributes dissolve into the essence because they become one with it, having no independent existence. This is the reality of monotheism (*tawhīd*). After this knowledge, the testimony of faith no longer stands, for all gods have merged into Allah's essence and vanished. Its meaning becomes clear: there is no reality save the true reality—the Self. From this station, only *Allāh* remains, for He is the One without equal, and none can know Him save Allah alone.

The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) exemplified perfect humanity. Maulana Ali proclaimed: "We are the Most Beautiful Names of Allah"—*huwa al-ʿalāmah al-ʿuẓmā wa-āyātuhu al-kubrā* (He is the Greatest Sign and His Mighty Verses). The Messenger declared: "Whoever sees me has seen the Truth." Thus the Messenger, Ali, and the Imams are those who manifested divine attributes within human physicality. They are mirrors wherein divine qualities reflect. The brighter divine truth shines upon them, the brighter the reflection in these perfected beings.

In the first sermon of *Nahj al-Balāghah*, Maulana Ali says: "The perfection of sincerity is to purify it from all attributes, for every attribute testifies to its own reality." Thus whoever describes an attribute of Allah assigns it as an attribute belonging to Allah; whoever imagines it a partner has introduced duality; whoever introduces duality has divided the divine; whoever divides has become ignorant. Maulana Ali's teaching here—that purifying Allah from His attributes constitutes monotheism—does not deny these attributes' reality. Rather, it denies the notion that attributes exist autonomously, externally affixed to the Truth, or subsisting apart from Him. Allah is He whose attributes know no limitation. What is being denied is that human imagination and language can capture the reality of any divine attribute. If attributes are not separate from the essence, and if Allah's essence is eternal and unlimited, then the attributes too are infinite. When the essence cannot be comprehended, neither can the attributes.

One must simultaneously affirm and negate: affirm that attributes are inseparable from the essence; negate that they can be incorporated into human thought and conception. This paradox expresses the relationship between the human soul and divine truth. Humanity is desolate, bereft of independent existence, yet never separated from truth—becoming oblivious to itself in worship. When humanity ceases to exist, Allah's existence alone remains. Though great contradiction appears here, the profound reality is that the sense of divine truth's perfect existence connects with the sense of the self's non-existence.

The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "On the Night of Ascension, I learned the true meaning of the divine names and saw them return to their object and entity. What I perceived was the names, and my own existence was my own. My ascension was within me, pointing to me, and through it I came to know that I am a pure servant with not the slightest trace of divinity."

Similarly, when Maulana Ali describes his greatness in his sermons, he describes the greatness of Allah revealed through him. They are the embodiment of divine greatness—and divine greatness is the highest expression of self-denial. Someone once said to Imam Jaʿfar al-Ṣādiq: "You are arrogant!" He replied: "Arrogance is the province of Allah alone. I have wholly cleansed the field of my self from pride, replacing it with the grandeur of Allah. So long as selfish arrogance exists, divine greatness cannot manifest in that place; yet when divine greatness is present through the eradication of ego, divine attributes shine upon the mirror of self—a mirror rendered transparent by divine realities—more brilliantly and swiftly. This radiance was kindled when I purged the dust of ego and desire (*al-hawā*) from the mirror of my heart."

Now let us return to the *hadīth qudsī*: "My servant approaches Me through obligatory duties, beloved to Me above all, until he ceases not to draw near through voluntary acts until I love him. When I love him, I become his hearing by which he hears, his sight by which he sees, his hand by which he grasps, and his feet by which he walks."

Consider the apparent contradiction herein: obligatory duties are most beloved to Allah; yet voluntary remembrance draws the servant into such closeness that Allah loves him with a love that permeates his senses and faculties, mirroring divine unity. This paradox dissolves when we understand that when Allah loves obligatory acts, He loves something seemingly separate from His essence. Yet when Allah loves a servant who has become oblivious of himself through remembrance, that servant becomes manifold because he has become the manifestation of Allah, unified with Him. At such a moment, Allah's love of the servant becomes Allah's love of Himself. God desired to know Himself, thus He created this cosmos. When humanity denies itself in remembrance and knowledge of Allah, the divine command *to know Myself* is fulfilled.

Maulana Ali proclaimed: "Knowledge rains from me, yet no bird can soar to me!" Knowledge rains from you because you have become one with the source of knowledge itself. The Qur'an states:

> ⟪quran 76:5-6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ ٱلْأَبْرَارَ يَشْرَبُونَ مِن كَأْسٍۢ كَانَ مِزَاجُهَا كَافُورًا ‎ ⟫
> *Verily, the Abrar (pious, who fear Allah and avoid evil), shall drink a cup (of wine) mixed with water from a spring in Paradise called Kafur.*
> — **Quran 76:5-6**

This wine of camphor signifies Allah's essence itself. The righteous increase this fountain because the wine is camphor itself—without duality, without separation. Divine remembrance not only removes the heart's rust and vivifies it but dissolves the very name and trace of duality through the grace of the One remembered. It purifies the heart from all *shirk* (association of partners with Allah) and establishes the principle of monotheism. To comprehend this reality requires the negation of all apparent secondary causes.

On one hand, humanity comes to know Allah through the impossibility of knowing Him, for He transcends the veil of creation. On the other, in remembrance, when humanity becomes oblivious of itself, the distinction between Creator and creature vanishes. At that moment, the person's soul unites with nothing else; rather, that state becomes a state of dissolution. Its existence vanishes, and only consciousness remains—a consciousness belonging to nothing, attached to no entity. Then the person reaches the station of *ʿārif billāh* (one who knows through Allah); otherwise, he remains in the station of knowing about Allah. As Maulana Ali taught: "Know Allah through Allah!" The aim of remembrance is not merely to make one forget all except Allah but to understand that nothing exists save Allah. Ali (peace be upon him) declared: "When the heart is illumined by divine remembrance, the condition of seeing replaces blindness, and hearing replaces deafness. Wherever he looks, he perceives the Face of Allah."

> ⟪quran 2:115⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْمَشْرِقُ وَٱلْمَغْرِبُ ۚ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا۟ فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ ‎⟫
> *And to Allah belong the east and the west, so wherever you turn yourselves or your faces there is the Face of Allah.*
> — **Quran 2:115**

And:

> ⟪quran 24:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ مَن فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱلطَّيْرُ صَٓفَّتٍۢ ۖ كُلٌّۭ قَدْ عَلِمَ صَلَاتَهُۥ وَتَسْبِيحَهُۥ ۚ ‎⟫
> *See you not (O Muhammad PBUH) that Allah, He it is Whom glorify whosoever is in the heavens and the earth, and the birds with wings out-spread (in their flight).*
> — **Quran 24:41**

In his sermons, Amīr al-Muʾminīn declares: "I am the Sign of Allah Almighty! I know the secrets of God! I am the boundary of all boundaries! I am the companion of the rays of Allah's divine glory! I am the First, the Last, the Outward, the Inward! I am the Face of Allah! I am the mirror of Allah, His pen and His tablet! I am he whom the Gospels call al-ʿAliyāh! I am he who possesses the mysteries of the Messenger of Allah!"[^cite-62]

Though these words suggest *shirk* to the external observer, those of inner understanding comprehend their true meaning. Only when we understand the first declaration—"I am the Sign of Allah Almighty"—does all else become clear. In this sermon, Maulana Ali identifies himself with the knowledge Allah has of Himself, not with human knowledge of Allah. The knowledge Allah possesses of His own self differs profoundly from that which humanity possesses. Knowledge, knower, and known become one when they reach this supreme knowledge, just as knowledge and existence become unified upon reaching the apex of consciousness. At this station, the knower becomes self-aware; knowledge is the consciousness that truth possesses of itself. Consciousness accesses this knowledge when it annihilates every particle of its existence in Allah. One must forget oneself to remember God. To become the knowledge of Allah, everything must become what Allah Himself is. At that moment, humanity becomes a ray of divine greatness. All *al-sirr* (secrets) are hidden within the Ultimate Secret—the essence of Allah, which encompasses all divine names. Thus you declare: "I am the First, the Last, the Outward, the Inward."

When you call yourself the Face of Allah, this teaching may be understood through the comparison to a mirror. When one looks in a mirror, the mirror ceases to exist; all attention focuses on the reflected face. The viewer scarcely realizes the mirror's existence—the mirror loses its identity. Conversely, when attention fixes on the mirror, one cannot perceive the reflection. Thus the mirror becomes identified with the form one perceives. At that moment, mirror and form become one, though they remain two distinct objects simultaneously. So long as attention remains on the mirror, it becomes a veil obscuring the face; but once the gaze turns to the face, the veil rises and perfect obedience emerges. The mirror's effacement before the face corresponds to humanity's annihilation before divinity, while the image in the mirror corresponds to the remembrance of Allah.

Again, we encounter paradox: these *walīs* of Allah—those who understand themselves as the opposite of annihilation and dissolution before divine majesty—are precisely those who correctly interpret Allah's names and attributes. The attributes belonging to God are not theirs; yet these saints and the *ṣūfiyyah* represent the beautiful names of Allah. The light of these qualities shines through them because they have burned the mirror of their heart with divine remembrance, erasing all stains of egoism. Physicality cannot prevent them from reflecting this radiance. These are beings whose hearts dwell in heaven whilst their bodies labor on earth. Even whilst living in this world, their lives have perished, as Allah has declared:

> ⟪quran 29:64⟫
